I say: but the speech of al-Nahr in what passed is explicit that it is from the long, and it is apparent from the speech of al-Hidayah as well as per his explanation in its wording where he responded to his brother. His statement: (And he did not mention the number of verses recited in each prayer etc.) He did not clarify whether the mentioned number is sunnah or mustahabb. It preceded from al-Nahr that recitation from al-Mufassal is sunnah and the specific amount is another sunnah, but in al-Siraj from al-Muhit is what indicates that the mentioned amount is mustahabb. For he mentioned that recitation in prayer has five types: fard, wajib, sunnah, mustahabb, makruh. Fard: one verse; wajib: al-Fatiha and a surah; sunnah: the long of al-Mufassal in Fajr and Zuhr, its medium in Asr and Isha, its short in Maghrib; mustahabb: that he recites in Fajr when a resident in the first rak'ah the amount of thirty or forty verses besides al-Fatiha, and in the second the amount of twenty to thirty besides al-Fatiha; and makruh: that he recites al-Fatiha alone or al-Fatiha with one or two verses. His statement: (And it was said: one considers etc.) i.e., he recites in winter and summer forty, and in autumn and spring fifty to sixty. Thus in al-Fath. His statement: (contrary to) the first statement etc. He said in al-Nahr: I say: it is possible that by the lazy is meant Fajr only, and nothing of the Qur'an is specified for a prayer, and the follower does not recite but listens and is silent, even if it is short, five or six verses besides al-Fatiha, and the author of al-Bada'i' attributed it to al-Asl. It is mentioned in al-Hawi that the limit of prolongation in Maghrib in each rak'ah is five verses or a short surah, and the limit of medium and shortening is a surah from the short of al-Mufassal. And he chose in al-Bada'i' that there is no fixed estimation in recitation, but it varies according to the time and the condition of the imam and the people, and the summary is that it is appropriate for the imam to recite an amount that is light for the people and not burdensome, while being complete. And similarly in al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, which did not specify the number of verses to recite in each prayer. The author, Ibn Nujaym, compiles various Hanafi positions from authoritative sources. He begins by noting the differences among the mashayikh and reports. The core ruling is that in Fajr, the recitation besides Fatiha should be between forty and sixty verses minimum, with flexibility for longer or shorter based on the time and the congregation. For Zuhr, the majority follow the same number as Fajr, though some say it should be medium. For Asr and Isha, twenty verses in the first two rak'ahs is the apparent narration. For Maghrib, a short surah is recommended. The passage also clarifies that these numbers are mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. The imam should consider the congregation's capacity and avoid hardship. The conclusion is that in Fajr, the absolute minimum is forty verses in both rak'ahs combined.

Key Terms
طوال المفصل (tiwal al-mufassal): The long surahs of the Mufassal section (the last seventh of the Quran, from Surah Qaf to the end), such as al-Hujurat and Qaf.
أوساط المفصل (awsat al-mufassal): The medium-length surahs of the Mufassal, such as al-Tariq and al-Buruj.
قصار المفصل (qisar al-mufassal): The short surahs of the Mufassal, from al-Zalzalah to an-Nas.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 60
D) 100

Key Takeaway
The relied-upon Hanafi position is that Fajr recitation should not go below 40 verses (excluding Fatiha), and this is a mustahabb recommendation, not an obligation.

Recitation in Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, and Isha: Hanafi Standards
Compilation of Hanafi rulings on the quantum of Qur'an recitation in each obligatory prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the recommended number of verses for each obligatory prayer (excluding Fajr) according to the Hanafi school, including variations in Zuhr.

Core Idea
Zuhr matches Fajr in length; Asr and Isha require twenty verses; Maghrib a short surah—each tailored to time and congregation.

While Fajr has a clear minimum, the other prayers have specific recommendations that reflect the time of day and typical occupations. This lesson covers the number of verses and type of surahs for Zuhr, Asr, Isha, and Maghrib, noting the intra-Hanafi variation on Zuhr.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer and its recommended number
Zuhr: like Fajr (40-60 verses) according to majority, or like Asr (20) according to al-Quduri. Asr and Isha: 20 verses in first two rak'ahs (zahir al-riwayah). Maghrib: a short surah (qisar al-mufassal).
These are for the first two rak'ahs only; for the last two, only Fatiha.
2
Understand the ikhtilaf on Zuhr
The author notes that some say Zuhr is like Fajr (long surahs, many verses), others say like Asr (medium surahs, 20 verses). The majority favor the longer recitation.
The mufta bihi is the longer recitation, but the imam may consider the congregation.
3
Recognize the type of surahs
For Zuhr and Fajr: long surahs (tiwal al-mufassal). For Asr and Isha: medium (awsat). For Maghrib: short (qisar).
These categories are based on the Mufassal section of the Quran.
4
Apply the principle of flexibility
The imam should consider the congregation's capacity and the season. The numbers may be adjusted but not below the recommended minima.
The text from al-Bada'i' says there is no fixed estimation; it varies.

ويتعلموا .اهـ. ولم يذكر المصنف عدد الآيات التي تقرأ في كل صلاة لاختلاف الآثار والمشايخ، والمنقول في الجامع الصغير أنه يقرأ في الفجر في الركعتين سوى الفاتحة أربعين أو خمسين أو ستين آية واقتصر في الأصل على الأربعين وروى الحسن في المجرد ما بين ستين إلى مائة، ووردت الأخبار بذلك كله عنه الله ثم قالوا : يعمل بالروايات كلها بقدر الإمكان واختلفوا في كيفية العمل به فقيل ما في المجرد من المائة محمل الراغبين، وما في الأصل محمل الكسالى أو الضعفاء وما في الجامع الصغير من الستين محمل الأوساط، وقيل ينظر إلى طول الليالي وقصرها وإلى كثرة الأشغال وقلتها قال في فتح القدير : الأولى أن يجعل هذا محمل اختلاف فعله عليه الصلاة والسلام بخلاف القول الأول فإنه لا يجوز فعله عليه لأنهم لم يكونوا كسالى فيجعل قاعدة لفعل الأئمة في زماننا ويعلم منه أنه لا ينقص في الحضر عن الأربعين وإن كانوا كسالى لأن الكسالى محملها .اهـ. فالحاصل أنه لا ينقص عن الأربعين في الركعتين في الفجر على كل حال على جميع الأقوال وقال فخر الإسلام قال مشايخنا : إذا كانت الآيات قصاراً فمن الستين إلى مائة وإذا كانت أوساط فخمسين، وإذا كانت طوالاً فأربعين، وجعل المصنف الظهر كالفجر والأكثرون على أنه يقرأ في الظهر بالطوال. وذكر في منية المصلي معزياً إلى القدوري أن الظهر كالعصر يقرأ فيه بالأوساط، وأما في عدد الآيات ففي الجامع الصغير أن الظهر كالفجر في العدد لاستوائهما في سعة الوقت. وقال في الأصل: أو دونه لأنه وقت الاشتغال فينقص عنه تحرزاً عن الملال، وعينه في الحاوي بأنه دون أربعين إلى ستين. وأما عدد الآي في العصر والعشاء فعشرون آية في الركعتين الأوليين منهما كما في المحيط وغيره أو خمسة عشر آية فيهما كما في الخلاصة، وذكر قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير أنه ظاهر الرواية. وأما قدر ما في المغرب ففي التحفة والبدائع سورة أيضاً. أقول لكن كلام النهر فيما مر صريح في أنها من الطوال وهو ظاهر كلام الهداية أيضاً على ما قرره في عبارتها حيث رد على أخيه . قوله : (ولم يذكر المصنف عدد الآيات التي تقرأ في كل صلاة الخ) لم يبين أن العدد المذكور هل هو سنة أو مستحب، وتقدم عن النهر أن القراءة من المفصل سنة ومقدار الخاص سنة أخرى، لكن في السراج عن المحيط ما يدل على أن المقدار المذكور مستحب فإنه ذكر أن القراءة في الصلاة على خمسة أوجه : فرض وواجب وسنة ومستحب مكروه. فالفرض آية، والواجب الفاتحة وسورة والمسنون طوال المفصل في الفجر والظهر وأوساطه في العصر والعشاء وقصاره في المغرب، والمستحب أن يقرأ في الفجر إذا كان مقيماً في الركعة الأولى قدر ثلاثين آية أو أربعين سوى الفاتحة، وفي الثانية قدر عشرين إلى ثلاثين سوى الفاتحة والمكروه أن يقرأ الفاتحة وحدها أو الفاتحة ومعها آية أو آيتان . قوله : (وقيل ينظر الخ أي يقرأ في الشتاء وفي الصيف أربعين وفي الخريف والربيع خمسين إلى ستين. كذا في الفتح. قوله : بخلاف) القول الأول الخ) قال في النهر أقول: يجوز أن يراد بالكسالى الفجر فقط ولم يتعين شيء من القرآن لصلاة ولا يقرأ المؤتم بل يستمع وينصت وإن قصيرة خمس آيات أو ست آيات سوى الفاتحة وعزاه صاحب البدائع إلى الأصل، وذكر في الحاوي أن حد التطويل في المغرب في كل ركعة خمس آيات أو سورة قصيرة، وحد الوسط والاختصار سورة من قصار المفصل، واختار في البدائع أنه ليس في القراءة تقدير معين بل يختلف باختلاف الوقت وحال الإمام والقوم والجملة فيه أنه ينبغي للإمام أن يقرأ مقدار ما يخف على القوم ولا يثقل عليهم بعد أن يكون على التمام وهكذا في الخلاصة .
and they learn. He did not mention the number of verses to be recited in each prayer due to differences in reports and shaykhs. It is transmitted in al-Jami' al-Saghir that in Fajr, in the two rak'ahs besides al-Fatiha, forty or fifty or sixty verses are recited. In al-Asl he restricted to forty. Al-Hasan narrated in al-Mujarrad between sixty and one hundred. Reports came about all that from him. Then they said: one acts on all the reports as much as possible. They differed on how to act accordingly. It was said: the one hundred in al-Mujarrad is for those who desire much, the one in al-Asl is for the lazy or weak, and the sixty in al-Jami' al-Saghir is for the middle. It was said: one considers the length and shortness of nights and the abundance and scarcity of occupations. He said in Fath al-Qadir: the first is to make this the explanation of the variation in his action, contrary to the first statement, for it is not permissible that he acted on it because they were not lazy. So it is made a basis for the action of imams in our time, and it is understood from it that he does not decrease in the settled area from forty even if they are lazy, because the lazy is their explanation. The conclusion: it is not less than forty in the two rak'ahs of Fajr in every case according to all statements. Fakhr al-Islam said: our shaykhs said: if the verses are short, then from sixty to one hundred; if medium, fifty; if long, forty. The author made Zuhr like Fajr, and the majority that he recites in Zuhr with the long. It is mentioned in Munyat al-Musalli, attributed to al-Quduri, that Zuhr is like Asr, reciting with the medium. As for the number of verses, in al-Jami' al-Saghir that Zuhr is like Fajr in number because they are equal in spaciousness of time. He said in al-Asl: or less than it because it is a time of occupation, so it is decreased to avoid boredom, and he specified in al-Hawi that it is less than forty to sixty. As for the number of verses in Asr and Isha: twenty verses in the first two rak'ahs of them as in al-Muhit and others, or fifteen verses in them as in al-Khulasa. Qadikhan mentioned in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir that it is the apparent narration. As for the amount in Maghrib, in al-Tuhfa and al-Bada'i' a surah also. I say: but the speech of al-Nahr in what passed is explicit that it is from the long, and it is apparent from the speech of al-Hidayah as well as per his explanation in its wording where he responded to his brother. His statement: (And he did not mention the number of verses recited in each prayer etc.) He did not clarify whether the mentioned number is sunnah or mustahabb. It preceded from al-Nahr that recitation from al-Mufassal is sunnah and the specific amount is another sunnah, but in al-Siraj from al-Muhit is what indicates that the mentioned amount is mustahabb. For he mentioned that recitation in prayer has five types: fard, wajib, sunnah, mustahabb, makruh. Fard: one verse; wajib: al-Fatiha and a surah; sunnah: the long of al-Mufassal in Fajr and Zuhr, its medium in Asr and Isha, its short in Maghrib; mustahabb: that he recites in Fajr when a resident in the first rak'ah the amount of thirty or forty verses besides al-Fatiha, and in the second the amount of twenty to thirty besides al-Fatiha; and makruh: that he recites al-Fatiha alone or al-Fatiha with one or two verses. His statement: (And it was said: one considers etc.) i.e., he recites in winter and summer forty, and in autumn and spring fifty to sixty. Thus in al-Fath. His statement: (contrary to) the first statement etc. He said in al-Nahr: I say: it is possible that by the lazy is meant Fajr only, and nothing of the Qur'an is specified for a prayer, and the follower does not recite but listens and is silent, even if it is short, five or six verses besides al-Fatiha, and the author of al-Bada'i' attributed it to al-Asl. It is mentioned in al-Hawi that the limit of prolongation in Maghrib in each rak'ah is five verses or a short surah, and the limit of medium and shortening is a surah from the short of al-Mufassal. And he chose in al-Bada'i' that there is no fixed estimation in recitation, but it varies according to the time and the condition of the imam and the people, and the summary is that it is appropriate for the imam to recite an amount that is light for the people and not burdensome, while being complete. And similarly in al-Khulasa.
Source pages p. 595

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, which did not specify the number of verses to recite in each prayer. The author, Ibn Nujaym, compiles various Hanafi positions from authoritative sources. He begins by noting the differences among the mashayikh and reports. The core ruling is that in Fajr, the recitation besides Fatiha should be between forty and sixty verses minimum, with flexibility for longer or shorter based on the time and the congregation. For Zuhr, the majority follow the same number as Fajr, though some say it should be medium. For Asr and Isha, twenty verses in the first two rak'ahs is the apparent narration. For Maghrib, a short surah is recommended. The passage also clarifies that these numbers are mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. The imam should consider the congregation's capacity and avoid hardship. The conclusion is that in Fajr, the absolute minimum is forty verses in both rak'ahs combined.

Key Terms
طوال المفصل (tiwal al-mufassal): The long surahs of the Mufassal section.
أوساط المفصل (awsat al-mufassal): Medium surahs of the Mufassal.
قصار المفصل (qisar al-mufassal): Short surahs of the Mufassal.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), how many verses should be recited in the first two rak'ahs of Asr prayer?
A) 10
B) 20
C) 15
D) 40

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school recommends 20 verses for Asr and Isha, a short surah for Maghrib, and Zuhr similar to Fajr (long surahs), with flexibility based on circumstances.

Module 8 · Lesson 363

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
10 min
The Legal Status of Recitation Quantity: Mustahabb vs Fard/Wajib
Compilation of Hanafi rulings on the quantum of Qur'an recitation in each obligatory prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between the obligatory (fard/wajib) and recommended (sunnah/mustahabb) elements of Quran recitation in prayer according to the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
The quantity of recitation beyond Fatiha and a surah is mustahabb; the obligatory minimum is much simpler.

A common misunderstanding is that the specified verse counts are mandatory. This lesson clarifies the Hanafi classification of recitation into five categories: fard, wajib, sunnah, mustahabb, and makruh. The specific numbers for each prayer fall under sunnah or mustahabb, not fard or wajib.

Guided Path
1
List the five categories of recitation in prayer
From al-Muhit: fard (one verse), wajib (Fatiha + surah), sunnah (specific surah types), mustahabb (specific numbers), makruh (Fatiha alone or with one-two verses).
These categories are explained in the text from al-Siraj.
2
Identify which category each quantity belongs to
The type of surah (long, medium, short) is sunnah. The specific number of verses (40, 20, etc.) is mustahabb according to the dominant view.
Some scholars call the numbers 'sunnah' but the text edges towards mustahabb.
3
Understand the consequence of omission
Leaving fard invalidates prayer; leaving wajib requires sajdah al-sahw; leaving sunnah or mustahabb is not sinful but reduces reward.
The text does not explicitly state consequences but principles of fiqh apply.
4
Apply to a practical scenario
If an imam recites only Fatiha and a short surah (5 verses) in Fajr, the prayer is valid but the mustahabb quantity is missed; it is makruh to recite only Fatiha or one-two verses.
The text says it is makruh to recite only Fatiha or Fatiha with one-two verses.

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is an expansion on the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq, which did not specify the number of verses to recite in each prayer. The author, Ibn Nujaym, compiles various Hanafi positions from authoritative sources. He begins by noting the differences among the mashayikh and reports. The core ruling is that in Fajr, the recitation besides Fatiha should be between forty and sixty verses minimum, with flexibility for longer or shorter based on the time and the congregation. For Zuhr, the majority follow the same number as Fajr, though some say it should be medium. For Asr and Isha, twenty verses in the first two rak'ahs is the apparent narration. For Maghrib, a short surah is recommended. The passage also clarifies that these numbers are mustahabb (recommended), not obligatory. The imam should consider the congregation's capacity and avoid hardship. The conclusion is that in Fajr, the absolute minimum is forty verses in both rak'ahs combined.

Key Terms
فرض (fard): One verse: the absolute minimum recitation necessary for the prayer to be valid.
واجب (wajib): Fatiha and a surah (or equivalent) in the first two rak'ahs; omission requires sajdah al-sahw.
سنة (sunnah): Reciting the appropriate category of surah from al-Mufassal for each prayer.
مستحب (mustahabb): Reciting the specific number of verses (e.g., 40 in Fajr); recommended but not emphasized.
مكروه (makruh): Reciting only Fatiha or Fatiha with one or two verses; disliked but not haram.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi classification from al-Muhit, what is the ruling of reciting only al-Fatiha and no other verses in prayer?
A) Fard
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah
D) Makruh

Key Takeaway
The quantity of recitation beyond Fatiha and a surah is mustahabb; the prayer is valid even if the recommended numbers are not met, as long as the fard (one verse) and wajib (Fatiha + surah) are fulfilled.

Sunnah of Lengthening the First Rak'ah of Fajr Only
Hanafi ruling on sunnah of lengthening first rak'ah in Fajr, with intra-madhhab dispute.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on lengthening the first rak'ah in Fajr, explain the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and apply the tarjih to determine the mufta bihi.

Core Idea
Lengthening the first rak'ah is sunnah mu'akkadah for Fajr only, per the majority, despite a minority Hanafi view extending it.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies that the recommendation to lengthen the first rak'ah is unique to Fajr, based on an explicit hadith. The author also discusses an intra-Hanafi disagreement: Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani extends it to Zuhr and Asr using a different hadith. The majority and the mufta bihi position restrict it to Fajr. We will trace the evidence and see how the school reconciles conflicting hadiths.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is lengthening the first rak'ah of Fajr by reciting more verses. Its ruling is sunnah mu'akkadah (confirmed sunnah), not wajib.
The text states 'متفق عليه' (agreed upon) for its sunniyyah.
2
Understand the scope from the matn
The word 'فقط' (only) in the matn indicates that this sunnah is exclusive to Fajr according to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
This is the majority position within the Hanafi school.
3
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that lengthening the first rak'ah is also sunnah in Zuhr and Asr. This is a valid ikhtilaf among the three senior imams.
The text says 'خلافاً لمحمد' (contrary to Muhammad).
4
Examine the proofs for each side
The majority cite the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri showing equal recitation in Zuhr and Asr. Imam Muhammad cites the hadith of Abu Qatada showing lengthening in Zuhr and Asr as well.
Both hadiths are from authentic sources.
5
Analyze the tarjih and reconciliation
The Hanafi response reconciles the two hadiths by interpreting Abu Qatada's report as referring to lengthening from non-recitation elements (du'a, etc.). The explicit text of Abu Sa'id takes precedence. The mufta bihi is the majority view.
Al-Ramli confirms people act on the choice of al-Bada'i' which follows the majority.

His statement: (And you lengthen the first of Fajr only) is an explanation of the sunnah. This—meaning lengthening the first rak'ah of Fajr—is agreed upon, transmitted from the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to this day as in al-Nihaya, and because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness, so the imam helps the congregation by lengthening it hoping that they will catch it, because there is no shortcoming from them due to sleep. He did not specify in al-Mukhtasar the limit of lengthening, but al-Kafi specified it: the difference should be by a third and two-thirds, so in the first two-thirds and in the second one-third. He said: This is an explanation of istihbab (recommendation). As for the ruling, even if the difference is excessive, there is no harm because of the reported tradition. He chose in al-Khulasa the amount of half, for he said: the limit of lengthening in Fajr is that he recites in the second rak'ah twenty to thirty verses, and in the first thirty to sixty verses. In his statement 'only' there is an indication that lengthening is not sunnah in other than Fajr. This is their statement (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), contrary to Muhammad, because of the hadith of al-Bukhari from Abu Qatada that he (peace be upon him) used to lengthen the rak'ah of Zuhr and shorten the second, and likewise in Asr and likewise in Fajr. The madhhab is argued with the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that he (peace be upon him) used to recite in Zuhr prayer in the first two rak'ahs in each rak'ah about thirty verses, and in Asr in the first two rak'ahs in each rak'ah fifteen verses. For it is an explicit text for equality in recitation, contrary to the hadith of Abu Qatada, for it is possible that the lengthening in it arises from the totality of praise, seeking refuge, the Basmala, and recitation of less than three, so it is interpreted accordingly to reconcile the two conflicting hadiths as much as possible. The researcher in Fath al-Qadir discussed that the interpretation does not work for his statement 'and likewise Fajr', and that it is better that it is obligatory for the weak, and it is not denied that he (peace be upon him) had weak companions sometimes, so it is possible that he took care of their situation when they prayed with him. His statement: (and he chose in al-Bada'i' etc.) al-Ramli said: People today act on what he chose in al-Bada'i'. His statement: (explanation) (of the sunnah. I say: Rather, al-Halabi narrated in Sharh al-Munya consensus on its being sunnah. His statement: (and he chose in al-Khulasa the amount of half) Some virtuous person objected to it, the gist being that the statement of al-Khulasa does not imply that, and there is no difference between it and the statement of al-Kafi, for if he recited in the first sixty and in the second thirty, the difference would be by a third and two-thirds, and if we assume that he declared in al-Khulasa the amount of half, that does not contradict it either, because what is in the second is half of what is in the first, so it is not a different statement opposed to what is in
Source pages p. 596

Commentary
This passage explains the Hanafi ruling on lengthening the first rak'ah of Fajr. The author comments on the matn phrase 'and you lengthen the first of Fajr only.' He states that this is a sunnah, agreed upon by the early Muslims. The reason is that Fajr is a time when people may be drowsy, so the imam lengthens the first rak'ah to allow latecomers to join. The amount of lengthening is specified as a ratio: in the first rak'ah, recite two-thirds of the total, and in the second one-third (from al-Kafi). Alternatively, al-Khulasa suggests reciting 30-60 verses in the first and 20-30 in the second, which amounts to approximately half. The phrase 'only' indicates that this sunnah applies exclusively to Fajr, which is the position of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf. Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani disagrees, citing a hadith from Abu Qatada that the Prophet lengthened the first rak'ah in Zuhr and Asr as well. The Hanafi response is that the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri shows equality in recitation for Zuhr and Asr, so the lengthening in Abu Qatada's report might be due to other parts of the prayer (du'a, etc.). The discussion also clarifies that this lengthening is sunnah (mustahabb), not wajib, as there is consensus on its sunnah status. Later Hanafi scholars like al-Ramli confirm that the operative ruling is based on al-Bada'i', which gives flexibility to the imam based on the congregation.

Key Terms
تطويل (tatwil): Lengthening the first rak'ah of Fajr by reciting more verses than in the second.
الركعة الأولى (al-rak'ah al-ula): The first unit of prayer; in Fajr, it is recommended to be longer than the second.
سنة (sunnah): A recommended practice of the Prophet; not obligatory but meritorious.

Key Terms from Source Passage

According to the Hanafi school (majority view), in which prayer is it sunnah to lengthen the first rak'ah?
A) Fajr only
B) Fajr and Zuhr
C) All five prayers
D) Only Maghrib

Key Takeaway
The sunnah of lengthening the first rak'ah in Fajr is a confirmed practice, exclusive to Fajr per the majority Hanafi view, and is not wajib.

Prolonging the First Rak'ah in Fajr: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on scope of prolonging first rak'ah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi positions on prolonging the first rak'ah in Fajr and evaluate the evidence used by Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Muhammad al-Shaybani.

Core Idea
Prolonging the first rak'ah in Fajr is sunnah; the ikhtilaf is whether it applies only to Fajr.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, the author addresses a well-known intra-Hanafi dispute: is the sunnah of prolonging the first rak'ah over the second specific to the Fajr prayer, or does it extend to all prayers? While the majority of the madhhab holds it is only for Fajr, Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani maintained it applies generally. We will trace the arguments and see how the Hanafi scholars reconciled the conflicting hadith evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the agreed sunnah
Note that all Hanafi imams agree that prolonging the first rak'ah over the second is a sunnah, especially in Fajr. The author mentions this is transmitted continuously from the Prophet (peace be upon him).
The sunnah status is not disputed; only its scope is.
2
State the point of ikhtilaf
The disagreement: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that this sunnah applies only to Fajr, while Muhammad al-Shaybani holds it applies to all prayers (Zuhr, Asr, etc.).
3
Examine the hadith evidence for each view
Muhammad relies on the hadith of Abu Qatadah where the Prophet lengthened the first rak'ah in Zuhr, Asr, and Fajr. Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf rely on the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri showing equal recitation in Zuhr and Asr.
Both hadith are from Bukhari and are authentic (zanni al-thubut).
4
Analyze the Hanafi reconciliation
The majority interprets Abu Qatadah's hadith as referring to prolongation due to supplications (thana', ta'awwudh, basmalah) not necessarily recitation length, thus reconciling with the explicit equality in Abu Sa'id's hadith.
In Fajr, the prolongation is specifically for recitation due to the time of sleep.
5
Determine the mufta bihi and practice
The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf, so imams should only prolong the first rak'ah in Fajr, not in other prayers.
Later scholars like al-Ramli confirm this is what people act upon.

His saying: (And you prolong the first of Fajr only) is an explanation of the sunnah. And this - meaning the prolongation of the first rak'ah of Fajr - is agreed upon by transmission from the time of the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) to our day, as in al-Nihayah, and because it is a time of sleep and heedlessness, so the imam helps the congregation by prolonging it hoping that they will catch it, for there is no negligence from them due to sleep. And al-Mukhtasar did not specify the limit of prolongation, but al-Kafi specified it: that the difference should be by a third, two-thirds, two-thirds in the first and a third in the second. He said: This is a statement of desirability. As for the statement of the ruling, even if the difference is excessive, there is no harm due to the transmission of the athar. And al-Khulasah chose half, for he said: The limit of prolongation in Fajr is that he reads in the second rak'ah from twenty to thirty verses, and in the first from thirty to sixty verses. And in his saying 'only' there is indication that prolongation is not sunnah in other than Fajr, and that is their view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) contrary to Muhammad, due to the hadith of al-Bukhari from Abu Qatadah that he (peace be upon him) used to lengthen the rak'ah of Zuhr and shorten the second, and similarly in 'Asr, and similarly in Subh. And the madhhab argues with the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri that he (peace be upon him) used to recite in Zuhr in the first two rak'ahs each rak'ah about thirty verses, and in 'Asr in the first two each rak'ah about fifteen verses. For it is an explicit text on equality in recitation, unlike the hadith of Abu Qatadah, for it is possible that the prolongation therein arose from the totality of praise, seeking refuge, the basmalah, and reciting less than three, so it is interpreted accordingly to reconcile the contradictory as much as possible. His saying: (and he chose in al-Bada'i etc.) al-Ramli said: The people today act upon what he chose in al-Bada'i. His saying: (statement of the sunnah) and as for what al-Bahansi mentioned in Sharh al-Multaqa is strange, hence his student al-Baqani said in his Sharh: In al-Kafi and other books of the madhhab, prolonging the first over the second is sunnah, and I have not seen in the famous books of the madhhab anyone who said it is obligatory, so refer. I say: Rather al-Halabi in Sharh al-Munyah transmitted consensus on its being sunnah. His saying: (and he chose in al-Khulasah half) was objected to by some scholars, the gist being that the wording of al-Khulasah does not indicate that, and that there is no difference between it and the wording of al-Kafi, for if he reads sixty in the first and thirty in the second, the difference is by a third and two-thirds, and if we assume that he stated in al-Khulasah half, that does not contradict it either, because what is in the second is half of what is in the first, so it is not another view different from what is in al-Kafi, as is suggested by his contrasting it with it, so ponder.

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling of prolonging the first rak'ah over the second in the Fajr prayer. The author begins by stating that prolonging the first rak'ah of Fajr is a sunnah, as transmitted continuously from the Prophet (peace be upon him) and because it helps the congregation catch the prayer. The limit of prolongation is defined in al-Kafi as two-thirds in the first and one-third in the second, while al-Khulasah specifies half (e.g., 30-60 verses in first, 20-30 in second). The core dispute: Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf hold that this prolongation is only for Fajr, based on the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri showing equal recitation in Zuhr and 'Asr. Muhammad al-Shaybani holds that it applies to all prayers, based on the hadith of Abu Qatadah. The Hanafi response interprets Abu Qatadah's hadith as referring to prolongation due to other factors (supplications, etc.) and not necessarily to recitation length. The author also notes that some later scholars like al-Ramli follow the view of al-Bada'i (practical consideration). The passage concludes that the sunnah status is consensual, not obligatory.

Key Terms
إطالة (italah): Prolonging the recitation or other aspects of the first rak'ah over the second.
تطويل (tatwil): Same as italah, prolongation.
مسنونة (masnunah): Recommended, sunnah, not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Maghrib only

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is that prolonging the first rak'ah is sunnah only in Fajr, based on the hadith of Abu Sa'id al-Khudri, and Muhammad's view is marjuh.

Prolongation in Other Prayers and Exception for Jumu'ah/Eid
Discussion on prolongation in other prayers and exception for Jumu'ah/Eid

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prolonging the second rak'ah over the first in prayers other than Fajr, and explain why Jumu'ah and Eid are exceptions based on the Prophet's practice.

Core Idea
Prolonging the second rak'ah over the first is makruh tanzih, but the Prophet's practice in Jumu'ah and Eid removes that dislike.

In the previous lesson, we learned that prolonging the first rak'ah over the second in Fajr is recommended (sunnah). But what about other prayers? This passage addresses whether prolongation (making one rak'ah longer than the other) is disliked in prayers like Zuhr, Asr, Maghrib, Isha, and how Jumu'ah and Eid are special exceptions. We will also see an intra-Hanafi dispute between Imam Muhammad and the two shaykhs (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf), and how the later fatwa resolves it.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi position on prolongation in non-Fajr prayers
Identify the ruling: In prayers other than Fajr, making the second rak'ah longer than the first is makruh tanzih (disliked) if done without a valid reason. This is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi).
The dislike is only when the difference is at least three verses, and not for a good intention like helping latecomers.
2
Identify the intra-Hanafi dispute
Note that Imam Muhammad held that prolongation is allowed in all prayers (including non-Fajr), citing a hadith about similarity. However, Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf restrict the recommendation to Fajr only. Their evidence is stronger, so the fatwa is on their view.
Al-Ramli and al-Halabi support Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.
3
Examine the Prophet's practice in Jumu'ah and Eid as a dalil
The Prophet (peace be upon him) recited Surah al-A'la (19 verses) in the first rak'ah of Jumu'ah and Surah al-Ghashiyah (26 verses) in the second – a clear prolongation of the second over the first. This is established in the two Sahihs.
This seems to contradict the general dislike, so we need to resolve it.
4
Analyze how the Prophet's practice creates an exception
The passage explains that the dislike applies to what is not established by the Sunnah. The Prophet's action removes the dislike because his practice is the Sunnah. Alternatively, the dislike is only tanzih (light dislike), and his action elevates it to permissible or recommended. Thus, Jumu'ah and Eid are exceptions.
Also, the three-verse threshold is for short surahs; in long surahs, a greater difference may be insignificant.
5
Conclude the mufta bihi ruling
The final ruling: In non-Fajr prayers, prolonging the second rak'ah over the first is makruh tanzih unless there is a valid reason (e.g., to help latecomers). In Jumu'ah and Eid, equality is preferred, but if the imam follows the Prophet's recitation, it is not disliked.
This is the position of the majority of later Hanafi scholars.

From al-Dirayah: interpreting as similarity in the essence of prolongation, not in its amount, so it is not the obvious meaning. Hence he said in al-Khulasah regarding the view of Muhammad that it is 'more beloved' etc. And his student al-Halabi criticized him, saying that their view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf) regarding the sunnah of prolonging the first over the second in Fajr in terms of amount does not depend on this hadith, for they can prove it with another evidence, so their view is more beloved, not his. Since the strength of their evidence is apparent, the fatwa is on their view. Thus what is in al-Mi'raj that the fatwa is on Muhammad's view is weak. In al-Muhit, citing al-Fatawa: If the imam lengthens the recitation in the first rak'ah so that the people can catch it, there is no harm if the prolongation does not burden the congregation. So it indicates that prolongation in other prayers, if intended for good, is not makruh; otherwise there is harm (makruh tanzih). And the absolute statements imply that Jumu'ah and the two Eids are also subject to the dispute, as in Jami' al-Mahbubi. In Nazm al-Zandustiti: The two rak'ahs are equal in recitation in Jumu'ah and the two Eids by consensus. And it is restricted to the first (rak'ah), because prolonging the second over the first is makruh by consensus. The disliked difference is by three verses; if one or two verses, it is not disliked, because he recited in Maghrib al-Mu'awwidhatayn, and one of them is longer than the other by one verse. Thus in al-Kafi. And this ruling is problematic due to what is established in the two Sahihs: his recitation in Jumu'ah and the two Eids: in the first Surah al-A'la (Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la) and in the second Surah al-Ghashiyah (Hal ataka hadith al-ghashiyah), even though the second is longer than the first by more than three verses: the first has nineteen verses, the second twenty-six. It may be answered that this dislike applies to what is not established by the Sunnah; as for what is reported from him (peace be upon him) in some prayers, it is not disliked, or the dislike is tanzih, and his action removes the dislike. His saying: (And this ruling is problematic etc.) al-Khayr al-Ramli said: I say: In Sharh Munyat al-Musalli by al-Halabi, and in al-Qunyah: If he recites in the first of 'Asr (Surah al-'Asr) and in the second (Surah al-Humazah), it is disliked, because the first has three verses and the second nine, and the great increase is disliked. As for what is reported that he recited in the first of Jumu'ah Surah al-A'la and in the second Surah al-Ghashiyah, the second exceeds the first by seven, but seven in long surahs is insignificant unlike short surahs, because six here is double the original, and seven there is less than half of it. So it is known that the mentioned prolongation is only disliked if it is excessively long, without regard to the number of verses. End of his words in the commentary. And I say: His statement 'because six here' i.e., in al-Humazah, is double the original i.e., al-'Asr; and his statement 'and seven there' i.e., in Hal ataka, is less than half of it, i.e., the original which is Sabbih. And Allah knows best. End of al-Ramli's words. I say: In the expression of Shaykh Ibrahim al-Halabi in his large commentary, there is an addition that should be mentioned, for he said after the words of al-Qunyah: And it is known from this that the three verses are only disliked in short surahs because the length becomes apparent by that amount clearly.
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on prolongation, now focusing on other prayers and the exception of Jumu'ah and Eid. It begins by affirming that the fatwa is on the view of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (only Fajr), and that Muhammad's view is weak. It then cites al-Muhit that prolongation in other prayers is not makruh if the imam intends good and does not burden the congregation; otherwise it is makruh tanzih. The passage then addresses a specific issue: prolonging the second rak'ah over the first (e.g., in Maghrib) is disliked by consensus, and the disliked difference is generally three verses, but exceptions exist when the Prophet himself did so (e.g., in Jumu'ah reciting Surah al-A'la and al-Ghashiyah, where the second is longer). The commentator resolves this by noting that such prolongation is only disliked when it is excessive and not in line with the Sunnah; the Prophet's practice removes the dislike. The discussion also includes a nuance: the three-verse threshold applies to short surahs where a small difference is noticeable; in long surahs, a larger difference may be insignificant. The passage concludes with a reference to the commentary of al-Halabi and al-Ramli, emphasizing that the ruling depends on the overall extent of prolongation, not merely the number of verses.

Key Terms
كراهة التنزيه (karahah al-tanzih): Dislike that is not prohibited; it is better to avoid but not sinful.
التفاوت بثلاث آيات (al-tafawut bi-thalath ayat): A difference of three verses between the recitation of the two rak'ahs, which is the threshold for dislike.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is makruh because the second is longer
B) It is permissible and not makruh because the Prophet did so
C) It is haram
D) It is wajib

Key Takeaway
Prolonging the second rak'ah over the first is makruh tanzih in non-Fajr prayers, but Jumu'ah and Eid are exceptions based on the Prophet's practice.

The Hanafi Dispute on Lengthening the First Rak'ah (Tatwil)
Intra-Hanafi dispute on the scope of sunnah tatwil

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the positions of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on lengthening the first rak'ah and explain why the fatwa follows the Sahibayn.

Core Idea
The fatwa restricts sunnah tatwil to Fajr only.

This lesson explores an important intra-Hanafi dispute: whether it is recommended to lengthen the first rak'ah over the second in all prayers or only in Fajr. The text from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq presents the arguments and the tarjih that settles the operative ruling.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ikhtilaf
What is the point of disagreement? Abu Hanifa held that lengthening the first rak'ah is sunnah in all prayers, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad restrict it to Fajr.
This is an intra-Hanafi disagreement, not between madhhabs.
2
Locate the dalil for each side
Abu Hanifa's proof is a hadith showing general prophetic practice of lengthening. The Sahibayn have an independent proof (not explicitly cited here) that they rely on.
The text mentions that the Sahibayn do not need the hadith cited for Abu Hanifa.
3
Analyse the tarjih
Later scholars, including the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, favour the Sahibayn because their evidence is stronger. The fatwa is placed on their view.
The claim in al-Mi'raj that the fatwa is on Muhammad's view is considered weak.
4
Determine the mufta bihi
The operative ruling is that lengthening the first over the second is sunnah only in Fajr. In other prayers, it is not sunnah and may be disliked if excessive.
This applies to obligatory prayers; supererogatory prayers have a different ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة
الدراية من
حمل على التشبيه في أصل الإطالة لا في قدرها فهو غير المتبادر ولذا قال في الخلاصة في قول محمد إنه أحب اهـ وتعقبه تلميذه الحلبي بأنه لا يتوقف قولهما باستنان تطويل الأولى على الثانية في الفجر من حيث القدر على الاحتجاج بهذا الحديث فإن لهما أن يثبتان بدليل آخر، فالأحب قولهما لا قوله. وحيث ظهر قوة دليلهما كان الفتوى على قولهما، فما في معراج أن الفتوى على قول محمد ضعيف. وفي المحيط معزياً إلى الفتاوى: الإمام إذا طول القراءة في الركعة الأولى لكي يدركها الناس لا بأس إذا كان تطويلاً لا يثقل على القوم اهـ. فأفاد أن التطويل في سائر الصلوات إن كان لقصد الخير فليس بمكروه وإلا ففيه بأس وهو بمعنى كراهة التنزيه وظاهر إطلاقهم أن الجمعة والعيدين على الخلاف كذلك جامع المحبوبي وفي نظم الزندوستي: تستوي الركعتان في القراءة في الجمعة والعيدين بالاتفاق. وقيد بالأولى لأن إطالة الثانية على الأولى تكره إجماعاً، وإنما يكره التفاوت بثلاث آيات، فإن كان آية أو آيتين لا يكره لأنه قرأ في المغرب بالمعوذتين وإحداهما أطول من الأخرى بآية. كذا في الكافي. ويشكل على هذا الحكم ما ثبت في الصحيحين من قراءته في الجمعة والعيدين في الأولى بسبح اسم ربك الأعلى وفي الثانية «بهل أتاك حديث الغاشية مع أن الثانية أطول من الأول بأكثر من ثلاث آيات فإن الأولى تسع عشرة آية، والثانية ست وعشرون آية وقد يجاب بأن هذه الكراهة في غير ما وردت به السنة، وأما ما ورد عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام في شيء من الصلوات فلا أو الكراهة تنزيهية وفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام تعليماً للجواز لا يوصف بها، والأول أولى لأنهم صرحوا باستنان قراءة هاتين السورتين في الجمعة والعيدين وقيد بالفرض لأنه يسوي في السنن والنوافل بين ركعاتها في القراءة إلا فيما وردت به السنة أو الأثر . كذا في منية المصلي. وصرح في المحيط بكراهة تطويل ركعة من التطوّع ونقص أخرى. وأطلق في جامع المحبوبي عدم كراهة إطالة الأولى على الثانية في السنن والنوافل لأن أمرها سهل واختاره أبو اليسر ومشى عليه في خزانة الفتاوى كما ذكره في شرح منية المصلي فكان الظاهر عدم الكراهة .
Book of Prayer - Chapter on Description of Prayer. The ruling is based on analogy in the principle of lengthening, not in its extent, so it is not the immediate understanding. Hence, in al-Khulasa, regarding Muhammad's statement that it is beloved... and his student al-Halabi objected that their view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the recommendation of lengthening the first over the second in Fajr, in terms of extent, does not depend on this hadith, because they can establish it with another proof. So the beloved view is theirs, not his. Since their proof is stronger, the fatwa is on their view. What is in al-Mi'raj that the fatwa is on Muhammad's view is weak. In al-Muhit, quoting from al-Fatawa: If the imam lengthens the recitation in the first rak'ah so that people may catch it, there is no harm if it is not burdensome on the congregation. So it indicates that lengthening in other prayers, if for a good purpose, is not disliked; otherwise, it is blameworthy, which is tanzihi dislike. Their general statement indicates that Friday and the two Eids are likewise disputed. In Jami' al-Mahbubi and Nazm al-Zandustani: The two rak'ahs in Friday and Eid are equal in recitation by consensus. It is restricted to the first because lengthening the second over the first is disliked by consensus. Disparity is only disliked by three verses; if one or two verses, it is not disliked because he recited in Maghrib the two mu'awwidhat and one is longer than the other by one verse. So in al-Kafi. This ruling is problematic given what is established in the two Sahihs: he recited in Friday and Eid in the first 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la' and in the second 'Hal ataka hadith al-ghashiya', whereas the second is longer than the first by more than three verses, because the first is 19 verses and the second is 26 verses. It can be answered: This dislike applies to what is not established by the Sunnah; as for what is reported from him (peace be upon him) in any prayer, there is no dislike, or the dislike is tanzihi, and his action is for teaching permissibility, not to be described with it. The first is better because they explicitly stated the recommendation of reciting these two surahs in Friday and Eid. It is restricted to obligatory prayers because he makes equal in supererogatory and nafl prayers between their rak'ahs in recitation, except what is established by Sunnah or athar. So in Munyat al-Musalli. And in al-Muhit, it is clearly stated that lengthening one rak'ah of supererogatory and shortening another is disliked. In Jami' al-Mahbubi, it is stated absolutely that there is no dislike in lengthening the first over the second in supererogatory and nafl prayers because their matter is easy; Abu al-Yusr chose this and it is followed in Khizanat al-Fatawa as mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, so the apparent ruling is no dislike.
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recommended length of recitation in the first rak'ah compared to the second. The author first discusses the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Hanifa held that lengthening the first over the second is recommended in all prayers, while the Sahibayn restricted it to Fajr. The text notes that in al-Khulasa, Muhammad's view is presented as 'beloved', but al-Halabi objected that the Sahibayn's proof is independent of the hadith cited. Since their evidence is stronger, the fatwa (operative ruling) is on their view. The author then cites al-Muhit: an imam may lengthen the first rak'ah to allow latecomers to join, provided it does not burden the congregation. For other prayers, if done for good intent, it is not disliked. The discussion moves to Friday and Eid prayers, where the two rak'ahs are equal by consensus. The disliked disparity is specified as three verses or more; less than that is permissible based on prophetic practice. An objection is raised: the Prophet recited in Friday and Eid surahs where the second is longer by more than three verses. The answer: that is not disliked because it follows the Sunnah, or the dislike is tanzihi. The passage concludes that for supererogatory and nafl prayers, there is no dislike in lengthening the first rak'ah, as this is the chosen view of Abu al-Yusr and followed in Khizanat al-Fatawa.

Key Terms
تطويل (tatwil): Lengthening the recitation in prayer; here specifically referring to the first rak'ah relative to the second.
كراهة تنزيه (karahah tanzih): Dislike that is not prohibitive; doing it is not sinful but leaving it is better.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi position in this passage, in which prayer is it sunnah to lengthen the first rak'ah over the second?
A) In all obligatory prayers
B) Only in Fajr
C) In Friday and Eid prayers
D) In all prayers including supererogatory

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi is that tatwil is sunnah only in Fajr; in other obligatory prayers it is not sunnah and may be disliked if excessive.

Rulings on Disparity in Recitation Between Rak'ahs
Details on permissible disparity and exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on disparity in recitation length between rak'ahs and identify the exceptions for Friday/Eid and supererogatory prayers.

Core Idea
Disparity of three verses or more is disliked unless it follows the Sunnah or is in supererogatory prayers.

Beyond the dispute on tatwil, the passage provides detailed rulings on how much disparity is permissible and in which prayers. It addresses the consensus on lengthening the second over the first and the specific cases of Friday, Eid, and supererogatory prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general rule
Disparity in recitation length is disliked (makruh) if it is three verses or more. If one or two verses, it is not disliked.
The basis is the Prophet's recitation of the mu'awwidhat in Maghrib, where one surah is one verse longer.
2
Note the exception for Friday and Eid
In Friday and Eid prayers, the two rak'ahs are equal by consensus, but the prophetic practice shows a longer second rak'ah. This is not disliked because it follows the Sunnah.
The hadith from Sahihayn is used as evidence.
3
Apply to supererogatory prayers
According to the chosen view (Abu al-Yusr, Khizanat al-Fatawa), there is no dislike in lengthening the first over the second in supererogatory and nafl prayers.
Some texts still consider it disliked; the passage follows the easier view.
4
Understand the rationale
The dislike is tanzihi (not prohibitive). Prophetic practice overrides the general dislike. For supererogatory, the matter is easy and not subject to strict rules.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة
الدراية من
حمل على التشبيه في أصل الإطالة لا في قدرها فهو غير المتبادر ولذا قال في الخلاصة في قول محمد إنه أحب اهـ وتعقبه تلميذه الحلبي بأنه لا يتوقف قولهما باستنان تطويل الأولى على الثانية في الفجر من حيث القدر على الاحتجاج بهذا الحديث فإن لهما أن يثبتان بدليل آخر، فالأحب قولهما لا قوله. وحيث ظهر قوة دليلهما كان الفتوى على قولهما، فما في معراج أن الفتوى على قول محمد ضعيف. وفي المحيط معزياً إلى الفتاوى: الإمام إذا طول القراءة في الركعة الأولى لكي يدركها الناس لا بأس إذا كان تطويلاً لا يثقل على القوم اهـ. فأفاد أن التطويل في سائر الصلوات إن كان لقصد الخير فليس بمكروه وإلا ففيه بأس وهو بمعنى كراهة التنزيه وظاهر إطلاقهم أن الجمعة والعيدين على الخلاف كذلك جامع المحبوبي وفي نظم الزندوستي: تستوي الركعتان في القراءة في الجمعة والعيدين بالاتفاق. وقيد بالأولى لأن إطالة الثانية على الأولى تكره إجماعاً، وإنما يكره التفاوت بثلاث آيات، فإن كان آية أو آيتين لا يكره لأنه قرأ في المغرب بالمعوذتين وإحداهما أطول من الأخرى بآية. كذا في الكافي. ويشكل على هذا الحكم ما ثبت في الصحيحين من قراءته في الجمعة والعيدين في الأولى بسبح اسم ربك الأعلى وفي الثانية «بهل أتاك حديث الغاشية مع أن الثانية أطول من الأول بأكثر من ثلاث آيات فإن الأولى تسع عشرة آية، والثانية ست وعشرون آية وقد يجاب بأن هذه الكراهة في غير ما وردت به السنة، وأما ما ورد عنه عليه الصلاة والسلام في شيء من الصلوات فلا أو الكراهة تنزيهية وفعله عليه الصلاة والسلام تعليماً للجواز لا يوصف بها، والأول أولى لأنهم صرحوا باستنان قراءة هاتين السورتين في الجمعة والعيدين وقيد بالفرض لأنه يسوي في السنن والنوافل بين ركعاتها في القراءة إلا فيما وردت به السنة أو الأثر . كذا في منية المصلي. وصرح في المحيط بكراهة تطويل ركعة من التطوّع ونقص أخرى. وأطلق في جامع المحبوبي عدم كراهة إطالة الأولى على الثانية في السنن والنوافل لأن أمرها سهل واختاره أبو اليسر ومشى عليه في خزانة الفتاوى كما ذكره في شرح منية المصلي فكان الظاهر عدم الكراهة .
Book of Prayer - Chapter on Description of Prayer. The ruling is based on analogy in the principle of lengthening, not in its extent, so it is not the immediate understanding. Hence, in al-Khulasa, regarding Muhammad's statement that it is beloved... and his student al-Halabi objected that their view (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) regarding the recommendation of lengthening the first over the second in Fajr, in terms of extent, does not depend on this hadith, because they can establish it with another proof. So the beloved view is theirs, not his. Since their proof is stronger, the fatwa is on their view. What is in al-Mi'raj that the fatwa is on Muhammad's view is weak. In al-Muhit, quoting from al-Fatawa: If the imam lengthens the recitation in the first rak'ah so that people may catch it, there is no harm if it is not burdensome on the congregation. So it indicates that lengthening in other prayers, if for a good purpose, is not disliked; otherwise, it is blameworthy, which is tanzihi dislike. Their general statement indicates that Friday and the two Eids are likewise disputed. In Jami' al-Mahbubi and Nazm al-Zandustani: The two rak'ahs in Friday and Eid are equal in recitation by consensus. It is restricted to the first because lengthening the second over the first is disliked by consensus. Disparity is only disliked by three verses; if one or two verses, it is not disliked because he recited in Maghrib the two mu'awwidhat and one is longer than the other by one verse. So in al-Kafi. This ruling is problematic given what is established in the two Sahihs: he recited in Friday and Eid in the first 'Sabbih isma rabbika al-a'la' and in the second 'Hal ataka hadith al-ghashiya', whereas the second is longer than the first by more than three verses, because the first is 19 verses and the second is 26 verses. It can be answered: This dislike applies to what is not established by the Sunnah; as for what is reported from him (peace be upon him) in any prayer, there is no dislike, or the dislike is tanzihi, and his action is for teaching permissibility, not to be described with it. The first is better because they explicitly stated the recommendation of reciting these two surahs in Friday and Eid. It is restricted to obligatory prayers because he makes equal in supererogatory and nafl prayers between their rak'ahs in recitation, except what is established by Sunnah or athar. So in Munyat al-Musalli. And in al-Muhit, it is clearly stated that lengthening one rak'ah of supererogatory and shortening another is disliked. In Jami' al-Mahbubi, it is stated absolutely that there is no dislike in lengthening the first over the second in supererogatory and nafl prayers because their matter is easy; Abu al-Yusr chose this and it is followed in Khizanat al-Fatawa as mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, so the apparent ruling is no dislike.
Source pages p. 597

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the recommended length of recitation in the first rak'ah compared to the second. The author first discusses the positions of Abu Hanifa and the two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). Abu Hanifa held that lengthening the first over the second is recommended in all prayers, while the Sahibayn restricted it to Fajr. The text notes that in al-Khulasa, Muhammad's view is presented as 'beloved', but al-Halabi objected that the Sahibayn's proof is independent of the hadith cited. Since their evidence is stronger, the fatwa (operative ruling) is on their view. The author then cites al-Muhit: an imam may lengthen the first rak'ah to allow latecomers to join, provided it does not burden the congregation. For other prayers, if done for good intent, it is not disliked. The discussion moves to Friday and Eid prayers, where the two rak'ahs are equal by consensus. The disliked disparity is specified as three verses or more; less than that is permissible based on prophetic practice. An objection is raised: the Prophet recited in Friday and Eid surahs where the second is longer by more than three verses. The answer: that is not disliked because it follows the Sunnah, or the dislike is tanzihi. The passage concludes that for supererogatory and nafl prayers, there is no dislike in lengthening the first rak'ah, as this is the chosen view of Abu al-Yusr and followed in Khizanat al-Fatawa.

Key Terms
تطويل (tatwil): Lengthening the recitation in prayer; here specifically referring to the first rak'ah relative to the second.
كراهة تنزيه (karahah tanzih): Dislike that is not prohibitive; doing it is not sinful but leaving it is better.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on disparity of five verses between rak'ahs in a non-Friday obligatory prayer?
A) Sunnah
B) Makruh tanzih
C) Haram
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Disparity of three verses or more is disliked unless it follows the Sunnah or occurs in supererogatory prayers.

Dislike of Specifying Particular Surahs for Prayers: The Hanafi Ruling and Its Evidences
Ruling on the dislike of specifying surahs for prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on persistently specifying surahs for prayers, explain the evidence from the Quran and the principle of iham al-tafdil, and distinguish between the absolute dislike view and the conditional view of some Hanafis.

Core Idea
Persistently reciting specific surahs for specific prayers is disliked to avoid suggesting superiority and abandoning other surahs.

This lesson examines the Hanafi ruling on a common practice: reciting certain surahs, like Surah al-Sajdah in Friday Fajr, on a regular basis. The Hanafi school considers this disliked (makruh tanzihi) based on the Quranic command to recite what is easy, and the concern that it implies those surahs are superior and leads to neglecting others. We will explore the evidence, the disagreement among Hanafi scholars, and the correct application.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is persistently specifying a particular surah for a particular prayer (e.g., always reciting Surah al-Sajdah in Friday Fajr). The Hanafi ruling is that it is makruh tanzihan (disliked, not sinful).
The dislike is tied to continuity (mudawamah); occasional recitation without persistence is not disliked.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The main evidence is the Quranic verse (73:20): 'So recite what is easy of the Quran.' This indicates that no surah is obligatory beyond al-Fatiha, and specifying one persistently suggests a restriction not intended.
The verse is qati' al-thubut but zanni al-dalala regarding this ruling, as it only implies general permission.
3
Understand the legal reasoning (wajh al-dalalah)
Persistent specification creates iham al-tafdil (the impression of superiority) and leads to hjar al-baqi (abandoning other surahs). Both are disliked; the author prefers to base the dislike on iham al-ta'yin (suggestion of being fixed/necessary) rather than abandonment.
The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq cites Fath al-Qadir to support this preference.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Al-Tahawi and al-Isbijabi condition the dislike on the belief that the prayer is invalid without that surah; otherwise, if recited for ease or blessing, there is no dislike. The majority (apparent from al-Hidayah) say it is disliked absolutely.
The mufta bihi is the absolute dislike, as it aligns with the zahir of the texts.
5
Apply the ruling to scenarios and note the length estimation issue
The dislike applies when there is persistent specification. If one recites these surahs occasionally (e.g., once a month) or reads other surahs in between, it is not disliked. Also, the passage discusses that disparity in length (verses vs. words) must be considered when evaluating whether an increase is apparent.
This resolves apparent contradictions about reciting longer surahs in one rak'ah vs. shorter ones in another.

His statement: 'And nothing specific of the Quran is determined for a prayer' due to the general meaning of His statement 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' [73:20]. By 'not determined' he means not obligatory; otherwise, al-Fatiha is determined as wajib for every prayer. He referred to the dislike of specifying a surah for a prayer because it involves abandoning others and suggesting superiority, like specifying Surah al-Sajdah and Hal Ata 'ala al-Insan for Friday Fajr, and Sabbih Ism, Qul Ya Ayyuha al-Kafirun, and Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad for Witr. So in al-Hidayah and others. Its apparent meaning is that persistence is absolutely disliked, whether one believes the prayer is valid without it or not, because the evidence for dislike is not detailed: it is the suggestion of superiority and abandonment of others. Therefore, there is no need for what al-Tahawi and al-Isbijabi mentioned of dislike if one considers it a necessity that others are disliked. But if one recites for ease or blessing (tabarruk), there is no dislike, provided one occasionally recites others to prevent the ignorant from thinking others are invalid. So and the better view is to make the evidence for dislike the suggestion of specification (iham al-ta'yin) rather than abandonment of others, because abandonment only follows if one does not recite others in another prayer. In Fath al-Qadir: Then the requirement of the evidence is non-persistence, not persistence on non-recitation as practiced by the Hanafis of this time; rather, it is recommended to recite those sometimes for blessing from the reported (ma'thur), because the suggestion of specification is removed by occasionally leaving it. Good, but it may be understood that if the increase is less than half, it is not disliked; this is not so. What is correct is that if the increase is clearly apparent, it is disliked; otherwise not, due to hardship in avoiding what is obvious, and because such is found in hadith. Do not neglect what was mentioned: that the estimation by verses is only considered when they are similar; when they differ, the estimation is by words and letters. Otherwise, 'Alam Nashrah' has 8 verses and 'Lam Yakun' has 8 verses, but there is no doubt that if one recites the first in the first rak'ah and the second in the second, it is disliked because of the apparent increase and length, even if not in terms of verses, but in terms of words and letters. Apply this. So with this mentioned that the estimation by words is considered when there is disparity in length of verses, the problem is resolved as mentioned in al-Sharnablaliyya: the disparity between the two surahs in terms of words due to the disparity of their verses in length and shortness without proximity, and their disparity in words is slight. His statement: 'And the better view is to make...' this is taken from al-Fath where he said: The truth is that the evidence for dislike is the suggestion of specification. And the requirement of making the evidence for dislike that, rather than abandonment of others, is that specification for one praying alone is not disliked because the suggestion is absent with respect to him, as will come from al-Fath, even though the author did not accept that and considered it.

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on specifying certain surahs for particular prayers, such as reciting Surah al-Sajdah and Hal Ata in Fajr on Friday, or Sabbih Ism, Qul Ya Ayyuha al-Kafirun, and Qul Huwa Allahu Ahad in Witr. The basis is the Quranic verse 'So recite what is easy of the Quran' (73:20), indicating that no specific surah is obligatory beyond al-Fatiha. The Hanafi texts (e.g., al-Hidayah) state that it is disliked (makruh) to consistently specify these surahs because it implies they are superior and leads to abandoning other surahs. The author discusses whether the dislike is unconditional or depends on intent. Al-Tahawi and al-Isbijabi said that if one believes the prayer is only valid with that surah, it is disliked; if one recites for ease or blessing, it is not disliked, provided one sometimes recites others to avoid misunderstanding. The author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq prefers to base the dislike on the 'suggestion of specification' (iham al-ta'yin) rather than abandonment, because abandonment only occurs if one never recites others. He cites Fath al-Qadir, which recommends occasionally reciting these surahs for blessing but not persistently. The passage then discusses the estimation of length difference: when verses are similar, count verses; when they differ, count words and letters. This resolves apparent contradictions regarding the dislike of disparity in recitation length. The author ends with a critical note on the view that there is no dislike for the individual praying alone, but the author of al-Bahr al-Ra'iq does not accept that fully.

Key Terms
تعيين سورة (ta'yin surat): Specifying a particular surah for a particular prayer on a regular basis.
إيهام التفضيل (iham al-tafdil): Giving the impression that the specified surah is superior to others.
مداومة (mudawamah): Persistent and continual practice of reciting a specific surah for a specific prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the text, what is the main reason for the dislike of persistently reciting specific surahs in certain prayers?
A) It is against the Quran's command
B) It suggests superiority of those surahs and abandonment of others
C) It is considered a sin (haram)
D) It invalidates the prayer

Key Takeaway
Persistently specifying a surah for a prayer is disliked (makruh tanzihi) to avoid suggesting its superiority and neglecting other Quranic recitation, based on the Quranic command of general recitation.

The Karahah of Constantly Reciting Specific Surahs
Ruling on specifying surahs with evidence and intra-Hanafi discussion

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on constantly reciting specific surahs for specific prayers and explain the two underlying causes (iham al-ta'yin and hajr al-baqi) with their juristic implications.

Core Idea
Constant recitation of the same surah for a specific prayer is makruh because it implies obligation and abandons other Quranic recitation.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author discusses whether it is permissible to always recite, for example, Surah al-Sajdah in the Fajr of Friday or specific surahs in Witr. While no surah besides al-Fatiha is obligatory, the Hanafi school cautions against habitual specification that could mislead others or neglect the rest of the Quran. You will learn the evidence and the preferred position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Ruling
The act is the constant recitation of a specific surah for a specific prayer (e.g., always reciting Surah al-Ikhlas in Witr). The ruling is makruh tanzihi (disliked) according to the Hanafi school.
This karahah applies only to insistence on the same surah, not to occasional or varied recitation.
2
Locate the Dalil
The primary proof is the general command in Quran 73:20, 'So recite what is easy of the Quran,' which shows that no specific surah is obligatory. This is cited to negate obligation.
The dalil is used to establish that the karahah is not about prohibition of the surah itself, but about the habitual practice.
3
Understand the Causes of Karahah
Two main causes are given: (1) iham al-ta'yin – giving the false impression that the surah is mandatory; (2) hajr al-baqi – abandoning the rest of the Quran by never reciting other surahs in that prayer.
The author later prefers iham al-ta'yin as the primary cause, but the mashayikh also consider hajr al-baqi independently.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Some scholars (al-Tahawi, al-Isbijabi) held that karahah only applies if one believes the surah is mandatory; otherwise, reciting for ease or blessing is not disliked. The majority, however, hold absolute karahah due to hajr al-baqi.
The mufta bihi is absolute karahah, as stated: 'فتكره المداومة مطلقاً.'
5
Apply to Contemporary Practice
Even if one prays alone, the karahah remains because hajr al-baqi is not limited to congregational settings. Therefore, one should vary surahs and avoid constant repetition.
Recommended practice: recite the sunnah surahs (e.g., al-Kafirun and al-Ikhlas in Fajr sunnah) but occasionally substitute others.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب صفة الصلاة
الصلاة والسلام تعليماً للجواز لا يوصف بها، والأول أولى لأنهم صرحوا باستنان قراءة هاتين السورتين في الجمعة والعيدين وقيد بالفرض لأنه يسوي في السنن والنوافل بين ركعاتها في القراءة إلا فيما وردت به السنة أو الأثر . كذا في منية المصلي. وصرح في المحيط بكراهة تطويل ركعة من التطوّع ونقص أخرى. وأطلق في جامع المحبوبي عدم كراهة إطالة الأولى على الثانية في السنن والنوافل لأن أمرها سهل واختاره أبو اليسر ومشى عليه في خزانة الفتاوى كما ذكره في شرح منية المصلي فكان الظاهر عدم الكراهة .
قوله: (ولم يتعين شيء من القرآن [لصلاة] لإطلاق قوله تعالى فاقرءوا ما تيسر من القرآن [المزمل: ۲۰] أراد بعدم التعيين عدم الفرضية وإلا فالفاتحة متعينة على وجه الوجوب لكل صلاة. وأشار إلى كراهة تعيين سورة لصلاة لما فيه من هجر الباقي وإيهام التفضيل كتعيين سورة «السجدة» وهل أتى على الإنسان في فجر كل جمعة وسبح اسم ربك» و«قل يا أيها الكافرون» و«قل هو الله أحد» في الوتر . كذا في الهداية وغيرها. وظاهره أن المداومة مكروهة مطلقاً، سواء اعتقد أن الصلاة تجوز بغيره أو لا، لأن دليل الكراهة لم يفصل وهو أن إيهام التفضيل وهجر الباقي فحينئذ لا حاجة إلى ما ذكره الطحاوي والاسبيجابي من الكراهة إذا رآه حتماً يكره غيره، أما لو قرأ للتيسير عليه أو تبركاً بقراءته فلا كراهة لكن بشرط أن يقرأ غيرها أحياناً لئلا يظن الجاهل أن غيرها لا يجوز .اهـ. والأولى أن يجعل دليل كراهة المداومة إيهام التعيين لا هجر الباقي لأنه إنما يلزم لو لم يقرأ الباقي في صلاة أخرى. وفي فتح القدير: ثم مقتضى الدليل عدم المداومة لا المداومة على العدم كما يفعله حنفية العصر، بل يستحب أن يقرأ ذلك أحياناً تبركاً بالمأثور فإن لزوم الإيهام ينتفي ولورود مثل هذا في الحديث. ولا تغفل عما تقدم أن التقدير بالآيات إنما يعتبر عند تقاربها، وأما عند تفاوتها فالمعتبر التقدير بالكلمات والحروف وإلا فـ ألم نشرح لك ثمان آيات و لم يكن ثمان آيات، ولا شك أنه التفاوت بطول الآي وقصرها اندفع الإشكال أيضاً كما ذكره في الشرنبلالية قال: إذ التفاوت بين السورتين من حيث الكلمات لتفاوت آياتهما في الطول والقصر من غير تقارب وتفاوتهما في الكلمات يسير قوله : ( والأولى أن يجعل الخ هذا مأخوذ من الفتح حيث قال : فالحق أنه أي دليل الكراهة إيهام التعيين .اهـ ومقتضى جعل دليل الكراهة ذلك دون هجر الباقي أنه لا يكره التعيين للمنفرد لانتفاء الإيهام بالنسبة إليه كما سيأتي عن الفتح مع أن المؤلف لم يرض بذلك ونظر فيه
