ولذا قالوا السنة أن يقرأ في ركعتي الفجر بقل يا أيها الكافرون» و«قل هو الله أحد». وظاهر هذا إفادة المواظبة على ذلك وذلك لأن الإيهام المذكور منتف بالنسبة إلى المصلي نفسه اهـ. وفيه نظر لما صرح به في غاية البيان من كراهة المواظبة على قراءة السور الثلاث في الوتر أعم من كونه في رمضان إماماً أو لا فما في فتح القدير مبني على أن العلة إيهام التعيين، وأما على ما علل به المشايخ من هجر الباقي فهو موجود، سواء كان يصلي وحده أو إماماً، وسواء كان في الفرض أو في غيره، فتكره المداومة مطلقاً.
Book of Prayer - Chapter on Description of Prayer. Peace and blessings as instruction for permissibility is not described by it, and the first is better because they explicitly stated the recommendation of reciting these two surahs on Friday and the two Eids, and he restricted it to obligatory because it equalizes the supererogatory and optional prayers between their rak'ahs in recitation except what is reported by Sunnah or athar. Likewise in Munyat al-Musalli. And in al-Muhit, he explicitly stated the dislike of lengthening a rak'ah of supererogatory and shortening another. And in Jami' al-Mahbubi, he declared the absence of dislike of lengthening the first over the second in supererogatory and optional prayers because their matter is easy, and Abu al-Yusr chose it and followed it in Khizanat al-Fatawa as mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli, so the apparent is no dislike. He said: (And nothing of the Quran is specified for a prayer) due to the generality of His statement, exalted: So recite what is easy of the Quran [al-Muzzammil:20]. He intended by non-specification the lack of obligation; otherwise, al-Fatiha is specified on the basis of obligation for every prayer. And he indicated the dislike of specifying a surah for a prayer because of abandoning the rest and implying preference, like specifying Surah al-Sajdah and 'Has there come to man' in the Fajr of every Friday, and 'Glorify the name of your Lord', and 'Say: O disbelievers', and 'Say: He is Allah, [the] One' in the Witr. Likewise in al-Hidayah and others. Its apparent is that constancy is disliked absolutely, whether one believes that the prayer is permissible with other than it or not, because the evidence for dislike did not differentiate. So then there is no need for what al-Tahawi and al-Isbijabi mentioned: dislike if he sees it as mandatory that other than it is disliked; but if he recites for ease or blessing, there is no dislike, but on condition that he recites other than it sometimes so that the ignorant does not think that other than it is not permissible. End. And it is better to make the evidence for dislike of constancy iham al-ta'yin, not hajr al-baqi, because it is only necessitated if he did not recite the rest in another prayer. And in Fath al-Qadir: Then the requirement of evidence is non-constancy, not constancy upon non-existence as the Hanafis of the age do; rather, it is recommended that he recite that sometimes for blessing of the transmitted, for the implication of iham is removed by leaving it sometimes. Good, except that perhaps one may mistakenly think. From it: that when the increase is less than half, it is not disliked, and it is not so; and what is proper is that if the increase is clearly apparent, it is disliked; otherwise not, due to the difficulty of avoiding reality, and due to the occurrence of such in the hadith. And do not neglect what preceded that estimation by verses is only considered when they are close; but when they differ, estimation by words and letters is considered, otherwise 'Alam nashrah laka' is eight verses and 'Lam yakun' is eight verses, and there is no doubt that if one recites the first in the first and the second in the second, it is disliked due to what we said of apparent increase and length, even if not in terms of verses, but in terms of words and letters, and analogize to this. End. And by this mentioned that estimation is by words when there is difference in length and shortness of verses, the difficulty is resolved, as mentioned in al-Sharnablaliyya, he said: For the difference between the two surahs in terms of words is due to the difference of their verses in length and shortness without proximity, and their difference in words is small. He said: (And it is better that) etc. This is taken from al-Fath where he said: The truth is that it, i.e., the evidence for dislike, is iham al-ta'yin. End. And the implication of making the evidence for dislike that, rather than hajr al-baqi, is that specification is not disliked for the one praying alone, because the iham is negated with respect to him, as will come from al-Fath, although the author did not approve of that and considered it. He recited a verse of encouragement or deterrence, or gave a sermon, or sent blessings upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, and the distant is like the near. Therefore they said: The sunnah is to recite in the two rak'ahs of Fajr 'Say: O disbelievers' and 'Say: He is Allah, [the] One'. And the apparent of this indicates constant practice upon that, because the aforementioned iham is negated with respect to the worshipper himself. End. And there is consideration for what is explicitly stated in Ghayat al-Bayan: dislike of constant practice on reciting the three surahs in Witr, whether in Ramadan as an imam or not. So what is in Fath al-Qadir is based on the cause being iham al-ta'yin; but on the basis of what the mashayikh gave as cause of hajr al-baqi, it exists, whether he prays alone or as imam, and whether in obligatory or other, so constant practice is disliked absolutely.
Source pages p. 598

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, discussing the permissibility and ruling of specifying particular surahs for particular prayers. The author begins by clarifying that no specific surah is obligatory (fard) for any prayer, based on the general Quranic command to recite what is easy (Quran 73:20). However, the Fatiha is obligatory in every prayer as a condition of validity. The main ruling is that it is makruh (disliked) to habitually recite the same surahs for specific prayers, such as always reciting Surah Sajdah in Fajr of Friday, or repeating the same three surahs in Witr. The underlying reasons are twofold: first, it gives the false impression that those surahs are compulsory (iham al-ta'yin), and second, it leads to abandoning other parts of the Quran (hajr al-baqi). The passage then presents a debate among scholars about which reason is primary. Some, like al-Tahawi and al-Isbijabi, held that the karaahah only applies if one believes the surah is mandatory; otherwise, reciting for ease or blessing is not disliked, provided one occasionally recites other surahs. The preferred view, taken from Fath al-Qadir and supported by the mashayikh, is that constant practice (muwazabah) is makruh absolutely, because the cause of hajr al-baqi is always present. Even for a lone worshipper, it is still makruh because hajr al-baqi is not limited to congregation. The author also addresses the issue of lengthening one rak'ah over another in supererogatory prayers, noting that it is not necessarily disliked when done moderately. The passage concludes by affirming the sunnah of reciting specific surahs in the Fajr sunnah, but warns against making it a constant habit that leads to abandoning other surahs.

Key Terms
إيهام التعيين (iham al-ta'yin): Giving the impression that a particular surah is specifically required or obligatory for a particular prayer.
هجر الباقي (hajr al-baqi): Abandoning the rest of the Quran by constantly reciting only certain surahs or verses.
المواظبة (al-muwazabah): Continuous and habitual practice; constancy in reciting specific surahs for specific prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is it makruh to constantly recite the same surahs for specific prayers (e.g., Surah Sajdah in Fajr on Friday)?
A) Because it is considered bid'ah
B) Because it gives the impression that the surah is obligatory or leads to abandoning other surahs
C) Because the Prophet forbade specifying surahs altogether
D) Because it invalidates the prayer if the surah is omitted

Key Takeaway
Constant recitation of the same surah for a specific prayer is makruh tanzihi due to iham al-ta'yin and hajr al-baqi.

The Muqtadi's Recitation: Ruling and Proof
Ruling with proof on follower's recitation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the muqtadi's recitation behind the imam and explain the proof from the hadith and its specification of the general Quranic command.

Core Idea
The follower does not recite; the imam's recitation suffices, based on a specific hadith.

One of the key questions in congregational prayer is whether the follower should recite when the imam recites. This lesson examines the Hanafi position that the muqtadi must remain silent and listen, even in silent prayers. The primary evidence is a prophetic hadith that specifies the general command to recite in the Quran. Understanding this ruling requires analyzing how a khabar al-wahid can specify an 'amm text.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the muqtadi's recitation of Quran behind the imam. The ruling is that he does not recite but listens and remains silent, in both jahri and sirri prayers.
2
Locate the primary dalil
The primary proof is the hadith: 'Whoever has an imam, the imam's recitation is his recitation.' This hadith is a khabar al-wahid but is accepted for specification.
The hadith is cited from multiple chains.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The hadith explicitly states that the imam's recitation suffices for the follower. This specifies the general command in Quran 73:20 ('So recite what is easy') by excluding the follower from the obligation to recite.
The general command initially includes all, but the hadith removes the follower.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
There is a narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani that recommends recitation in silent prayers as a precaution, while Abu Yusuf and the later position from Muhammad hold it is makruh. The relied-upon position is absolute non-recitation.
The author sides with the absolute prohibition.
5
Understand the final tarjih
The tarjih is based on the clarity of the hadith and the threat implied in reciting behind the imam. The practical ruling for fatwa is that the muqtadi does not recite at all.
This is the mufta bihi position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يقرأ المؤتم بل يستمع وينصت وإن قرأ آية الترغيب أو الترهيب أو خطب أو صلى على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والنائي كالقريب) للحديث المروي من طرق عديدة من كان له إمام فقراءة القرآن له قراءة (۱) فكان مخصصاً لعموم قوله تعالى فاقرءوا ما تيسر بناء على أنه خص منه المدرك في الركوع إجماعاً فجاز تخصيصه بعده بخبر الواحد ولعموم الحديث «لا صلاة إلا بقراءة » فإن قلت : حيث جاز تخصيصه بعده بخبر الواحد فينبغي تخصيص عمومها بالفاتحة عملاً بخبر الفاتحة قلت التخصيص الأوّل إنما هو في المأمورين ولم يقع تخصيص لعموم المقروء فلم يجز تخصيصه بالظني. أطلقه فشمل الصلاة الجهرية والسرية، وفي الهداية ويستحسن على سبيل الاحتياط فيما يروى عن محمد ويكره عندهما لما فيه من الوعيد وتعقبه في غاية البيان بأن محمداً صرح في كتبه بعدم القراءة خلف الإمام فيما يجهر . بما سينقله عن غاية البيان قوله : (فما) في فتح القدير مبني الخ قال في النهر أقول: قد علل المشايخ بهما كما قدمناه عن الهداية والظاهر أنهما علة واحدة لا علتان وبهذا اتجه ما في الفتح. قول المصنف : (وإن قرأ آية الترغيب أو الترهيب أي يستمع المؤتم وإن قرأ الإمام ما ذكر . قال في النهر : وكذا الإمام لا يشتغل بغير قراءة القرآن سواء أم في الفرض أو النفل . أما المنفرد ففي الفرض كذلك، وفي النفل يسأل الجنة ويتعوّذ من النار عند ذكرهما ويتفكر في آية المثل وقد ذكروا فيه حديث حذيفة رضي الله تعالى عنه وأنه صلى معه عليه الصلاة والسلام فما مر بآية فيها ذكر الجنة إلا سأل فيها، وما مر بآية فيها ذكر النار إلا تعوّذ فيها. وهذا يقتضي أن الإمام يفعل في النافلة وهم صرحوا بالمنع إلا أنهم عللوا بالتطويل على المقتدي وعلى هذا لو أمّ من يطلب منه ذلك فعله يعني في التراويح والكسوف وإلا فالتجمع في النافلة مكروه في غيرهما قوله: (ولم يقع تخصيص لعموم المقروء الخ) حاصله أن في الآية صيغتي عموم علامة الجمع وما والتخصيص حصل للأولى
(۱) رواه ابن ماجه في كتاب الإقامة باب ۱۳ أحمد في مسنده (۳۳۹/۳) بلفظ «فقراءة الإمام» بدل «فقراءة القرآن».
(۲) رواه مسلم في كتاب الصلاة حديث .٤٢ أبو داود في كتاب الصلاة باب ١٣٢. الترمذي في كتاب الصلاة باب .١١٦ أحمد في مسنده (٣٠٨/٢، ٤٢٨).
His statement: (And the follower does not recite, but listens and remains silent, even if he recites a verse of encouragement or deterrence, or gives a sermon, or sends blessings upon the Prophet, peace be upon him, and the distant is like the near) due to the hadith narrated through many chains: 'Whoever has an imam, the imam's recitation is his recitation' (1). Thus it was a specification of the generality of His statement, exalted: So recite what is easy of the Quran, based on the fact that the one who catches the bowing is excluded from it by consensus, so it is permissible to specify it by a khabar wahid. And due to the generality of the hadith 'No prayer except with recitation'. If you say: Since it is permissible to specify it by a khabar wahid, then one should specify its generality with al-Fatiha, acting upon the hadith of al-Fatiha. I say: The first specification was concerning those commanded, and no specification has occurred for the generality of what is recited, so it is not permissible to specify it by the zanni. He made it absolute, so it includes jahri and sirri prayers. And in al-Hidayah: It is considered mustahsan as a precaution in what is narrated from Muhammad, and it is disliked according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) due to the threat. And he criticized it in Ghayat al-Bayan by saying that Muhammad explicitly stated in his books that there is no recitation behind the imam in what is audible. As he will quote from Ghayat al-Bayan. He said: (So what) in Fath al-Qadir is based on... He said in al-Nahr: I say: The mashayikh have given cause with both as we presented from al-Hidayah, and the apparent is that they are one cause, not two causes, and with this what is in al-Fath is consistent. The statement of the author: (And if he recites a verse of encouragement or deterrence) means the follower listens even if the imam recites what was mentioned. He said in al-Nahr: Likewise, the imam does not occupy himself with other than reciting the Quran, whether he leads in obligatory or supererogatory. As for the one praying alone, in obligatory it is likewise; and in supererogatory, he asks for Paradise and seeks refuge from Hellfire when they are mentioned, and ponders over the verse of the parable, and they mentioned the hadith of Hudhayfah, may Allah be pleased with him, that he prayed with him, peace be upon him, and he did not pass by a verse mentioning Paradise except that he asked for it, and did not pass by a verse mentioning Hellfire except that he sought refuge from it. This necessitates that the imam does this in supererogatory, and they explicitly prohibited it except that they cited the reason of lengthening for the follower. Based on this, if he leads someone who seeks that from him, he does it, meaning in Tarawih and Eclipse; otherwise, congregation in supererogatory is disliked in other than these two. He said: (And no specification has occurred for the generality of what is recited, etc.) The gist is that in the verse there are two forms of generality: the sign of the plural and 'ma', and specification occurred for the first. (1) Narrated by Ibn Majah in Book of Iqamah, Bab 13; Ahmad in his Musnad (3/339) with the wording 'the imam's recitation' instead of 'the Quran's recitation'. (2) Narrated by Muslim in Book of Prayer, Hadith 42; Abu Dawud in Book of Prayer, Bab 132; al-Tirmidhi in Book of Prayer, Bab 116; Ahmad in his Musnad (2/308, 428).
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof, addressing the recitation of the muqtadi (follower) behind the imam. The core ruling is that the follower does not recite the Quran, but listens and remains silent, even if the imam recites verses of encouragement or deterrence, gives a sermon, or sends blessings. This applies whether the prayer is jahri (audible) or sirri (silent). The primary evidence is the hadith: 'Whoever has an imam, the imam's recitation is his recitation.' This hadith specifies the general command in Quran 73:20 to 'recite what is easy', since the general command includes all prayers, but the follower is exempted by this hadith. The passage then addresses an objection: if this hadith can specify the general command, why not also specify that only al-Fatiha must be recited based on the hadith 'No prayer except with recitation'? The answer is that the hadith regarding the imam specifies who must recite (the followers are excluded), but it does not specify what must be recited; therefore, the general command to recite remains applicable to the imam. The text also clarifies that this ruling includes both jahri and sirri prayers. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: According to a narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani, it is mustahsan (recommended) for the follower to recite al-Fatiha in silent prayers as a precaution, while according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two) it is makruh due to the threat. However, al-Ghayah al-Bayan notes that Muhammad himself stated in his books that there is no recitation behind the imam in audible prayers, indicating that the mustahsan view may apply only to silent prayers. The relied-upon position is that the follower does not recite at all, as the hadith is clear. The passage also discusses the imam's actions: he should not engage in non-Quranic speech during obligatory prayers, but in supererogatory prayers, it is permissible for him to supplicate, such as asking for Paradise or seeking refuge from Hell, based on the practice of the Prophet as reported by Hudhayfah. The imam may recite such supplications in Tarawih and Eclipse prayers if the followers desire it; otherwise, congregational supererogatory prayers other than these are disliked.

Key Terms
المؤتم (al-mu'tam): The follower in congregational prayer who prays behind an imam.
الجهرية والسرية (al-jahriyyah wa al-sirriyyah): Prayers where the imam recites aloud (Fajr, Maghrib, Isha) and prayers where he recites silently (Zuhr, Asr).
خبر الواحد (khabar al-wahid): A hadith narrated by one or a few companions, not reaching tawatur, used to specify a general Quranic command.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) The hadith 'Whoever has an imam, the imam's recitation is his recitation'
C) Consensus of the Sahaba
D) The hadith 'No prayer except with recitation'

Key Takeaway
The muqtadi must not recite behind the imam; the imam's recitation suffices, based on the prophetic hadith that specifies the general obligation.

The Follower's Obligation to Listen and Be Silent Behind the Imam
Establishing that the follower must listen and be silent during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the follower's recitation behind the imam, identify the primary evidence, and distinguish between the positions of the Sahibayn and Abu Hanifa.

Core Idea
The follower does not recite; the imam's recitation suffices, and silence is obligatory.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq establishes a core Hanafi position: the follower (mu'tamm) must not recite behind the imam in any prayer. The author presents the hadith evidence and addresses an intra-Hanafi difference, ultimately affirming the relied-upon view. Understanding this ruling clarifies a key distinction between Hanafi and Shafi'i practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling
The matn states: the follower does not recite; he listens and is silent. This applies to all prayers, loud and quiet.
The phrase 'wa la yaqra'u' indicates prohibition.
2
Locate the primary proof
The hadith 'Man kana lahu imamun fa qira'atu al-Qur'ani lahu qira'atun' is the main evidence.
The hadith is narrated through multiple chains but is ahad, hence zanni al-thubut.
3
Understand the specification
This hadith specifies the general Quranic command to recite (faqra'u ma tayassara) for the follower. The specification is justified by consensus on exceptions and the principle that a khabar wahid can specify a general text.
The specification does not extend to limiting the content to al-Fatiha; that would require a separate qat'i evidence.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
A weak narration from Muhammad al-Shaybani allows recitation in sirri prayers as a precaution, but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad in his dominant view) consider it makruh. Abu Hanifa holds absolute prohibition.
The claim of precaution is rejected because leaving recitation acts on the stronger proof.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
The relied-upon position is that of Abu Hanifa: the follower must not recite in any prayer. The ruling is makruh tahrimi due to the zanni nature of the evidence.
Al-Hidayah and Fath al-Qadir affirm this tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (ولا يقرأ المؤتم بل يستمع وينصت وإن قرأ آية الترغيب أو الترهيب أو خطب أو صلى على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والنائي كالقريب) للحديث المروي من طرق عديدة من كان له إمام فقراءة القرآن له قراءة فكان مخصصاً لعموم قوله تعالى فاقرءوا ما تيسر بناء على أنه خص منه المدرك في الركوع إجماعاً فجاز تخصيصه بعده بخبر الواحد ولعموم الحديث «لا صلاة إلا بقراءة » فإن قلت : حيث جاز تخصيصه بعده بخبر الواحد فينبغي تخصيص عمومها بالفاتحة عملاً بخبر الفاتحة قلت التخصيص الأوّل إنما هو في المأمورين ولم يقع تخصيص لعموم المقروء فلم يجز تخصيصه بالظني. أطلقه فشمل الصلاة الجهرية والسرية، وفي الهداية ويستحسن على سبيل الاحتياط فيما يروى عن محمد ويكره عندهما لما فيه من الوعيد وتعقبه في غاية البيان بأن محمداً صرح في كتبه بعدم القراءة خلف الإمام فيما يجهر وما لا يجهر فيه . قال : وبه نأخذ وهو قول أبي حنيفة. ويجاب عنه بأن صاحب الهداية لم يجزم بأنه قول محمد بل ظاهرها أنها رواية ضعيفة. وفي فتح القدير: والحق أن قول محمد كقولهما. والمراد من الكراهة كراهة التحريم وفي بعض العبارات أنها لا تحل خلفه وإنما لم يطلقوا اسم الحرمة عليها لما عرف من أن أصلهم أنهم لا يطلقونها إلا إذا كان الدليل قطعياً، ودعوى الاحتياط في القراءة خلفه ممنوعة بل الاحتياط تركها لأنه العمل بأقوى الدليلين، وقد روي عن عدة من الصحابة فساد الصلاة بالقراءة خلفه فأقواهما المنع. وأشار بقوله «بل يستمع وينصت إلى آخره إلى أن الآية نزلت في الصلاة وهي قوله تعالى (وإذا قرىء القرآن فاستمعوا له وانصتوا لعلكم ترحمون [الأعراف : ٢٠٤] وهو قول أكثر أهل التفسير. ومنهم من قال : نزلت في الخطبة . قال في الكافي : ولا تنافي بينهما فإنما أمروا بهما فيها لما فيها من قراءة القرآن وحاصل الآية أن المطلوب بها أمران الاستماع والسكوت، فيعمل بكل منهما والأول يخص الجهرية، والثاني لا فيجري على إطلاقه فيجب السكوت عند القراءة مطلقاً. ولما كان العبرة إنما هو لعموم اللفظ لا لخصوص السبب وجب الاستماع لقراءة القرآن خارج الصلاة أيضاً ولهذا قال في الخلاصة : رجل يكتب الفقه وبجنبه رجل يقرأ القرآن ولا يمكنه استماع القرآن فالإثم على القارىء . وعلى هذا لو قرأ على السطح في الليل جهراً والناس نيام يأثم. وفي القنية وغيرها الصبي إذا كان يقرأ القرآن وأهله يشتغلون بالأعمال ولا يستمعون إن كان شرعوا في العمل قبل قراءته لا يأثمون وإلا أثموا.
His saying: (And the follower does not recite, but rather listens and is silent, even if he recites a verse of encouragement or warning, or delivers a sermon, or sends blessings upon the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, and the distant one is like the near one) because of the hadith narrated through many chains: 'Whoever has an imam, the recitation of the Quran is recitation for him.' So it became a specification of the generality of His statement, the Exalted: 'So recite what is easy [of the Quran]' based on the fact that from it was specified the one who catches the bowing by consensus, so it is permissible to specify it after that with a hadith of a single narrator, and because of the generality of the hadith 'There is no prayer except with recitation.' If you say: Since it is permissible to specify it after that with a hadith of a single narrator, then one should specify its generality with al-Fatihah, acting on the hadith of al-Fatihah. I say: The first specification is only concerning those commanded, and no specification occurred for the generality of what is recited, so it is not permissible to specify it with a speculative proof. He made it absolute, so it includes both loud and quiet prayers. In al-Hidayah: It is considered commendable as a precaution in what is narrated from Muhammad, and it is disliked according to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) because of the threat [contained in the hadith]. It was criticized in Ghayat al-Bayan because Muhammad stated in his books that there is no recitation behind the imam in loud prayers and in quiet prayers. He said: We adopt this, and it is the saying of Abu Hanifah. The response to that is that the author of al-Hidayah did not confirm that it was the saying of Muhammad; rather, its apparent meaning is that it is a weak narration. In Fath al-Qadir: The truth is that the saying of Muhammad is like their saying (the two). And the intended meaning of dislike is dislike of prohibition, and in some expressions it is that it is not permissible behind him, and they only did not apply the name of prohibition to it because of what is known that their principle is that they do not apply it except when the evidence is definitive. The claim of precaution in reciting behind him is rejected; rather, precaution is to leave it because it is acting on the stronger of the two proofs. And it has been narrated from several companions that the prayer is corrupted by reciting behind him, so the stronger of the two is prohibition. And he indicated by his saying 'rather he listens and is silent' to the end that the verse was revealed concerning prayer, and it is His statement, the Exalted: 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent that you may receive mercy' [al-A'raf: 204], and this is the saying of most of the commentators. And some of them said: It was revealed concerning the sermon. Al-Kafi said: There is no contradiction between them, for they were commanded with both because of what is in it of Quran recitation. The conclusion of the verse is that what is required by it are two matters: listening and silence. Each is acted upon. The first is specific to loud prayers, and the second is not, so it is applied absolutely. So silence is obligatory during recitation without qualification. And since consideration is only for the generality of the wording, not for the specificity of the cause, listening to the recitation of the Quran outside of prayer is also obligatory. For this reason, al-Khulasa said: A man writes fiqh and next to him another man recites the Quran, and he cannot listen to the Quran, so the sin is upon the reciter. And based on this, if he recites on the roof at night loudly while people are sleeping, he sins. In al-Qunyah and others: A child who recites the Quran while his family is occupied with work and they do not listen – if they started work before his recitation, they do not sin; otherwise, they sin.
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hanafi school (Zahir al-Riwayah) concerning the follower's recitation behind the imam. The matn states that the follower must not recite; rather, he listens and is silent. The author of the sharh then provides the evidence: a hadith that the imam's recitation suffices for the follower, and the Quranic verse commanding listening and silence. He discusses the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: a narration from Muhammad reports that the follower should recite in quiet prayers as a precaution, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) consider it disliked. Abu Hanifa holds that the follower does not recite at all. The relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is that of Abu Hanifa, and the dislike is at the level of karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibitively disliked) because the evidence is zanni (speculative). The commentary also extends the obligation of listening and silence to outside the prayer context, citing examples from Hanafi works. The ruling applies equally to the distant follower (na'i) as to the close one.

Key Terms
مؤتم (mu'tamm): The person praying behind an imam (follower).
استماع (istimā'): Active listening to the imam's recitation with attention.
إنصات (inṣāt): Being silent and not engaging in any speech or recitation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on the follower reciting behind the imam in a quiet (sirri) prayer?
A) It is permissible and recommended.
B) It is prohibited (haram) because the evidence is definitive.
C) It is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) and the follower must remain silent.
D) It is obligatory to recite al-Fatiha.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that the follower must not recite behind the imam in any prayer; silence and listening are obligatory, and recitation is prohibitively disliked.

Constant Repetition of Surahs and Rulings on Targhib/Tarhib Recitation
Ruling on constant surah repetition and targhib/tarhib

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on constant repetition of specific surahs in prayer and explain the conduct of the follower and imam when verses of targhib/tarhib are recited, citing the relevant proofs.

Core Idea
Constant surah repetition is disliked as it abandons others; followers remain silent upon hearing targhib/tarhib.

This lesson examines two related rulings from the chapter of prayer: the dislike of persistently reciting the same surahs (like in Witr) and the proper conduct of the follower and imam when verses of encouragement or warning are recited. Both derive from the principles of avoiding confusion and unnecessary prolongation of prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two main rulings
The passage discusses (a) the ruling on constant repetition of specific surahs and (b) the conduct of the follower and imam during targhib/tarhib verses.
2
Analyze the cause for dislike
For constant repetition, the cause is either confusion of specification (that the surahs might be thought obligatory) or abandonment of other surahs. The latter is always present, so constancy is disliked absolutely.
The text cites Ghayat al-Bayan for this ruling.
3
Examine the proof for the follower's silence
The hadith of Hudhayfah shows the Prophet's practice in supererogatory prayer, but the Hanafi position restricts it to the one praying alone; the follower remains silent to avoid prolongation for the congregation.
4
Distinguish between obligatory and supererogatory
In obligatory prayer, neither imam nor follower engage in asking or seeking refuge; in supererogatory, the one praying alone may do so, and the imam may do so if the followers desire it (as in taraweeh and eclipse).
5
Note the condition for imam's action
The imam in supererogatory may recite targhib/tarhib and ask/seek refuge only if the followers want that; otherwise, it is disliked.
Gathering for supererogatory prayer other than taraweeh and eclipse is itself disliked.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قرأ آية الترغيب والترهيب أو خطب أو صلى على النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم والنائي كالقريب. ولذا قالوا السنة أن يقرأ في ركعتي الفجر بقل يا أيها الكافرون وقل هو الله أحد. وظاهر هذا إفادة المواظبة على ذلك وذلك لأن الإيهام المذكور منتف بالنسبة إلى المصلي نفسه اهـ. وفيه نظر لما صرح به في غاية البيان من كراهة المواظبة على قراءة السور الثلاث في الوتر أعم من كونه في رمضان إماماً أو لا فما في فتح القدير مبني على أن العلة إيهام التعيين، وأما على ما علل به المشايخ من هجر الباقي فهو موجود، سواء كان يصلي وحده أو إماماً، وسواء كان في الفرض أو في غيره، فتكره المداومة مطلقاً. قول المصنف : (وإن قرأ آية الترغيب أو الترهيب أي يستمع المؤتم وإن قرأ الإمام ما ذكر . قال في النهر : وكذا الإمام لا يشتغل بغير قراءة القرآن سواء أم في الفرض أو النفل . أما المنفرد ففي الفرض كذلك، وفي النفل يسأل الجنة ويتعوّذ من النار عند ذكرهما ويتفكر في آية المثل وقد ذكروا فيه حديث حذيفة رضي الله تعالى عنه وأنه صلى معه عليه الصلاة والسلام فما مر بآية فيها ذكر الجنة إلا سأل فيها، وما مر بآية فيها ذكر النار إلا تعوّذ فيها. وهذا يقتضي أن الإمام يفعل في النافلة وهم صرحوا بالمنع إلا أنهم عللوا بالتطويل على المقتدي وعلى هذا لو أمّ من يطلب منه ذلك فعله يعني في التراويح والكسوف وإلا فالتجمع في النافلة مكروه في غيرهما.
He recited a verse of encouragement or warning, or he delivered a sermon, or he sent blessings upon the Prophet, may God bless him and grant him peace, and the distant one is like the near one. Therefore, they said: It is Sunnah to recite in the two rak'ahs of Fajr 'Say, O disbelievers' and 'Say, He is God, One.' The apparent meaning of this indicates constancy upon that, and that is because the mentioned confusion is absent concerning the worshipper himself. But there is consideration for what was stated in Ghayat al-Bayan of the dislike of constancy upon reciting the three surahs in Witr, whether in Ramadan as imam or not. So what is in Fath al-Qadir is based on the cause being the confusion of specification. But according to what the scholars have reasoned of abandoning the rest, it exists, whether he prays alone or as imam, and whether in obligatory or other prayers. So constancy is disliked absolutely. The author's saying: (And if he recites a verse of encouragement or warning) meaning the follower listens, even if the imam recited what was mentioned. Al-Nahr said: Likewise, the imam does not occupy himself with other than recitation of the Quran, whether he prays as imam in obligatory or supererogatory. As for the one praying alone, in obligatory it is likewise, and in supererogatory he asks for Paradise and seeks refuge from Hellfire when they are mentioned and reflects on the verse of the example. They mentioned the hadith of Hudhayfah, may God be pleased with him, that he prayed with him, peace be upon him, and he did not pass by a verse mentioning Paradise except that he asked for it, and he did not pass by a verse mentioning Hellfire except that he sought refuge from it. This requires that the imam does it in supererogatory prayer, and they stated the prohibition except that they reasoned it with prolonging for the follower. Based on this, if he leads someone who seeks that, he does it, meaning in taraweeh and eclipse prayers; otherwise, gathering in supererogatory prayer is disliked in other than these.
Source pages p. 599

Commentary
This passage begins by quoting a portion of the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq: the ruling that the follower listens and is silent even if the imam recites verses of targhib (encouragement) or tarhib (warning), or delivers a khutbah, or sends salawat. The same ruling applies to the distant follower (na'i) as to the close one. The commentary then discusses a related issue: it is Sunnah to recite specific surahs in the Fajr prayer (Surah al-Kafirun and Surah al-Ikhlas). However, constant repetition (mudawamah) of these surahs might be disliked if it leads to abandoning other surahs. The author cites Ghayat al-Bayan that constant repetition of the three surahs (Qul Huwa Allah, Qul A'udhu bi Rabb al-Falaq, Qul A'udhu bi Rabb al-Nas) in Witr is disliked, regardless of whether one is imam or alone, in Ramadan or not. The cause ('illa) is either confusion of specification (that one might think these surahs are obligatory) or abandonment of other surahs. The latter cause always applies, so constancy is disliked absolutely. The text then returns to the matn: if the imam recites a verse of targhib or tarhib, the follower does not ask for Paradise or seek refuge; he simply listens. The imam in obligatory prayer does not do so either, but in supererogatory prayer (nafl), the one praying alone may ask and seek refuge based on the practice of the Prophet ﷺ reported in Hadith of Hudhayfah. However, the imam leading a congregation in nafl (e.g., taraweeh, eclipse) should not do so because it prolongs the prayer for the followers, unless the followers desire it. Gathering for nafl prayer other than taraweeh and eclipse is disliked.

Key Terms
ترغيب (targhīb): Encouragement or motivation towards good deeds; verses mentioning Paradise or mercy.
ترهيب (tarhīb): Warning or deterrence from evil; verses mentioning Hellfire or punishment.
مواظبة (muwāẓabah): Constancy or continuous repetition of a particular act, here reciting the same surahs regularly.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on constantly reciting the same three surahs (Qul Huwa Allah, Qul A'udhu bi Rabb al-Falaq, Qul A'udhu bi Rabb al-Nas) in Witr prayer?
A) It is Sunnah to do so every night.
B) It is mandatory (wajib).
C) It is disliked (makruh) because it leads to abandoning other surahs.
D) It is prohibited (haram) because it confuses the people.

Key Takeaway
Constant repetition of specific surahs is makruh tanzihi; followers must remain silent during targhib/tarhib verses, and imams may engage in such recitation only in supererogatory prayers when followers desire it.

The Follower's Recitation Behind the Imam in Audible Prayers
Commentary on the ruling that a follower must not recite behind the imam in audible prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on recitation behind the imam in audible prayers and identify the primary Quranic proof and its application.

Core Idea
The follower must remain silent; recitation behind the imam invalidates the prayer.

In this lesson, we examine a key ruling from the Hanafi school regarding the follower's recitation (qira'ah) when praying behind an imam in audible prayers (jahriyyah). The passage clarifies the relied-upon position, the evidence from the Quran, and the reasoning behind why the ruling is classified as prohibitory dislike (karahah tahrimiyyah) rather than absolute prohibition (haram). We also explore the adab (etiquette) of not supplicating when the imam recites verses of mercy or punishment.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
First, recognize that the act in question is the follower (mu'tamm) reciting Quran (or any words) behind the imam during an audible prayer. The Hanafi ruling is that this is not permissible and invalidates the prayer if done intentionally.
The ruling applies to all audible prayers (Fajr, Maghrib, Isha, and Jumu'ah).
2
Locate the Primary Dalil
The main evidence is the Quranic verse 7:204: 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent that you may receive mercy.' The commentator explains that this verse was revealed concerning prayer, according to the majority of exegetes.
The command to 'listen' (istimā') and 'be silent' (insāt) is imperative, and in Hanafi usul, al-amr yufīdu al-wujūb (the imperative indicates obligation).
3
Trace the Wajh al-Dalalah (How the Dalil Proves the Ruling)
The verse commands two actions: listening and silence. These are obligatory. Since the follower is already hearing the imam's recitation, silence becomes the required response. Any recitation by the follower would violate this command, thus invalidating the prayer.
The principle of 'ibrah bi-umum al-lafz (consideration of the general wording) extends the ruling to recitation outside prayer as well, though the context is prayer.
4
Note the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
There is a weak narration attributed to Imam Muhammad al-Shaybani that the follower may recite in silent prayers. However, this report is considered weak (da'if), and the relied-upon position (muftā bihi) is the view of Abu Hanifa that recitation is prohibited in all prayers.
Even in silent prayers, the preferred view is to remain silent, as precaution is to act upon the stronger evidence.
5
Understand the Adab Concerning Verses of Targhib and Tarhib
When the imam recites a verse mentioning paradise or mercy (āyat al-targhib) or a verse about punishment (āyat al-tarhib), the follower should not supplicate for paradise or seek refuge from the fire, as this would distract from the obligation of listening. The follower remains silent and listens attentively.
This is based on the principle that the promise of mercy for listening is certain, whereas the answer to supplication is not guaranteed, especially when it distracts from hearing the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

كقولهما. والمراد من الكراهة كراهة التحريم وفي بعض العبارات أنها لا تحل خلفه وإنما لم يطلقوا اسم الحرمة عليها لما عرف من أن أصلهم أنهم لا يطلقونها إلا إذا كان الدليل قطعياً، ودعوى الاحتياط في القراءة خلفه ممنوعة بل الاحتياط تركها لأنه العمل بأقوى الدليلين، وقد روي عن عدة من الصحابة فساد الصلاة بالقراءة خلفه فأقواهما المنع. وأشار بقوله «بل يستمع وينصت إلى آخره إلى أن الآية نزلت في الصلاة وهي قوله «صلى» وحينئذ فلفظ المؤتم حقيقة بالنسبة إلى قوله وإن قرأ آية الترغيب والترهيب» مجاز باعتبار ما يؤول بالنسبة إلى الخطبة والصلاة، ويجوز الجمع بين الحقيقة والمجاز بلفظ واحد عند كثير من العلماء، وبهذا اندفع ما ذكره الشارح من الخلل في عبارة المختصر . واستثنى المصنف في الكافي من قوله صلى ما إذا ذكر الخطيب آية إن الله وملائكته ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٥٦] فإن السامع يصلي في نفسه سراً ائتماراً للأمر وجعل البعيد كالقريب للخطيب في أنه يسكت هو الاحتياط كما في الهداية والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم. فيلحقها التخصيص ثانياً بخلاف الثانية. قوله : ( عند كثير من العلماء) أي فيكون مبنياً على ما قالوه وإن كان مخالفاً لمذهبه من عدم جواز الجمع رعاية للاختصار والأصوب أن يقال: إنه جارٍ على مذهبنا أيضاً بناء على ما اختاره صاحب الهداية وغيره من جواز الجمع بينهما في سياق النفي وما هنا كذلك، ويمكن أن يكون ذلك مراد صاحب البحر. قوله : وبهذا) اندفع ما ذكره الشارح الخ) وذلك حيث قال: وقوله في المختصر أو خطب الخ ) ظاهر معطوف على قرأ» من قوله «وإن قرأ آية الترغيب والترهيب فلا يستقيم في المعنى لأنه يقتضي أن يكون الإنصات واجباً قبل الخطبة فيصير معنى الكلام يجب عليه الإنصات فيها وإن قرأ آية الترغيب أو الترهيب أو خطب، وأيضاً يقتضي أن تكون الخطبة والصلاة على النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام واقعين في نفس الصلاة وليس المراد ذلك، وإنما المراد أن ينصتوا إذا خطب وإن صلى على النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم اهـ. قال في النهر : وأجاب العيني بأن فاعل قرأ» هو الإمام وخطب هو الخطيب وهو في حالة الخطبة غير الإمام فيكون من عطف الجمل. ولا يلزم ما ذكر وأجاب منلاخسرو بأن المؤتم بمعنى من شأنه أن يأتم، وقوله «أو خطب» عطف على «قرأ» المحذوف والمعنى لا يقرأ المؤتم إذا قرأ إمامه بل يستمع وينصت وإن قرأ آية ترغيب أو ترهيب، ولا يقرأ المؤتم إذا خطب إمامه أو صلى على النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم بل يستمع وينصت وإن قرأ آية ترغيب أو ترهيب وأنت خبير بأن ما قاله العيني إنما يتم على التجوز في المؤتم ويلزم على ما قاله خسرو التجوز في الإمام أيضاً وتقييد منع المؤتم عن القراءة بما إذا خطب مع أ ممنوع بمجرد خروجه للخطبة اهـ كلام النهر وأجاب ابن كمال باشا عن اعتراض الزيلعي بأنه لما كانت الخطبة قائمة مقام ركعتي الظهر نزل من حضرها منزلة المؤتم فلا دلالة في أو صلى على النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ، على أن تكون الخطبة والصلاة على النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم واقعتين في نفس الصلاة، ولا اتجاه لما قيل أنه يقتضي أن يكون الإنصات واجباً قبل الخطبة لانعدام التنزيل المذكور اهـ. قوله : (واستثنى المصنف في الكافي الخ قال في النهر إلا أن إطلاقه يقتضي عدمه. قال في الفتح: وهو الأشبه. ورد كلامه أنه لو كتب حالة الخطبة كره أيضاً وهو الأصح كما في السراج . والحاصل أنه لا يأتي بما يفوت به الاستماع فلا يشمت عاطساً ولا يرد سلاماً . فتدبر
Book of Prayer - Section on Description of Prayer: In it and in what is not recited aloud. He said: And we adopt this, and it is the statement of Abu Hanifa. It is answered that the author of al-Hidayah did not confirm that it is the statement of Muhammad; rather its apparent meaning is that it is a weak narration. In Fath al-Qadir: The truth is that Muhammad's statement is like theirs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad). The intended meaning of 'disliked' is prohibition (karahah tahrimiyyah), and in some expressions they said it is not permissible behind him, but they did not use the term 'prohibited' because their principle is that they only use it when the evidence is definitive. The claim that precaution is in reciting behind him is refuted; rather precaution is to leave it because it is acting upon the stronger of the two evidences. It has been narrated from several companions that prayer is invalidated by reciting behind him, so the stronger of the two is prohibition. He indicated by his statement 'rather he listens and remains silent to the end' that the verse was revealed concerning prayer, which is His statement (Exalted): 'And when the Quran is recited, listen to it and be silent that you may receive mercy' [al-A'raf 7:204], and it is the statement of most exegetes. Among them are those who said it was revealed concerning the sermon. Al-Kafi said: There is no contradiction between them; for they were commanded both in it due to the recitation of the Quran in it. The conclusion of the verse is that it requires two things: listening and silence, so each is acted upon. The first is specific to audible prayers, and the second is not, so it applies absolutely, so silence is obligatory during recitation absolutely. Since consideration is for the generality of the wording, not the specificity of the cause, listening to the recitation of the Quran outside of prayer is also obligatory. For this reason, al-Khulasah said: A man is writing fiqh and next to him a man reciting the Quran and he cannot listen to the Quran, then the sin is on the reciter. Similarly, if one recites loudly on the roof at night while people are sleeping, he sins. In al-Qunyah and others: A child who is reciting Quran and his family is busy with work not listening—if they started working before his recitation, they do not sin; otherwise they sin. And his statement 'and if' is for connection. An 'ayah of encouragement' is that in which paradise or mercy is mentioned; an 'ayah of discouragement' is that in which the fire is mentioned. And 'discouragement' means frightening. In his expression there is observance of etiquette where he said 'listens and is silent' and did not say 'does not ask for paradise or seek refuge from the fire'. He did not ask and seek refuge because it would violate the obligation of listening, and because Allah has promised him mercy if he listens and is silent, and His promise is certain, while answering supplication is not certain, especially when preoccupied from hearing the Quran with supplication. The pronoun in his statement 'recited' refers to the imam, and likewise in 'delivered a sermon' and 'prayed'. Thus the word 'follower' is literal with respect to his statement 'and if he recites an ayah of encouragement or discouragement' and metaphorical with respect to what devolves upon the sermon and prayer. And combining literal and metaphorical in one word is permitted according to many scholars. By this, what the commentator mentioned of defect in the expression of al-Mukhtasar is repelled. And the author in al-Kafi made an exception from his statement 'prayed' for when the khatib mentions the ayah 'Indeed Allah and His angels...' [al-Ahzab 56], then the listener prays in himself secretly, acting upon the command, and making the distant like the near to the khatib in that he is silent—this is precaution as in al-Hidayah, and Allah knows best. Then the specification attaches to it secondly unlike the second. His statement: 'according to many scholars' i.e. it is built upon what they said, even if it contradicts his (the author's) madhhab of not permitting combination, in consideration of brevity. The more correct is to say it proceeds on our madhhab as well, based on what the author of al-Hidayah and others chose of permitting combination between them in the context of negation, and this is like that. It is possible that this is the intent of the author of al-Bahr. His statement: 'and by this is repelled what the commentator mentioned' i.e. where he said: His statement in al-Mukhtasar 'or delivered a sermon etc.' apparently is conjuncted to 'recited' from his statement 'and if he recites an ayah of encouragement and discouragement' so it is not correct in meaning because it necessitates that silence be obligatory before the sermon, so the meaning becomes: silence is obligatory upon him in it even if he recites an ayah of encouragement or discouragement or delivers a sermon. Also it necessitates that the sermon and praying upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) be occurring within the prayer itself, and that is not intended. Rather the intention is that they should be silent when he delivers a sermon even if he prays upon the Prophet (peace be upon him) end. Al-Nahr said: Al-Ayni answered that the subject of 'recited' is the imam, and 'delivered a sermon' is the khatib, and he in the state of the sermon is not the imam, so it is from the conjunction of sentences. And it does not necessitate what was mentioned. And Mulla Khusraw answered that 'follower' means one who is apt to follow, and his statement 'or delivered a sermon' is conjuncted to the omitted 'recited', and the meaning: the follower does not recite when his imam recites, but rather listens and is silent, even if he recites an ayah of encouragement or discouragement; and the follower does not recite when his imam delivers a sermon or prays upon the Prophet (peace be upon him), but rather listens and is silent even if he recites an ayah of encouragement or discouragement. And you are aware that what al-Ayni said is only complete with metaphorical use of 'follower', and what Khusraw said necessitates metaphorical use of 'imam' as well, and restricting the prohibition of the follower's recitation to when he delivers a sermon with 'and' is prevented by his mere exiting for the sermon end of al-Nahr's speech. And Ibn Kamal Pasha answered the objection of al-Zayla'i that since the sermon stands in place of the two rak'ahs of Dhuhr, those present are considered as followers, so there is no indication in 'or prays upon the Prophet (peace be upon him)' that the sermon and praying upon the Prophet are occurring within the prayer itself, and there is no direction for what is said that it necessitates that silence be obligatory before the sermon due to the absence of the mentioned analogy end. His statement: 'and the author in al-Kafi made an exception etc.' al-Nahr said: But its absolute expression implies its non-existence. Al-Fath said: It is more similar. And his statement was refuted: if he writes during the sermon, it is also disliked, and it is the most correct as in al-Siraj. The conclusion: he should not do anything that wastes listening, so he should not respond to a sneeze nor return a greeting. So reflect.
Source pages p. 600

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) on the ruling regarding the follower's recitation behind the imam in audible prayers. The base text (matn) states that the follower must listen and remain silent. The commentator clarifies the relied-upon position (mufta bihi) is Abu Hanifa's view, which prohibits recitation. He then addresses an intra-Hanafi dispute: there is a narration that Muhammad al-Shaybani allowed recitation in silent prayers, but this is deemed weak by the author of al-Hidayah. The commentator explains why the ruling is called 'disliked' (makruh) rather than 'prohibited' (haram): because the evidence for prohibition is not definitive (qat'i). Nevertheless, precaution is to abstain from recitation. The primary proof is the Qur'anic verse (7:204) which commands listening and silence. The verse is interpreted to apply to prayer, and by the principle of general wording ('ibrah bi'umum al-lafz), it also applies outside prayer. The commentator then discusses the exception for verses of mercy and punishment: if the imam recites such verses, the follower should not supplicate or seek refuge because it distracts from the obligatory listening. This is a matter of adab. The passage also tackles a grammatical issue in the matn regarding the conjunction 'or' and how to reconcile literal and metaphorical meanings. Finally, the commentator mentions that during the sermon, one should not even respond to a sneeze or return a greeting, to maintain attention to the Khutbah.

Key Terms
آية الترغيب (ayat al-targhib): A verse in which paradise or mercy is mentioned, encouraging the listener to seek reward.
آية الترهيب (ayat al-tarhib): A verse in which the fire or punishment is mentioned, warning the listener.
المؤتم (al-mu'tamm): The person following the imam in prayer; the follower.
الإنصات (al-insat): Silence and attentiveness; it is the required state when the imam recites.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
When the imam recites an ayah of mercy (آية الترغيب) during audible prayer, what should the follower do?
A) Supplicate for paradise
B) Remain silent and listen
C) Recite the same ayah silently
D) Seek refuge from the fire

Key Takeaway
The follower must remain silent and listen during the imam's audible recitation; recitation invalidates the prayer, and this ruling is derived from the Quranic command to be silent.

Responding Silently When the Imam Recites a Verse of Blessing
Analyzes whether listeners silently send blessings when the imam recites a verse of blessings during khutbah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on audibly sending blessings during the Friday khutbah and identify the proof and the exceptions.

Core Idea
During the khutbah, the obligation to listen overrides the command to send blessings aloud.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common scenario: the imam recites a verse commanding blessings on the Prophet (Al-Ahzab 33:56) while delivering the Friday khutbah. Should the listener respond audibly? The Hanafi school maintains that the silence required during the khutbah takes precedence, and any verbal response, even blessings, is prohibited. This lesson unpacks the proof from the Quran and the reasoning of later Hanafi authorities.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what action is being ruled upon (audible vocalization of blessings during khutbah) and its legal classification (makruh tahrimi).
The ruling applies to the listener, not the khatib.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the primary evidence: the Qur'anic command to send blessings (Al-Ahzab 33:56) and the obligation of attentive silence (based on other hadith).
The command to send blessings is overridden by the higher obligation of listening.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
Explain how the command is interpreted: the imperative 'sallu' is general, but it is restricted by the context of khutbah, making silent internal fulfillment sufficient.
The Hanafi principle of takhsis (specification) is at work.
4
Note the ikhtilaf and responses
Review objections raised by earlier scholars (e.g., al-Zayla'i) and how later commentators (al-Ayni, Mulla Khusraw, Ibn Kamal Pasha) defended the ruling.
The ikhtilaf is internal (within Hanafi commentaries) and external (with Shafi'is).
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Conclude that the relied-upon position is complete silence; even writing is disliked, and the listener should not respond to a sneeze or greeting.
The ruling is based on istihsan and the need to preserve the sanctity of the khutbah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
المصنف في الكافي من قوله صلى ما إذا ذكر الخطيب آية إن الله وملائكته ﴾ [الأحزاب: ٥٦] فإن السامع يصلي في نفسه سراً ائتماراً للأمر وجعل البعيد كالقريب للخطيب في أنه يسكت هو الاحتياط كما في الهداية والله سبحانه وتعالى أعلم.
:
الترغيب والترهيب فلا يستقيم في المعنى لأنه يقتضي أن يكون الإنصات واجباً قبل الخطبة فيصير معنى الكلام يجب عليه الإنصات فيها وإن قرأ آية الترغيب أو الترهيب أو خطب، وأيضاً يقتضي أن تكون الخطبة والصلاة على النبي عليه الصلاة والسلام واقعين في نفس الصلاة وليس المراد ذلك، وإنما المراد أن ينصتوا إذا خطب وإن صلى على النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم اهـ. قال في النهر : وأجاب العيني بأن فاعل قرأ» هو الإمام وخطب هو الخطيب وهو في حالة الخطبة غير الإمام فيكون من عطف الجمل.
أنه
ولا يلزم ما ذكر وأجاب منلاخسرو بأن المؤتم بمعنى من شأنه أن يأتم، وقوله «أو خطب» عطف على «قرأ» المحذوف والمعنى لا يقرأ المؤتم إذا قرأ إمامه بل يستمع وينصت وإن قرأ آية ترغيب أو ترهيب، ولا يقرأ المؤتم إذا خطب إمامه أو صلى على النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم بل يستمع وينصت وإن قرأ آية ترغيب أو ترهيب وأنت خبير بأن ما قاله العيني إنما يتم على التجوز في المؤتم ويلزم على ما قاله خسرو التجوز في الإمام أيضاً وتقييد منع المؤتم عن القراءة بما إذا خطب مع أ ممنوع بمجرد خروجه للخطبة اهـ كلام النهر وأجاب ابن كمال باشا عن اعتراض الزيلعي بأنه لما كانت الخطبة قائمة مقام ركعتي الظهر نزل من حضرها منزلة المؤتم فلا دلالة في أو صلى على النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم ، على أن تكون الخطبة والصلاة على النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم واقعتين في نفس الصلاة، ولا اتجاه لما قيل أنه يقتضي أن يكون الإنصات واجباً قبل الخطبة لانعدام التنزيل المذكور اهـ. قوله : (واستثنى المصنف في الكافي الخ قال في النهر إلا أن إطلاقه يقتضي عدمه. قال في الفتح: وهو الأشبه. ورد كلامه أنه لو كتب حالة الخطبة كره أيضاً وهو الأصح كما في السراج . والحاصل أنه لا يأتي بما يفوت به الاستماع فلا يشمت عاطساً ولا يرد سلاما .
فتدبر
The author in al-Kafi said: 'His saying: (He sent blessings) when the khatib mentions a verse: 'Indeed Allah and His angels...' [Al-Ahzab: 56], then the listener sends blessings in his heart secretly, acting on the command, and considering the distant person as close to the khatib in that he remains silent is precautionary, as in al-Hidayah. And Allah Most High knows best.'
:
(Then discussion of) encouragement and warning: it is not sound in meaning because it would imply that silence is obligatory before the khutbah, so the meaning becomes: he must be silent during it even if he recites a verse of encouragement or warning or delivers a khutbah. Also it would imply that the khutbah and sending blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) occur within the prayer itself, which is not intended. Rather the intent is that they be silent when he delivers a khutbah, and even if he sends blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him) — end quote. He said in al-Nahr: Al-Ayni answered that the subject of 'recites' is the imam, and 'delivers a khutbah' is the khatib, and he is not the imam during the khutbah, so it is a conjunction of sentences. It does not necessitate what was mentioned. And Mulla Khusraw answered that 'the follower' means one who is meant to follow, and his saying 'or delivers a khutbah' is an conjunction to the omitted 'recites', meaning: the follower does not recite when his imam recites, but rather listens and is silent, even if he recites a verse of encouragement or warning; and the follower does not recite when his imam delivers a khutbah or sends blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him), but rather listens and is silent, even if he recites a verse of encouragement or warning. And you are aware that what al-Ayni said is only valid based on a metaphor in 'follower', and what Khusraw said requires a metaphor in 'imam' as well. And the restriction of preventing the follower from reciting only when he delivers a khutbah is rejected by the mere fact of his leaving for the khutbah — end quote from al-Nahr. And Ibn Kamal Pasha answered the objection of al-Zayla'i by saying: Since the khutbah stands in place of the two rak'ahs of zuhr, those who attend it are considered as followers, so there is no indication in 'or sends blessings on the Prophet (peace be upon him)' that the khutbah and sending blessings occur within the prayer itself. And there is no merit to what was said that it would imply that silence is obligatory before the khutbah, due to the absence of the aforementioned analogy — end quote. His saying: (And the author in al-Kafi made an exception...). He said in al-Nahr: But its absolute expression implies its absence. He said in al-Fath: And it is more appropriate. And his statement is rejected because if he writes during the khutbah it is also disliked, and that is the most correct as in al-Siraj. The gist is: he should not do anything that causes him to miss listening, so he does not respond to a sneeze nor returns a greeting. Reflect.
Source pages p. 601

Commentary
This passage is an expansion probe from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, analyzing a specific ruling within the chapter of Imamah: what should a listener do when the imam, during the Friday khutbah, recites a verse that mentions sending blessings on the Prophet (e.g., Al-Ahzab 33:56). The text begins by quoting the author of Al-Kafi, who rules that the listener should send blessings silently in his heart, acting on the Qur'anic command, but he should not do so audibly because he is obligated to listen attentively. The author then addresses objections that this would conflict with the obligation of silence. Al-Ayni and Mulla Khusraw offer grammatical and contextual solutions: the imam reciting is not the same as the khatib delivering the khutbah; 'follower' here is metaphorical. Ibn Kamal Pasha strengthens this by noting that the khutbah replaces two rak'ahs, so the listener is like a follower. The passage concludes with a general principle: the listener should avoid anything that distracts from listening, such as responding to a sneeze or returning a greeting. This is a Hanafi ruling based on istihsan and the need to preserve the sanctity of the khutbah.

Key Terms
الخطبة (al-khutbah): The sermon delivered by the khatib during Friday prayer and Eid prayers; listening to it is obligatory.
الإنصات (al-insaat): Attentive silence; the listener must refrain from any speech or movement that distracts from the khutbah.
الصلاة على النبي (al-salat 'ala al-nabi): Verbal blessing upon the Prophet Muhammad (e.g., 'Allahumma salli 'ala Muhammad'); during khutbah it should be done silently in the heart.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what should a listener do when the imam recites the verse about sending blessings (Al-Ahzab 33:56) during the Friday khutbah?
A) Recite the blessings aloud to respond to the Qur'anic command
B) Remain silent and send blessings only in his heart
C) Raise his hands and say 'Allahumma salli' loudly
D) Repeat the entire verse after the imam

Key Takeaway
The listener must remain completely silent during the khutbah, only sending blessings internally.

Ruling on Congregational Prayer and Conditions for Following the Imam
Ruling definition with conditions list

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer and list the ten conditions for valid following (qudwa) and six conditions for the imam.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah; its validity depends on ten conditions for the follower and six for the imam.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq lays out the foundational rules for forming a valid congregation. It clarifies the legal status of congregational prayer in the Hanafi school and details the precise conditions that must be met for the follower's prayer to be connected to the imam's. Understanding these conditions ensures your prayer is correct and any deficiency is avoided.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling of congregation
Locate where the text states the ruling: 'الجماعة سنة مؤكدة' (congregation is a confirmed sunnah). Note the intra-Hanafi variation: some scholars consider it wajib.
The relied-upon position is sunnah mu'akkadah; missing it without excuse is sinful.
2
List the ten conditions for the follower
Go through each of the ten shurut al-qudwa mentioned in the text. Understand the rationale behind each, e.g., 'follower behind' ensures the imam's leadership.
These conditions are for validity; violating any invalidates the follower's prayer.
3
List the six conditions for the imam
From the Sharnblali quote, identify the six conditions: Islam, puberty, intellect, masculinity, recitation, freedom from excuses.
These are prerequisites for someone to lead, not for the follower's validity directly.
4
Recognize the distinction between qudwa and imamah
The conditions for the follower (qudwa) are more detailed and relate to the act of following; conditions for the imam are about the imam's personal eligibility.
Both sets must be satisfied for a valid congregation.
5
Summarize the ikhtilaf
Note the difference between the matn's 'sunnah' and the view of some Hanafis that it is wajib. This is an intra-madhhab ikhtilaf.
The mufta bihi is sunnah mu'akkadah.

باب الإمامة
وهي صغرى وكبرى. فالصغرى اقتداء الغير بالمصلي، والكبرى استحقاق تصرف عام كما في السير. واعلم أن شرائط القدوة مفصلة : الأولى أن لا يتقدم المأموم على إمامه مع اتحاد الجهة، فإن تقدم مع اختلافها كالتحلق حول الكعبة صح الثاني علمه بانتقالات إمامه برؤية أو سماع، فإن كان بينهما حائل يشتبه عليه انتقالاته لم يصح الثالث اتحاد موقفهما فإن اختلف كما إذا كان بينهما نهر أو طريق لم يصح والمسجد مكان واحد وإن تباعد وفناؤه ملحق به الرابع نية المأموم الاقتداء مقارنة لتكبيرة الافتتاح فإن تأخرت عنه لم يصح. الخامس أن لا يكون حال الإمام أدنى من حال المأموم في الشرائط والأركان فإن استويا أو كان حال الإمام أعلى صح ويعاد عند قوله وفسد الخ». السادس مشاركة الإمام في الأركان، فإن سبقه المأموم بركن ولم يشاركه إمامه فيه لم يصح ذلك. السابع عدم محاذاة امرأة له إن نوى إمامه إمامتها الثامن علمه بحال إمامه من إقامة وسفر فلو اقتدى بإمام لا يعلم أنه مقيم أو مسافر لم تصح التاسع أن يكون بحال يصح له الدخول بنية إمامه فلا يجوز بناء فرض على فرض آخر . العاشر صحة صلاة إمامه اهـ . كذا في هامش النسخ المصححة معزواً إلى خط المؤلف في كتابه . قلت : وبقي شروط الإمامة وقد عدها الشرنبلالي في نور الإيضاح فقال : وشروط الإمامة للرجال الأصحاء ستة أشياء : الإسلام والبلوغ والعقل والذكورة والقراءة والسلامة من الأعذار كالرعاف والفافأة والتمتمة واللثغ وفقد شرط كطهارة وستر عورة اهـ. وقد نظمت شروط القدوة والإمامة الستة عشر بقولي :
أخي إن ترم إدراك شرط لقدوة فذلك عشر قد أتاك معددا تأخر مـؤتـم وعـلـم انـتـقـال مـن به انتم مع كون المكــانـيـن واحـدا وكون إمام ليس دون تبيعه بشرط وأركان ونية الاقتدا مشاركة في كل ركن وعلمه بحال إمام حل أم ســار مـبـعـدا وإن لا تحاذيـه الـتـي مـعـه اقـتـدت وصحة ما صلى الإمـام مـن ابـتـدا كذاك اتحاد الفرض هذا تمامها وست شروط للإمـامـة فـي المدى بلوغ وإسلام وعقل ذكورة قراءة مجز وانـتـفـا مـانـع اقـتـدا والله تعالى أعلم. قوله : (وذكر هو وغير الخ) قال في النهر : وفي المفيد الجماعة واجبة وسنة
Chapter of Imamah
It is minor and major. The minor is the following of another by the one praying, and the major is entitlement to general disposition as in al-Siyar. Know that the conditions of following are detailed: First: The follower should not step ahead of his imam when they are in the same direction; if he steps ahead when they differ (like circling around the Ka'bah) it is valid. Second: His knowledge of the imam's movements by sight or hearing; if there is a barrier that confuses his knowledge of the movements, it is not valid. Third: Unity of their standing place; if they differ, such as if there is a river or road between them, it is not valid; the mosque is one place even if far apart, and its courtyard is annexed to it. Fourth: The follower's intention of following should be concurrent with the opening takbir; if it comes after it, it is not valid. Fifth: The imam's state should not be inferior to the follower's state in conditions and pillars; if they are equal or the imam's state is higher, it is valid, and there is a repetition at his statement 'and following a man by a woman is invalidated'. Sixth: Partnership of the imam in the pillars; if the follower precedes the imam in a pillar and the imam does not join him in it, that is not valid. Seventh: Absence of a woman aligning with him if the imam intends her imamah. Eighth: His knowledge of the imam's state of residence or travel; if he follows an imam not knowing whether he is resident or traveler, it is not valid. Ninth: That he be in a state that makes it valid for him to enter with the intention of his imam; it is not permissible to build one obligatory prayer upon another. Tenth: The validity of the imam's prayer — end. Thus in the margin of corrected copies attributed to the author's handwriting in his book. I say: The conditions of imamah remain, and al-Sharnblali counted them in Nur al-Idah, saying: The conditions of imamah for healthy men are six things: Islam, puberty, intellect, masculinity, recitation, and freedom from excuses such as nosebleed, stammer, stutter, lisp, and lack of a condition like purity and covering of private parts — end. And I have versified the sixteen conditions of following and imamah in my saying:
O brother, if you seek to grasp a condition of following, there are ten already enumerated: that the follower be behind, knowledge of movements, being with him, that the two places be one, that the imam not be inferior in condition and pillars, intention of following, partnership in every pillar, knowledge of the imam's state whether halal or travel far away, and that the woman with him not be in line when he follows, and the validity of what the imam prayed from the beginning; likewise unity of the obligatory prayer — this completes them. And six conditions for imamah in scope: puberty, Islam, intellect, masculinity, sufficient recitation, and absence of preventing things for following. And Allah Most High knows best. His saying: (And he and others mentioned...). He said in al-Nahr: In al-Mufid, the congregation is obligatory and a sunnah.
Source pages p. 601

Commentary
This passage is a definition ruling from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq's commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq, detailing the ruling on congregational prayer and the conditions for its validity. It opens by defining Imamah in two senses: minor (actual following in prayer) and major (general authority). It then lists ten conditions for the follower (shurut al-qudwa) and six conditions for the imam (shurut al-imamah). These conditions are essential for the validity of the follower's prayer; if any are missing, the prayer is invalid or deficient. The text also includes a poetic summary (nazm) of all sixteen conditions for memorization. The passage ends with a citation from al-Nahr noting a variation in terminology: while the matn says 'sunnah mu'akkadah', some works call it obligatory (wajib). This reflects an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the legal weight of congregational prayer: the majority of later Hanafi scholars (mutakhkhirin) considered it wajib, but the relied-upon position (mu'tamad) remains sunnah mu'akkadah, meaning it is not fard but is strongly recommended and sinful to abandon without excuse. The conditions themselves are practical: the follower must not be ahead of the imam, must know the imam's movements, must be in the same place (or connected), must intend to follow at the takbir, the imam must not be inferior, the follower must not precede the imam in a pillar, no woman aligned with him if she is being led, knowledge of the imam's travel status, the follower's prayer must be of the same type (not supererogatory behind obligatory), and the imam's own prayer must be valid. The imam's conditions are basic: Islam, puberty, sanity, maleness, ability to recite correctly, and freedom from physical defects that affect recitation or movements. This comprehensive list is typical of Hanafi fiqh texts and serves as a practical guide for forming a valid congregation.

Key Terms
القدوة (al-qudwa): The act of following the imam in prayer; the conditions for its validity are detailed.
الإمامة الصغرى (al-imamah al-sughra): Minor imamah: leading others in prayer; the focus of this chapter.
ائتلاف الموقف (i'tilaf al-mawqif): Unity of standing place; the follower and imam must be in the same place or connected.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as stated in this passage, what is the minimum number of conditions for a valid follower (qudwa)?
A) Five
B) Ten
C) Six
D) Sixteen

Key Takeaway
Congregational prayer is sunnah mu'akkadah; its validity depends on ten conditions for the follower and six for the imam, all of which must be observed.

The Ruling on Congregational Prayer: Wajib or Sunnah Mu'akkadah?
Commentary expanding a matn statement on congregational prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the preponderant Hanafi ruling on congregational prayer, explain the intra-madhhab terminological dispute, and identify the legal consequences (ta'zir, rejection of testimony) that follow from the wajib position.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school — confirmed sunnah and wajib are practically equivalent for the rituals of Islam.

In this passage, Ibn Nujaym in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq unpacks the ruling on jama'ah found in Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The matn calls it a 'confirmed sunnah', but the commentary reveals that the majority of Hanafi scholars deem it wajib (obligatory). We will explore the evidence, the intra-Hanafi terminological dispute, and the concrete legal consequences such as ta'zir and rejection of testimony.

Guided Path
1
Identify the matn statement
The base text (Kanz al-Daqa'iq) states 'al-jama'ah sunnah mu'akkadah'. Understand what this phrase literally means: a confirmed Sunnah, something the Prophet consistently did.
Sunnah mu'akkadah is a rank just below wajib in Hanafi terminology.
2
Analyze the commentary's expansion
Ibn Nujaym immediately clarifies that the preponderant view (al-rajih) in the Hanafi school is wujub (obligation). He cites al-Bada'i' that this is from 'amma' (the generality) of our scholars. Note that he distinguishes between the verbal formulation and the actual legal force.
The commentary uses sources like al-Muhit, al-Qunyah, and al-Mujtaba to support the obligation.
3
Examine the evidence for obligation
List the proofs mentioned: (1) The Prophet's continuous practice without omission. (2) Severe warnings in hadith (e.g., 'Whoever does not attend...'). (3) Legal consequences: ta'zir (discretionary punishment) for leaving without excuse, rejection of testimony, and the responsibility of neighbors to enjoin. (4) The hadith of 27-fold superiority, combined with the above, indicates obligation.
The hadith of superiority alone is zanni; the cumulative evidence raises it to wujub.
4
Reconcile the terminological difference
Ibn Nujaym explains that those who call it sunnah mu'akkadah are not contradicting the wajib position in practice. Confirmed sunnah in matters of sha'a'ir (rituals) is treated as wajib. The obligation is specifically for habitual abandonment; occasional absence due to valid excuse or interpretation does not incur sin.
The reconciliation: constant attendance is sunnah mu'akkadah, but one must attend 'occasionally' as a wajib; habitually leaving is sinful.
5
Apply the mufta bihi position
The operative ruling is wajib. For fatwa, this means a man without excuse must attend jama'ah; if he habitually leaves, he is subject to ta'zir and his testimony is rejected. Exceptions: leaving due to forgetfulness or valid interpretation (e.g., the imam is from a deviant sect) does not incur these consequences.
The source also notes that leaving out of disdain (istikhfaf) leads to disbelief, not just sin.

قوله : (الجماعة سنة مؤكدة أي قوية تشبه الواجب في القوة. والراجح عند أهل المذهب الوجوب ونقله في البدائع عن عامة مشايخنا، وذكر هو وغيره أن القائل منهم أنها سنة مؤكدة ليس مخالفاً في الحقيقة بل في العبارة لأن السنة المؤكدة والواجب سواء خصوصاً ما كان من شعائر الإسلام ودليله من السنة المواظبة من غير ترك مع النكير على تاركها بغير أحاديث كثيرة. وفي للمجتبى والظاهر أنهم أرادوا بالتأكيد الوجوب لاستدلالهم بالأخبار الواردة بالوعيد الشديد بترك الجماعة. وصرح في المحيط بأنه لا يرخص لأحد في تركها بغير عذر حتى لو تركها أهل مصر يؤمرون بها فإن ائتمروا وإلا يحل مقاتلتهم، وفي القنية وغيرها : بأنه يجب التعزير على تاركها بغير عذر ويأثم الجيران بالسكوت. وفيها : لو انتظر الإقامة لدخول المسجد فهو مسيء. وفي المجتبى : ومن سمع النداء كره له الاشتغال بالعمل. وعن عائشة أنه حرام يعني حالة الأذان وإن عمل بعده قبل الصلاة فلا بأس به. وعن محمد : لا بأس بالإسراع إلى الجمعة والجماعة ما لم يجهد نفسه والسكينة أفضل فيها اهـ . وفي الخلاصة : يجوز التعزير بأخذ الماء ومن ذلك رجل لا يحضر الجماعة اهـ. وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى في محله أن معناه ماله عنه مدة ثم دفعه له لا أخذه على وجه التملك كما قد كما صرح به في البزازية وذكر في غاية البيان معزياً إلى الأجناس أن تارك الجماعة يتوهم يستوجب إساءة ولا تقبل شهادته إذا تركها استخفافاً بذلك ومجانة أما إذا تركها سهواً أو تركها بتأويل بأن يكون الإمام من أهل الأهواء أو مخالفاً لمذهب المقتدي لا يراعى مذهبه فلا يستوجب الإساءة وتقبل شهادته .اهـ. وفي شرح النقاية عن نجم الأئمة: رجل يشتغل
