على أن تركها بلا عذر يوجب إثماً مع أنه قول العراقيين والخراسانيون على أنه يأثم إذا اعتاد الترك كما في القنية اهـ. وفي شرح المنية للحلبي والأحكام تدل على الوجوب من أن تاركها من غير عذر يعزر وترد شهادته ويأثم الجيران بالسكوت عنه وهذه كلها أحكام الواجب وقد يوفق بأن ترتيب الوعيد في الحديث وهذه الأحكام مما يستدل به على الوجوب مقيد بالمداومة على الترك كما . قول عليه السلام لا يشهدون الصلاة وفي الحديث الآخر يصلون في بيوتهم، كما يعطيه ظاهر إسناد المضارع نحو بنو فلان يأكلون البر» أي عادتهم فيكون الواجب الحضور أحياناً، والسنة المؤكدة التي تقرب منه المواظبة عليها وحينئذ فلا منافاة بين ما تقدم وبين قوله عليه السلام صلاة الرجل في الجماعة تفضل على صلاته في بيته أو سوقه سبعاً وعشرين ضعفاً» (۱) اهـ. قوله : (إذا تركها استخفافاً) أي تهاوناً وتكاسلاً وليس المراد حقيقة الاستخفاف الذي هو الاحتقار فإنه كفر .
(۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الأذان باب ۳۰ ۳۱ الترمذي في كتاب المواقيت باب ٤٧. النسائي في كتاب الصلاة باب ۲۱ ابن ماجه في كتاب المساجد باب .١٦. الموطأ في كتاب الجماعة حديث ١. أحمد في مسنده (٣٧٦/۱، ٤٥٢) (١٠٢/٢، ١١٢).
His statement: (Congregational prayer is a confirmed sunnah) i.e. strong, resembling wajib in strength. And the preponderant view with the people of the madhhab is obligation, and it was transmitted in al-Bada'i' from the generality of our scholars. He and others mentioned that the one among them who says it is a confirmed sunnah is not opposed in reality but in expression, because the confirmed sunnah and the wajib are the same, especially what is from the rituals of Islam. Its evidence from the Sunnah is the continuous observance without abandonment, with censure upon its abandoner without excuse, supported by many hadiths. And in al-Mujtaba: the apparent is that they intended by 'confirmed' obligation, because they use as proof the reports of severe warning for leaving congregational prayer. And it is explicitly stated in al-Muhit that no one is permitted to leave it without an excuse, even if the people of a city leave it, they are commanded to do it; if they comply, otherwise it is permissible to fight them. And in al-Qunyah and others: it is obligatory to discipline (ta'zir) the one who leaves it without excuse, and the neighbors sin by remaining silent. And in it: if one waits for the iqamah to enter the mosque, he is doing wrong. And in al-Mujtaba: whoever hears the call, it is disliked for him to engage in work. And from Aisha: it is haram, meaning during the adhan, but if he works after it before the prayer, there is no harm. And from Muhammad: there is no harm in hurrying to Friday and congregational prayer as long as he does not exhaust himself, and calmness is better in that. In al-Khulasah: it is permissible to discipline by taking water, and among that is a man who does not attend congregational prayer. And it will come in its place, Allah willing, that its meaning is that he takes what he owes for a period then gives it to him, not taking it by way of ownership, as is explicitly stated in al-Bazzaziyyah. And it is mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan, attributed to al-Ajnas, that the abandoner of congregational prayer is considered to deserve misbehavior and his testimony is not accepted if he leaves it out of disdain and carelessness. But if he leaves it forgetfully or due to interpretation (e.g., the imam is from the people of desires or opposes the follower's madhhab, and does not consider his madhhab), then he does not deserve misbehavior and his testimony is accepted. In Sharh al-Niqayah from Najm al-A'immah: a man who occupies himself with repeating fiqh night and day and does not attend congregational prayer is not excused and his testimony is not accepted. And he also said: a man who occupies himself with [something unclear] ... the agreement is apparent for its obligation by the Sunnah, and this is the meaning of some saying it is called wajib and confirmed sunnah equally, except that this implies that leaving it without excuse incurs sin, and it is the saying of the Iraqis and Khurasanis that he sins if he habitually leaves it, as in al-Qunyah. In Sharh al-Munyah al-Halabi: the rulings indicate obligation, as the one who leaves it without excuse is disciplined (ta'zir), his testimony is rejected, and the neighbors sin by remaining silent about him. All these are rulings of the wajib. And it may be reconciled by saying that the threat in the hadith and these rulings, which indicate obligation, are restricted to persistent abandonment. As the Prophet's saying: 'They do not attend the prayer' and in another hadith: 'They pray in their homes', just as the apparent attribution of the present tense (e.g., 'Banu Fulan eat barley') indicates their custom. Thus the obligation is to attend occasionally, and the confirmed sunnah that is close to that is to be constant upon it. So there is no contradiction between the above and his saying (peace be upon him): 'A man's prayer in congregation is superior to his prayer in his house or market by twenty-seven degrees.' His statement: (if he leaves it out of disdain) i.e., laziness and neglect, and the intended meaning is not actual disdain which is contempt, for that is disbelief.
Source pages p. 602

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute on the legal status of congregational prayer (jama'ah) in the five daily prayers. The matn from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states 'al-jama'ah sunnah mu'akkadah', but the commentator (Ibn Nujaym) clarifies that the preponderant view among Hanafi scholars is that it is wajib (obligatory). He cites al-Bada'i' that the generality of our scholars hold it as wajib. Those who call it sunnah mu'akkadah are not really contradicting, because confirmed sunnah in matters of Islamic rituals (sha'a'ir) is equivalent to wajib in practice. The evidence for obligation includes: continuous practice of the Prophet without omission, censure on those who leave it, and severe warnings in hadith. The commentator then lists rulings that prove obligation: (1) In al-Muhit, it is not permitted to leave it without excuse; if an entire city leaves it, they are fought. (2) Ta'zir (disciplinary punishment) is applied to the one who leaves without excuse. (3) Neighbors sin by remaining silent. (4) Waiting for iqamah to enter the mosque is blameworthy. (5) Work is disliked after the adhan. (6) A narration from Aisha says it is haram during the adhan. (7) The testimony of one who habitually leaves out of disdain is rejected. (8) One who leaves due to interpretation (e.g., differing with imam's madhhab) is not punished. The commentator reconciles the differing expressions: the obligation is upon habitual abandonment, not occasional; constant attendance is a confirmed sunnah. Thus, the ruling is that jama'ah is wajib according to the majority, and the difference is terminological.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama‘ah): Congregational prayer led by an imam, specifically the five daily prayers in congregation.
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah—an act the Prophet consistently performed and encouraged, which in the Hanafi school is treated like wajib in terms of blame for leaving, though not legally obligatory in the strict sense.
التعزير (al-ta‘zir): Discretionary punishment prescribed by the judge for offenses not covered by fixed hudud, including leaving congregational prayer without excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the preponderant view in the Hanafi school, what is the legal status of congregational prayer (jama'ah) for men?
A) Fard 'ayn
B) Wajib
C) Sunnah mu'akkadah
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Congregational prayer for men is wajib in the Hanafi school, with legal consequences for habitual abandonment, despite some early Hanafis calling it sunnah mu'akkadah.

Obligation of Congregational Prayer and Consequences for Abandonment
This passage proves the obligation of jama'ah, explains its level (wajib/sunnah mu'akkadah), and details penalties for abandoning it without excuse.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on congregational prayer (wajib/sunnah mu'akkadah), identify the evidence from the Sunnah, and explain the legal consequences of abandonment without excuse.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is wajib in the Hanafi school; habitual abandonment incurs ta'zir and rejection of testimony.

This passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies the Hanafi ruling on jama'ah. While some call it sunnah mu'akkadah, the text shows it carries the weight of obligation (wajib) based on the Prophet's continuous practice and severe threats. Understanding this position is essential for recognizing the legal consequences of missing jama'ah without excuse.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Hanafi position
The passage opens by noting that calling jama'ah 'sunnah mu'akkadah' is equivalent to calling it wajib in practice. Locate where the author equates the two and notes that it is among the rituals of Islam.
The term 'wajib' here carries the force of obligation, with legal consequences.
2
Locate the dalil
Find the evidence from the Sunnah: the Prophet's continuous practice, his censure of those who abandon it, and the hadith of twenty-seven-fold reward. Note how these are used to prove obligation.
The passage emphasizes that the evidence is from many hadith, indicating strong proof.
3
Trace the legal consequences
Identify the rulings for the abandoner: ta'zir, rejection of testimony, and sin on neighbors who remain silent. Also note the ruling on fighting if a whole city abandons it.
These consequences show that jama'ah is treated as obligatory in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Distinguish between excuses
The passage discusses when abandonment is excused (forgetfulness, valid interpretation) and when it is not (istikhfaf, habitual carelessness). Note the distinction between repeating fiqh and repeating language.
Istikhfaf here means laziness, not contempt; the latter would be kufr.

كتاب الصلاة - باب الإمامة
سنة مؤكدة ليس مخالفاً في الحقيقة بل في العبارة لأن السنة المؤكدة والواجب سواء خصوصاً ما كان من شعائر الإسلام ودليله من السنة المواظبة من غير ترك مع النكير على تاركها بغير أحاديث كثيرة. وفي المجتبى والظاهر أنهم أرادوا بالتأكيد الوجوب لاستدلالهم بالأخبار الواردة بالوعيد الشديد بترك الجماعة. وصرح في المحيط بأنه لا يرخص لأحد في تركها بغير عذر حتى لو تركها أهل مصر يؤمرون بها فإن ائتمروا وإلا يحل مقاتلتهم، وفي القنية وغيرها : بأنه يجب التعزير على تاركها بغير عذر ويأثم الجيران بالسكوت. وفيها : لو انتظر الإقامة لدخول المسجد فهو مسيء. وفي المجتبى : ومن سمع النداء كره له الاشتغال بالعمل. وعن عائشة أنه حرام يعني حالة الأذان وإن عمل بعده قبل الصلاة فلا بأس به. وعن محمد : لا بأس بالإسراع إلى الجمعة والجماعة ما لم يجهد نفسه والسكينة أفضل فيها اهـ . وفي الخلاصة : يجوز التعزير بأخذ الماء ومن ذلك رجل لا يحضر الجماعة اهـ. وسيأتي إن شاء الله تعالى في محله أن معناه ماله عنه مدة ثم دفعه له لا أخذه على وجه التملك كما قد كما صرح به في البزازية وذكر في غاية البيان معزياً إلى الأجناس أن تارك الجماعة يتوهم يستوجب إساءة ولا تقبل شهادته إذا تركها استخفافاً بذلك ،ومجانة أما إذا تركها سهواً أو تركها بتأويل بأن يكون الإمام من أهل الأهواء أو مخالفاً لمذهب المقتدي لا يراعى مذهبه فلا يستوجب الإساءة وتقبل شهادته .اهـ. وفي شرح النقاية عن نجم الأئمة: رجل يشتغل بتكرار الفقه ليلاً ونهاراً ولا يحضر الجماعة لا يعذر ولا تقبل شهادته. وقال أيضاً: رجل يشتغل بتكرار اللغة فتفوته الجماعة لا يعذر بخلاف تكرار الفقه. قيل جوابه الأول فيمن واظب على ترك الجماعة تهاوناً، والثاني فيمن لا يواظب على تركها اهـ. وفي شرح المنية للحلبي والأحكام تدل على الوجوب من أن تاركها من غير عذر يعزر وترد شهادته ويأثم الجيران بالسكوت عنه وهذه كلها أحكام الواجب وقد يوفق بأن ترتيب الوعيد في الحديث وهذه الأحكام مما يستدل به على الوجوب مقيد بالمداومة على الترك كما قول عليه السلام لا يشهدون الصلاة وفي الحديث الآخر يصلون في بيوتهم، كما يعطيه ظاهر إسناد المضارع نحو بنو فلان يأكلون البر أي عادتهم فيكون الواجب الحضور أحياناً، والسنة المؤكدة التي تقرب منه المواظبة عليها وحينئذ فلا منافاة بين ما تقدم وبين قوله عليه السلام صلاة الرجل في الجماعة تفضل على صلاته في بيته أو سوقه سبعاً وعشرين ضعفاً اهـ. قوله : (إذا تركها استخفافاً) أي تهاوناً وتكاسلاً وليس المراد حقيقة الاستخفاف الذي هو الاحتقار فإنه كفر.
Book of Prayer - Chapter of Imamah. It is a confirmed sunnah, not differing in reality but in expression, because the confirmed sunnah and wajib are the same, especially what is among the rituals of Islam. Its evidence from the sunnah is continuous practice without leaving, with censure upon the one who abandons it without excuse, from many hadith. In al-Mujtaba: Apparently they intended by 'confirmed' the obligation, due to their inference from reports containing severe threat for abandoning the congregation. And it is explicitly stated in al-Muhit that no one is permitted to abandon it without excuse, such that if the people of a city abandon it, they are commanded to perform it; if they comply, otherwise they are fought. In al-Quniya and others: Ta'zir is obligatory upon the one who abandons it without excuse, and the neighbors sin by remaining silent. In it: If one waits for the iqamah to enter the mosque, he is doing wrong. In al-Mujtaba: Whoever hears the call, it is disliked for him to engage in work. From Aisha: It is haram, meaning at the time of adhan, and if he works after it before prayer, there is no harm. From Muhammad: There is no harm in hurrying to jumuah and congregation as long as he does not exhaust himself, and tranquility is better therein. In al-Khulasa: Ta'zir is permissible by taking water, and among that is a man who does not attend the congregation. It will come, if Allah wills, in its place that its meaning is that he has [money] with him for a period then gives it to him, not taking it as ownership, as explicitly stated in al-Bazzaziyya. And mentioned in Ghayat al-Bayan, attributed to al-Ajnas, that the abandoner of congregation is suspected of deserving blame, and his testimony is not accepted if he abandons it out of slighting and carelessness. As for if he abandons it forgetfully or due to an interpretation, such as the imam being a person of desires or opposing the follower's madhhab, not regarding his madhhab, then he does not deserve blame and his testimony is accepted. In Sharh al-Niqaya from Najm al-A'imma: A man who occupies himself with repeating fiqh night and day and does not attend the congregation is not excused and his testimony is not accepted. And he also said: A man who occupies himself with repeating language so that congregation is missed is not excused, unlike repeating fiqh. It was said: The first answer concerns one who persists in abandoning congregation out of carelessness, and the second concerns one who does not persist in abandoning it. In Sharh al-Munya al-Halabi: The rulings indicate obligation, because the one who abandons it without excuse is punished (ta'zir), his testimony is rejected, and the neighbors sin by remaining silent about him. These are all rulings of the wajib. And it may be reconciled by restricting the threat in the hadith and these rulings as evidence for obligation to persisting in abandonment, as in the saying of the Prophet, peace be upon him, 'they do not attend the prayer' and in another hadith 'they pray in their homes' – as the apparent meaning of the present tense reference like 'the sons of so-and-so eat wheat' – i.e., their habit. So the obligatory is to attend sometimes, and the confirmed sunnah that approaches it is continuity upon it. Then there is no contradiction between what preceded and his saying, peace be upon him, 'A man's prayer in congregation is superior to his prayer in his home or market by twenty-seven degrees.' His saying: 'If he abandons it out of slighting' means neglect and laziness, and the intended meaning is not the actual slighting which is contempt, for that is disbelief.
Source pages p. 603

Commentary
This passage is a detailed ruling with proof on the obligation of congregational prayer. It opens by addressing a common Hanafi expression: calling jama'ah a 'confirmed sunnah' (sunnah mu'akkadah) is not substantively different from calling it 'obligatory' (wajib), especially for rituals of Islam. The proof is the continuous practice of the Prophet (ﷺ) and his censure of those who abandoned it. The author then cites al-Mujtaba that Hanafis intend obligation by 'confirmed', using hadith with severe threats. Stronger evidence comes from al-Muhit: jama'ah is so mandatory that if a whole city abandons it, they are commanded, and if they refuse, they may be fought. This indicates a ruling of wajib, not merely sunnah. Additional consequences: ta'zir (disciplinary punishment) for the abandoner, sin on neighbors who remain silent, and discouragement of worldly work after the adhan. The passage then addresses excuses: if a person abandons jama'ah out of slighting (istikhfaf), his testimony is rejected; but if due to forgetfulness or a valid interpretation (e.g., the imam is an innovator), he is not at fault. There is a nuance: repeating fiqh (Islamic law) continuously is an excuse for missing jama'ah, but repeating language (like Arabic grammar) is not, unless one persists in missing it out of carelessness. The final reconciliation from Sharh al-Munya: the severe threats apply to those who habitually miss jama'ah, not to occasional absence. This aligns with the hadith of 27-fold reward, which does not contradict the obligation. The note clarifies that 'slighting' (istikhfaf) here means laziness, not contempt, which would be kufr.

Key Terms
سنة مؤكدة (sunnah mu'akkadah): A confirmed sunnah that the Prophet (ﷺ) consistently performed and never omitted; the text equates it to wajib in this context.
التعزير (al-ta'zir): Discretionary punishment determined by the judge for offenses without fixed hadd; here applied to one who abandons jama'ah without excuse.
استخفاف (istikhfaf): Slighting or treating as unimportant; in the text, it is distinguished from actual contempt (which would be kufr).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the consequence for a person who habitually abandons congregational prayer without excuse?
A) He is excused if he repeats fiqh daily
B) His testimony is rejected and he is punished by ta'zir
C) He only loses the reward of twenty-seven times
D) His neighbors are forbidden from speaking to him

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, congregational prayer is wajib, and habitual abandonment without excuse incurs legal consequences including ta'zir and rejection of testimony.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate

Minimum Number and Rulings for Congregation in Various Prayers
Ruling statement defining minimum jama'ah and its hukm for various prayers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number for a valid jama'ah, distinguish the hukm of jama'ah for each prayer type, identify the condition of validity for 'Eid and jumu'ah, and explain why voluntary jama'ah by mutual agreement is disliked in the Hanafi school.

Core Idea
Jama'ah requires only two: imam and one follower; its hukm varies from wajib to makruh depending on the prayer.

In this passage from Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author expands on the rulings of jama'ah not covered earlier. We learn that the minimum congregation is two persons—an imam and one discerning follower, regardless of gender or status. The hukm of jama'ah differs: it is wajib for the five daily prayers, a condition of validity for jumu'ah and 'Eid, sunnah for eclipse and tarawih, and even disliked for witr outside Ramadan (with scholarly difference). The passage also addresses voluntary congregations: arranging a group prayer by mutual agreement is generally disliked, but spontaneous prayer without adhan/iqamah is not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the minimum number and who qualifies
Find the statement that the minimum for jama'ah is two: the imam and one other. Note that the follower can be male, female, free, slave, or a discerning child. A non-discerning child does not count.
This is critical for fulfilling the virtue of jama'ah at home with family.
2
Categorize the hukm of jama'ah for each prayer type
Read the list: five daily prayers (wajib), jumu'ah (shart, not just wajib), 'Eid (wajib or sunnah but both agree it is a condition of validity), eclipse (sunnah), tarawih (sunnah kifayah), and witr in Ramadan (recommended), witr outside Ramadan (disliked according to some).
Note the intra-Hanafi difference on witr: al-Quduri says no dislike.
3
Understand the condition of validity for 'Eid and jumu'ah
The passage says jama'ah is a condition (shart) for the validity of 'Eid prayers on both opinions, just like jumu'ah. This means one cannot pray 'Eid individually.
This is a key point: even if 'Eid is considered sunnah, the congregation is still required for validity.
4
Examine the ruling on voluntary jama'ah by mutual agreement (tada'i)
The passage distinguishes between voluntary jama'ah arranged by agreement (disliked) and spontaneous jama'ah without adhan/iqamah (not disliked). Al-Halwani adds that with three followers there is no dislike by consensus; with four there is dispute.
This shows the Hanafi carefulness to avoid innovation (bid'ah) in voluntary prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولم يذكر المصنف بقية أحكامها فمنها : أن أقلها اثنان واحد مع الإمام في غير الجمعة لأنها مأخوذة من الاجتماع وهما أقل ما يتحقق بهما الاجتماع ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام الاثنان فما فوقهما جماعة (1) ضعيف كما في شرح منية المصلي، وسواء كان ذلك الواحد رجلاً أو امرأة، حراً أو عبداً أو صبياً يعقل ولا عبرة بغير العاقل. وهو وفي السراج الوهاج : لو حلف لا يصلي بجماعة وأم صبياً يعقل حنث في يمينه. ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يكون في المسجد أو بيته حتى لو صلى في بيته بزوجته أو جاريته أو ولده فقد أتى بفضيلة الجماعة. ومنها أنها واجبة للصلوات الخمس إلا للجمعة فإنها شرط فيها، وتجب لصلاة العيدين على القول بوجوبها وتسن فيها على القول بسنيتها، وفي الكسوف والتراويح سنة وسيأتي أن الصحيح أنها في التراويح سنة على الكفاية. ونص في جوامع الفقه على أنها فيها واجبة وهو غريب ويستحب في الوتر في رمضان على قول، ولا يستحب فيه على قول، وهي مكروهة في صلاة الخسوف وقيل لا . وأما ما عدا هذه الجملة ففي الخلاصة الاقتداء في الوتر خارج رمضان يكره، وذكر القدوري أنه لا يكره. وأصل هذا أن التطوع بالجماعة إذا كان على سبيل التداعي يكره في الأصل للصدر الشهيد، أما إذا صلوا بجماعة بغير أذان وإقامة في ناحية المسجد لا يكره. وقال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : إن كان سوى الإمام ثلاثة لا يكره في بالاتفاق، وفي الأربع اختلف المشايخ والأصح أنه يكره اهـ. كذا في شرح المنية. ولا يخفى أن الجماعة في العيدين وإن كانت واجبة أو سنة على القولين فيها فهي شرط الصحة على كل قول لأن شرائط العيدين وجوباً وصحة شرائط الجمعة إلا الخطبة فلا تصح صلاة العيدين منفرداً كالجمعة، ولا يلزم من بطلان الوصف بطلان الأصل على
And the author did not mention the remaining rulings of it. Among them is that the minimum is two: one with the imam, in other than jumu'ah, because it is derived from 'gathering' and they are the minimum by which gathering is realized; and due to his saying, peace be upon him, 'Two and above constitute a congregation' is weak, as in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And it is the same whether that one is a man or a woman, free or slave, or a discerning child; the non-discerning are not considered. And in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If one swears that he will not pray in congregation, and he leads a discerning child, he breaks his oath. There is no difference in that between being in the mosque or his house, such that if he prays in his house with his wife, his concubine, or his child, he has attained the virtue of congregation. And among them is that it is obligatory for the five daily prayers, except for jumu'ah for which it is a condition (shart). It is obligatory for the two 'Eid prayers according to the view that they are obligatory, and sunnah according to the view that they are sunnah. For eclipse and tarawih, it is sunnah; and it will come that the correct view is that for tarawih it is sunnah on kifayah. It is stated in Jawami' al-Fiqh that it is obligatory therein, which is odd. It is recommended for witr in Ramadan according to one view, and not recommended according to another. It is disliked in the prayer of lunar eclipse, and some say no. As for beyond these, in al-Khulasa: Following in witr outside Ramadan is disliked, and al-Quduri mentioned it is not disliked. The origin of this is that supererogatory prayer in congregation by mutual agreement is disliked in principle, according to al-Sadr al-Shahid. As for when they pray in congregation without adhan and iqamah in a corner of the mosque, it is not disliked. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: If besides the imam there are three, it is not disliked by agreement; for four, the scholars differed, and the correct view is that it is disliked. End quote. In Sharh al-Munya: It is not hidden that congregation in the two 'Eids, whether obligatory or sunnah according to the two views, is a condition of validity on every view, because the conditions of the two 'Eids, in terms of obligation and validity, are the conditions of jumu'ah except the sermon, so the 'Eid prayer is not valid individually, like jumu'ah. The invalidity of the description does not necessitate the invalidity of the origin.
Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement detailing the remaining rulings of congregational prayer (jama'ah) not covered earlier. It first addresses the minimum number: for other than jumu'ah, the minimum is one follower with the imam, making two persons total. The hadith 'Two and above constitute a congregation' is considered weak. The follower can be a man, woman, free, slave, or discerning child; a non-discerning child does not count. This is important for oaths: if a person swears not to pray in congregation and leads a discerning child, he breaks his oath. Importantly, praying at home with one's wife, concubine, or child still grants the virtue of congregation. The passage then categorizes jama'ah for different prayers: wajib for the five daily prayers (with jumu'ah's jama'ah being a condition of validity, not just obligation); obligatory for 'Eid according to one opinion, sunnah according to another, but in either case it is a condition of validity—'Eid prayer cannot be performed individually. For eclipse and tarawih, it is sunnah. For witr in Ramadan, it is recommended according to some; outside Ramadan, it is disliked according to some scholars, though al-Quduri holds no dislike. The dislike for voluntary congregational prayers applies when they are arranged by mutual agreement (tada'i); but if done spontaneously without adhan and iqamah in a corner of the mosque, it is not disliked. Al-Halwani's rule: if there are three followers, no dislike by consensus; with four followers, there is a difference, and the correct view is that it is disliked.

Key Terms
أقل الجماعة (aqall al-jama'ah): The minimum number required for a valid congregation: two persons (imam and one follower) for other than jumu'ah.
شرط الصحة (shart al-sihhah): A condition for validity of the prayer; for 'Eid and jumu'ah, jama'ah is a condition without which the prayer is invalid.
التداعي (al-tada'i): Mutual agreement to form a voluntary congregation; this is disliked in principle by Hanafis.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

B) Witr jama'ah outside Ramadan is disliked according to al-Sadr al-Shahid.
C) Jama'ah for 'Eid prayer is not required for validity.
D) Praying at home with one's wife does not count as jama'ah.

Key Takeaway
The minimum for jama'ah is two; its ruling varies by prayer, and voluntary congregations by mutual agreement are generally disliked unless spontaneous and small.

Salah — Prayer
beginner

Minimum Number for Congregation and Conditions of the Follower
Ruling with proof on minimum congregation and follower conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum number for congregational prayer in the Hanafi school, identify who qualifies as a follower, and explain the Hanafi disagreement on the reward of home congregation.

Core Idea
The minimum congregation is two: an imam and one follower, who may be a discerning child, woman, or slave; home congregation is valid but its reward is less than mosque.

This passage from the commentary on Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies two essential rulings: the minimal size for a valid congregation and who can serve as a follower. It also addresses a debate among later Hanafi scholars about whether praying at home with family carries the same reward as congregational prayer in the mosque. Understanding these points is crucial for correctly assessing the validity and virtue of congregational prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on minimum congregation
The text states that the minimum number for a valid congregational prayer (excluding Jumu'ah) is two: one imam and one follower. This is derived from the meaning of 'jama'ah' (gathering) and a hadith, though it is considered weak.
The hadith 'الاثنان فما فوقهما جماعة' is cited but noted as weak; however, the ruling is confirmed by other evidence.
2
Identify the conditions for a follower
Determine who may validly follow an imam. The passage says any sane, discerning person qualifies: man, woman, free, slave, or discerning child. A non-discerning person (e.g., infant) does not count.
A 'discerning child' (الصبي يعقل) is one who understands the prayer and can follow the imam's actions.
3
Recognize the scope of validity: mosque vs. home
The ruling applies whether the congregation is in the mosque or at home. Praying with one's wife, slave-girl, or child at home fulfills the congregation and brings reward, though with a possible difference in virtue.
The text then introduces an intra-Hanafi dispute about the reward at home.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on home congregation
Al-Halwani reportedly held that home congregation yields no reward and is blameworthy. The majority (including the commentator) hold that it does bring reward, though less than the mosque. This is the relied-upon view.
The commentator resolves the dispute by linking al-Halwani's opinion to his stance on the obligation to attend the mosque when called, which is not the dominant view.
5
Extract the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The mufta bihi is that home congregation is valid and rewardable, but the virtue is less than that of mosque congregation. This is based on the majority and confirmed by the commentary.
This reconciliation shows the method of tarjih among conflicting Hanafi positions.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
فمنها : أن أقلها اثنان واحد مع الإمام في غير الجمعة لأنها مأخوذة من الاجتماع وهما أقل ما يتحقق بهما الاجتماع ولقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام الاثنان فما فوقهما جماعة (1) ضعيف كما في شرح منية المصلي، وسواء كان ذلك الواحد رجلاً أو امرأة، حراً أو عبداً أو صبياً يعقل ولا عبرة بغير العاقل. وفي السراج الوهاج : لو حلف لا يصلي بجماعة وأم صبياً يعقل حنث في يمينه. ولا فرق في ذلك بين أن يكون في المسجد أو بيته حتى لو صلى في بيته بزوجته أو جاريته أو ولده فقد أتى بفضيلة الجماعة. قوله: (حتى لو صلى في بيته بزوجته الخ) سيأتي خلافه عن الحلواني من أنه لا ينال الثواب ويكون بدعة ومكروهاً لكن قال في القنية : اختلف العلماء في إقامتها في البيت والأصح أنها كإقامتها في المسجد إلا في الفضيلة، وهو ظاهر مذهب الشافعي رحمه الله تعالى اهـ. قلت: ويظهر لي أن ما سيأتي عن الحلواني مبني على ما مر عنه في الأذان من وجوب الإجابة بالقدم، وتقدم أن الظاهر خلافه فلذا صححوا خلاف ما قاله هنا أيضاً
Among them: that its minimum is two: one with the imam, except in Jumu'ah because it is derived from gathering and two is the least by which gathering is realized, and because of his saying (peace be upon him): 'Two or more constitute a congregation' – weak as in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli. And that one may be a man or a woman, free or slave, or a discerning child; the non-discerning is not considered. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If he swore not to pray in congregation and led a discerning child, he breaks his oath. There is no difference in this between being in the mosque or his home; even if he prayed in his home with his wife, his slave-girl, or his child, he has attained the virtue of congregation. His statement: ('Even if he prayed in his home with his wife, etc.') Its disagreement from al-Halwani will come later – that he does not receive the reward and it would be an innovation and disliked. But in al-Qunyah: The scholars disagreed about performing it at home, and the correct view is that it is like performing it in the mosque except in virtue, and this is the apparent madhhab of al-Shafi'i, may Allah have mercy on him. I say: It appears to me that what will come from al-Halwani is based on what was mentioned from him about the call to prayer regarding the obligation of responding by foot, and it was established that the apparent view is otherwise, so they declared correct the opposite of what he said here as well.
Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This passage from the sharh of Kanz al-Daqa'iq explains the minimum number for a valid congregation and who may serve as a follower. It states that the minimum is two: an imam and one follower, except for Friday prayer which requires a larger number. The proof is a hadith, though noted as weak. The follower can be any person of sound mind: man, woman, free, slave, or a discerning child. Non-discerning persons (e.g., an infant) are not valid as followers. If someone swears not to pray in congregation, leading a discerning child would break that oath because it is a valid congregation. The virtue of congregation is also attained by praying at home with family members. The commentary then addresses a disagreement: al-Halwani reportedly held that such a home congregation does not bring reward and is even blameworthy, but the majority consider it valid and rewarding, albeit with less virtue than mosque congregation. The commentator reconciles this by noting that al-Halwani's view is based on a different principle regarding the obligation to respond to the call to prayer. The relied-upon view is that home congregation is valid and brings reward.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): A group of two or more persons praying together with one imam.
الصبي يعقل (al-sabiyyu ya'qilu): A discerning child who understands the prayer and can follow the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum number for a valid congregational prayer (جماعة) according to the Hanafi school?
A) Three
B) Two
C) Five
D) One

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school holds that a valid congregation requires only two: an imam and one follower, who may be a discerning child or any sane person, and even home congregation is rewardable though less virtuous than mosque.

Rulings on Congregation for Different Prayers
Categorization of congregation rulings by prayer type

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on congregation for each prayer type (five daily, Jumu'ah, Eid, eclipse, Taraweeh, Witr) and identify which prayers require congregation as a condition of validity.

Core Idea
Congregation is obligatory for five daily, condition for Jumu'ah/Eid, sunnah for eclipse/Taraweeh, makruh for Witr outside Ramadan and habitual nafl.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq systematically categorizes the rulings on congregation (jama'ah) across different prayers. You will learn that while the five daily prayers require congregation as a wajib, Jumu'ah and Eid prayers require it as a condition (shart) for validity—meaning they cannot be performed individually. Other prayers like eclipse and Taraweeh are sunnah, and voluntary congregation is discouraged if done habitually. Understanding these distinctions is essential for correct practice.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prayer type
For each prayer mentioned (five daily, Jumu'ah, Eid, eclipse, Taraweeh, Witr), note the specific ruling given in the passage.
2
Distinguish wajib vs. shart
Recognize that for Jumu'ah and Eid, congregation is a condition (shart) for validity, not merely an obligation (wajib). This means the prayer is invalid without congregation, unlike the five daily where it is wajib but the prayer remains valid alone.
3
Note the intra-madhhab ikhtilaf
Observe the differences: for Eid, two opinions (wajib vs sunnah); for Witr in Ramadan (mustahab vs not); for Witr outside Ramadan (makruh vs not); and for voluntary congregation (makruh if habitual vs permissible if occasional).
4
Apply the condition rule
Understand that both opinions on Eid agree that congregation is a condition of validity, analogously to Jumu'ah. Therefore, Eid cannot be prayed alone.
The passage emphasizes: 'شرط الصحة على كل قول'.
5
Summarize the general principle
Synthesize the rulings: congregation is most emphasized for obligatory prayers, becomes a condition for Friday and Eid, and is less emphasized for supererogatory prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ومنها أنها واجبة للصلوات الخمس إلا للجمعة فإنها شرط فيها، وتجب لصلاة العيدين على القول بوجوبها وتسن فيها على القول بسنيتها، وفي الكسوف والتراويح سنة وسيأتي أن الصحيح أنها في التراويح سنة على الكفاية. ونص في جوامع الفقه على أنها فيها واجبة وهو غريب ويستحب في الوتر في رمضان على قول، ولا يستحب فيه على قول، وهي مكروهة في صلاة الخسوف وقيل لا . وأما ما عدا هذه الجملة ففي الخلاصة الاقتداء في الوتر خارج رمضان يكره، وذكر القدوري أنه لا يكره. وأصل هذا أن التطوع بالجماعة إذا كان على سبيل التداعي يكره في الأصل للصدر الشهيد، أما إذا صلوا بجماعة بغير أذان وإقامة في ناحية المسجد لا يكره. وقال شمس الأئمة الحلواني : إن كان سوى الإمام ثلاثة لا يكره في بالاتفاق، وفي الأربع اختلف المشايخ والأصح أنه يكره اهـ. كذا في شرح المنية. ولا يخفى أن الجماعة في العيدين وإن كانت واجبة أو سنة على القولين فيها فهي شرط الصحة على كل قول لأن شرائط العيدين وجوباً وصحة شرائط الجمعة إلا الخطبة فلا تصح صلاة العيدين منفرداً كالجمعة، ولا يلزم من بطلان الوصف بطلان الأصل على المذهب.
And among them: that it is obligatory for the five prayers, except for Friday – for it is a condition therein. It is obligatory for the Eid prayer according to the opinion of its obligation, and sunnah according to the opinion of its being sunnah. For eclipse and Taraweeh, it is sunnah; later it will come that the correct view is that it is sunnah on sufficiency for Taraweeh. It is stated in Jawami' al-Fiqh that it is obligatory in them, which is strange. It is mustahab in Witr in Ramadan according to one opinion, and not mustahab according to another. It is makruh in the eclipse prayer, and some said no. As for beyond these, in al-Khulasah: following in Witr outside Ramadan is makruh, and al-Quduri mentioned that it is not makruh. The basis of this is that voluntary congregation if done repeatedly (tada'i) is makruh in principle according to al-Sadr al-Shahid. However, if they pray in congregation without adhan and iqamah in a corner of the mosque, it is not makruh. Shams al-A'imma al-Halwani said: If besides the imam there are three, it is not makruh by agreement, regarding four the scholars disagreed and the correct is that it is makruh. This is in Sharh al-Munyah. It is obvious that congregation in the Eid prayers, whether it is obligatory or sunnah according to the two opinions, it is a condition of validity according to every opinion, because the conditions of Eid, obligation and validity, are the conditions of Friday except the khutbah. Therefore the Eid prayer is not valid individually like Friday, and the nullification of the description does not necessitate nullification of the essence according to the madhhab.
Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This passage enumerates the rulings on congregation (جماعة) for various prayers. For the five daily prayers, it is obligatory (واجب). For Jumu'ah, congregation is a condition (شرط) for validity. For Eid prayer, there are two views: some say it is obligatory, others say sunnah mu'akkadah; but in either case, congregation is a condition of validity – one cannot pray Eid alone. For eclipse (كسوف/خسوف) and Taraweeh prayers, congregation is sunnah. For Taraweeh, the correct view is that it is sunnah 'ala al-kifayah (sunnah on sufficiency). For Witr in Ramadan, some consider it mustahab, others do not. For Witr outside Ramadan, following in congregation is makruh according to the majority, but al-Quduri says it is not makruh. Voluntary congregational prayer (تطوع بالجماعة) is generally makruh if done repeatedly and habitually (على سبيل التداعي), but not if done occasionally without adhan and iqamah in a corner. The passage also notes a nuance: the conditions for Eid prayer are the same as Jumu'ah except for the khutbah, so Eid cannot be performed individually.

Key Terms
التطوع بالجماعة (al-tatawwu' bi al-jama'ah): Voluntary prayers performed in congregation.
الجماعة في العيدين (al-jama'ah fi al-'idayn): Congregation for Eid prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on praying Witr in congregation outside of Ramadan?
A) Sunnah
B) Wajib
C) Makruh
D) Mubah

Key Takeaway
Congregation is wajib for five daily prayers, a condition for Jumu'ah and Eid, sunnah for eclipse and Taraweeh, and makruh for Witr outside Ramadan and repeated voluntary congregations.

Hanafi Ruling on Repeating Congregation in a Mosque
Detailing the Hanafi view and differences on repeating congregational prayer in a mosque

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on repeating congregational prayer in a mosque, identify the exceptions, and evaluate the Shafi'i counterargument.

Core Idea
Repeating the congregation is disliked to preserve unity, but exceptions safeguard community rights.

When the residents of a mosque have already prayed, what should a latecomer do? The Hanafi school holds that repeating the entire congregation is generally disliked, based on the practice of the Companions. However, this ruling is nuanced: it depends on the mosque's ownership and location. In this lesson, you will explore the reasoning behind the Hanafi position, the Shafi'i objection, and the practical exceptions that allow repeated congregations in certain settings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Begin by identifying the default Hanafi ruling: repeating the congregation in a mosque that has residents is makruh tanzihi (disliked). Understand that the dislike is to avoid reducing the size of the main congregation and to follow the Companion's practice of praying alone when late.
This ruling applies when the mosque has a fixed community (ahl al-masjid).
2
Identify the opponent's view
Recognize the Shafi'i position that repetition is permissible, as the congregation is a right for every Muslim and later attendees are like the first.
Some later Hanafis like al-Sindi also allowed it, but this is not the relied-upon view.
3
Analyze the Hanafi proof
Examine the Hanafi dalil: the Companions prayed individually when they missed the congregation. This shows that repeating an entire congregation was not their practice. Additionally, repeating reduces the number in one congregation, which contradicts the encouraged ideal of a large unified congregation.
The Hanafi proof is based on both transmitted evidence (athar) and rational consideration (ma'qul).
4
Learn the exceptions
The Hanafi school allows repetition in two cases: (1) If the first congregation was by outsiders (ghuraba'), the residents may repeat with adhan and iqamah because the mosque is theirs. (2) If the mosque is on a public road (qari'at al-tariq) with no fixed community, repetition is allowed freely.
These exceptions are based on the idea of community right and lesser sanctity.
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
The difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i rulings affects mosque practice: Hanafis discourage multiple congregations in a neighborhood mosque, while Shafi'is permit them. In modern settings, this influences how mosques schedule prayers.
The Hanafi position aims to preserve the spirit of one united congregation.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (أما إذا صلوا بجماعة الخ) لا محل لهذا الجملة هنا وإنما محلها فيما بعد عند ذكر حكم المذهب. قوله: (ومنها حكم تكرارها في مسجد واحد (الخ قال قاضيخان في شرح الجامع الصغير : رجل دخل مسجداً قد صلى فيه أهله فإنه يصلي بغير أذان وإقامة لأن في تكرار الجماعة تقليلها. وقال الشافعي : لا بأس بذلك لأن أداء الصلاة بالجماعة حق المسلمين والآخرون فيها كالأولين والصحيح ما قلنا وهكذا روي عن أصحاب النبي صلى الله تعالى عليه وسلم أنهم إذا فاتتهم الجماعة صلوا وحداناً، وعن أبي يوسف رحمه الله أنه قال: إنما يكره تكرار الجماعة إذا كثر القوم، أما إذا صلوا في ناحية المسجد لا يكره. وهذا إذا كان صلى فيه أهله فإن صلى فيه قوم من الغرباء بالجماعة فلأهل المسجد أن يصلوا بعدهم بجماعة بأذان وإقامة لأن إقامة الجماعة في هذا المسجد حقهم، ولهذا كان لهم نصب المؤذن وغير ذلك فلا يبطل حقهم بإقامة غيرهم. وهذا إذا لم يكن المسجد على قارعة الطريق، فإن كان كذلك فلا بأس بتكرار الجماعة فيه بأذان وإقامة لأنه ليس له أهل معلوم حرمته أخف، ولهذا لا يقام فيه باعتكاف الواجب فكان بمنزلة الرباط في المفاوز وهناك تعاد مرة بعد أخرى فهذا كذلك اهـ بحروفه، ومثله في الحقائق وقدمنا نحوه في الأذان عن الكافي والمفتاح، وذكره مثله المؤلف عن السراج أقول : ومفاد هذه النقول كراهة التكرار مطلقاً أي ولو بدون أذان وإقامة وأن معنى قول قاضيخان المار يصلي بغير أذان وإقامة» أنه يصلي منفرداً إلا بالجماعة بدليل التعليل والاستدلال بالمروي عن الصحابة، ويؤيده قوله في الظهيرية : وظاهر الرواية أنهم يصلون وحداناً .اهـ. وحينئذ يشكل ما نقله الرملي عن رسالة العلامة السندي عن الملتقط وشرح المجمع وشرح درر البحار والعباب من أنه يجوز تكرار الجماعة بلا أذان ولا إقامة ثانية اتفاقاً قال : وفي بعضها إجماعاً. ثم ذكر أن ما يفعله أهل الحرمين مكروه اتفاقاً وأنه نقل عن بعض مشايخنا إنكاره حين حضر الموسم بمكة سنة إحدى وخمسين وخمسمائة منهم الشريف الغزنوي وأنه أفتى الإمام أبو قاسم الحبان المالكي سنة خمسين وخمسمائة بمنع الصلاة بأئمة متعددة وجماعات مترتبة وعدم جوازها على مذهب العلماء الأربعة ورد على من قال بخلافه. ونقل إنكار ذلك عن جماعة من الحنفية صريحاً.
His statement: ('As for if they pray in congregation, etc.') This sentence has no place here; its place is later when mentioning the ruling of the madhhab. His statement: ('And among them: the ruling on repeating it in one mosque, etc.') Qadi Khan said in Sharh al-Jami' al-Saghir: A man entered a mosque whose people had already prayed; he should pray without adhan and iqamah because repeating the congregation reduces it. Al-Shafi'i said: There is no harm in that because performing the prayer in congregation is a right of the Muslims, and the later ones are like the first ones. The correct is what we said. Thus it was narrated from the Companions of the Prophet (peace and blessings be upon him) that when they missed the congregation, they prayed individually. From Abu Yusuf (may Allah have mercy on him) that he said: Repeating the congregation is only disliked if the people are many; but if they pray in a corner of the mosque, it is not disliked. This is if its people have prayed. If a group of strangers prayed in congregation, then the people of the mosque may pray after them in congregation with adhan and iqamah because establishing the congregation in this mosque is their right, and therefore they have the right to appoint a mu'adhdhin, etc., so their right is not nullified by others' establishment. This is if the mosque is not on a public road (qari'at al-tariq); if it is, then there is no harm in repeating the congregation in it with adhan and iqamah because it has no known people, its sanctity is lighter, and therefore obligatory i'tikaf is not performed in it; it is like a ribat in the deserts where it is repeated time after time. Thus it is. Similarly in al-Haqa'iq, and we have presented the like in the section on adhan from al-Kafi and al-Miftah. The author mentioned it similarly from al-Siraj. I say: The import of these transmissions is the dislike of repetition absolutely, i.e., even without adhan and iqamah, and that the meaning of Qadi Khan's statement 'he prays without adhan and iqamah' is that he prays individually, not in congregation, by virtue of the reasoning and the evidence from the Companions. This is supported by his statement in al-Zahiriyyah: 'The apparent narration is that they pray individually.' Then what al-Ramli transmitted from the treatise of al-Allamah al-Sindi from al-Multaqat, Sharh al-Majma', Sharh Durar al-Bihar, and al-'Ubab becomes problematic – that it is permissible to repeat the congregation without a second adhan and iqamah, unanimously, and in some it is said by consensus. Then he mentioned that what the people of the Two Sanctuaries (Makkah and Madinah) do is disliked by consensus, and that it was transmitted from some of our shaykhs disapproving of it when he attended the mawsim in Makkah in the year 551 AH, among them al-Sharif al-Ghaznawi, and that Imam Abu Qasim al-Habban al-Maliki gave a fatwa in 550 AH forbidding prayer with multiple imams and successive congregations and its impermissibility according to the four madhhabs, and he rebutted those who said otherwise. He transmitted disapproval of that from a group of Hanafis explicitly.
Source pages p. 604

Commentary
This passage deals with the ruling on repeating the congregational prayer in the same mosque after the residents have already prayed. It begins with a cross-reference note that a certain phrase belongs later. Then it presents the discussion of Qadi Khan: if a person enters a mosque where the residents have already prayed, he should pray individually without adhan/iqamah, because repeating the congregation reduces it. The Shafi'i position is mentioned as allowing repetition. The Hanafi proof is the practice of the Companions who prayed alone when they missed the congregation. Hanafi opinions differ on the extent of the dislike: Abu Yusuf restricts the dislike to large groups; Muhammad al-Shaybani dislikes it only if done as a custom; but the majority consider it disliked absolutely. There are exceptions: if the first congregation was by outsiders, the residents may repeat with adhan/iqamah because the mosque is theirs. If the mosque is on a public road (qari'at al-tariq) with no specific community, repetition is allowed. The commentator then critiques the view of al-Sindi and others who claim consensus on permissibility of repetition without adhan/iqamah, asserting that the correct Hanafi view is the dislike of repetition absolutely. Historical support is given from the fatwas of a Maliki Imam and Hanafi shaykhs who forbade multiple congregations in the same mosque in Makkah.

Key Terms
تكرار الجماعة (takrar al-jama'ah): Performing two or more congregational prayers for the same obligatory prayer in the same mosque, one after the other.
قارعة الطريق (qari'at al-tariq): A mosque that is on a main public road, belonging to no specific neighborhood or community.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, repeating the congregation in a mosque is generally disliked but permissible in public mosques and when the first congregation was by outsiders.

Conditions for Obligation of Congregation and Valid Excuses
Ruling on who is obligated to attend congregation and list of valid excuses for missing it.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for the obligation of congregational prayer and identify valid excuses that lift the obligation.

Core Idea
Congregation is wajib upon able men, but valid excuses can lift the obligation.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq clarifies who must attend congregational prayer and when it is excused. The Hanafi school considers congregation a strong obligation (wajib) upon free adult males who are capable, but provides a detailed list of excuses that remove this duty. Understanding these conditions and excuses is essential for applying the ruling correctly in daily life.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its conditions
Locate the statement that congregation is not obligatory except on specific individuals. Note the conditions: male, adult, sane, free, and able without help.
The phrase 'لا تجب إلا على الرجال البالغين العاقلين الأحرار القادرين' is key.
2
List the individuals exempted
The text lists those who are not obligated: old man who cannot walk, sick, disabled, blind even if he has a guide. Understand the reasoning: inability, not merely difficulty.
The exemption for the blind is based on the principle that the ability of others is not considered (لا عبرة بقدرة الغير).
3
Identify the valid excuses
Scan for the excuses that cancel the obligation: extreme cold, intense darkness, rain and wind at night, fear of creditor, fear of losing property, attending a sick person, presence of food, etc.
The author later summarizes twenty excuses in verse.
4
Examine the evidence and wisdom
The passage cites the Quranic verse 'wa arka'u ma'a al-raki'in' as proof. Also discusses the wisdom: fostering harmony, removing loneliness, and teaching the ignorant.
The Hanafi principle: the imperative indicates obligation (al-amr yufidu al-wujub), but the dalala is zanni.
5
Note the intra-madhhab and cross-madhhab points
The text mentions agreement among Hanafis on the obligation, though other schools (Shafi'i) consider it sunnah. Also notes the difference between Jumu'ah and congregation.
The author states 'اتفاق' in Fath al-Qadir regarding the obligation.

Source Text

.اهـ. وأما حكمة مشروعيتها فقد ذكر في ذلك وجوه : أحدها قيام نظام الألفة بين المصلين ولهذه الحكمة شرعت المساجد في المحال لتحصيل التعاهد باللقاء في أوقات الصلوات بين الجيران. ثانيها دفع حصر النفس أن تشتغل بهذه العبادة وحدها. ثالثها تعلم الجاهل من العالم أفعال الصلاة وذكر بعضهم أنها ثابتة بالكتاب وهو قوله تعالى واركعوا مع الراكعين) [البقرة : ٤٣] فهي بالكتاب والسنة. وأما فضائلها ففي السنة الصحيحة أن صلاة الجماعة تفضل صلاة المنفرد ببضع وعشرين درجة وفي المضمرات إنه مكتوب في التوراة صفة أمة محمد وجماعتهم وأنه بكل رجل في صفوفهم تزاد في صلاتهم صلاة يعني إذا كانوا ألف رجل يكتب لكل رجل ألف صلاة. مطلقاً : والشافعية والمالكية حضر والموسم سنة إحدى وخمسين وخمسمائة .اهـ. قوله : (وتسقط بعذر البرد الشديد الخ) أقول : قد أوصلها في متن التنوير وشرحه الدر المختار إلى عشرين وقد نظمتها بقولي : خذ عد أعذاراً لترك جماعة عشرين نظماً قد أتى مثل الدرر مرض وإقعاد عـمـي وزمانة مطر وطين ثم برد قد أضر قطع لرجــل مـع يـد أو دونهـا فلج وعجز الشيخ قصد للسفر خوف على مال كذا من ظالم أو دائن وشهي أكل قد حضر
It is not obligatory except upon adult, sane, free men who are able to do it without [help]. So it is not obligatory upon an old man who cannot walk, nor upon a sick person, a handicapped person, or a blind person even if he finds someone to lead him. And according to Abu Hanifa, he is carried because it is known that the ability of others is not considered. It is verified in Fath al-Qadir that there is agreement, but the difference is in Jumu'ah, not in congregation. It is excused by extreme cold and intense darkness. It is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that among them are rain and wind in a dark night; but in the daytime, wind is not an excuse. Also if he is fighting off one of the two impurities or both, or if he fears that his creditor would imprison him for debt, or if he fears darkness, or intends to travel and the prayer is established and he fears missing the caravan, or if he is attending a sick person, or fears loss of his property, also if dinner is served and the Isha prayer is established and his soul desires it, also if food is served at a time other than Isha and his soul desires it. In Fath al-Qadir: If he misses it, it is not obligatory to search in mosques without difference among our scholars; rather, if he goes to another mosque for congregation, good, and if he prays in his neighborhood mosque individually, good. Al-Quduri mentioned: He gathers his family and prays with them, meaning he attains the reward of congregation. Shams al-A'imma said: The first in our time is to follow it. Al-Halwani was asked about one who occasionally gathers his family: Does he attain the reward of congregation? He said: No, it would be an innovation and disliked without excuse. And there is difference on the best: the congregation of his neighborhood mosque or the congregation of the central mosque. If there are two mosques, he chooses the oldest. If they are equal, the nearest. If they pray in the nearest and hear the iqamah of another, if he has already entered it, he does not come out, otherwise he goes to it. All this is based on the precedence of the nearest over the one who prefers the central mosque. If a man is a student, then his teacher's study circle is better by agreement. As for the wisdom of its legislation, there are aspects: one, establishing a system of harmony among worshippers; for this wisdom, mosques were established in neighborhoods to achieve mutual acquaintance through meeting at prayer times among neighbors. Second, removing the loneliness of the soul from engaging in this worship alone. Third, teaching the ignorant the actions of prayer from the knowledgeable. Some mentioned that it is established by the Book: the verse 'and bow with those who bow' (2:43). So it is by the Book and Sunnah. As for its virtues, in the authentic sunna, congregational prayer is superior to individual prayer by twenty-some degrees. In al-Mudmarat, it is written in the Torah the description of the nation of Muhammad and their congregation, and that for every man in their rows, an additional prayer is added to their prayer, meaning if they are a thousand men, each man is credited with a thousand prayers. Mutlaqan: The Shafi'is and Malikis attended the season in the year 551... He said: (And it is excused by extreme cold etc.) I say: It has been extended in Matn al-Tanwir and its commentary al-Durr al-Mukhtar to twenty, and I have organized them in my saying: Take count of excuses for leaving congregation twenty in order like pearls: illness, confinement, blindness, chronic disease, rain, mud, then cold that harms, amputation of a leg or foot, paralysis, old age, intention for travel, fear for property, likewise from an oppressor or creditor, and desire for food that is present.
Source pages p. 606

Commentary
This passage discusses the conditions for the obligation of congregational prayer and the valid excuses for missing it. According to the Hanafi school, congregation (jama'ah) is wajib upon free adult males who are capable of attending. The text lists excuses such as illness, blindness, extreme weather, fear of harm, attending to a sick person, or being in the midst of eating when food is present. The passage also discusses the wisdom of congregation and its virtues, citing the Quranic verse and hadith. The author includes a poetic summary of twenty excuses. Note that the obligation is lifted for those with valid excuses, and they may pray individually at home. The Hanafi view is clear: congregation is not fard but a strong obligation (wajib), and one should strive to attend unless a legitimate excuse prevents it.

Key Terms
صلاة الجماعة (ṣalāt al-jamāʿah): Congregational prayer performed by two or more people with one imam.
عذر (ʿudhr): A legal excuse that removes the obligation of congregational prayer.
ثواب الجماعة (thawāb al-jamāʿah): The reward specific to praying in congregation, greater than praying alone.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT a valid excuse for missing congregational prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Severe cold
B) Rain at night
C) Fear of losing one's property
D) Being a student attending a study circle

Key Takeaway
Congregational prayer is wajib upon qualified men, but a defined set of excuses lifts the obligation; missing without excuse is sinful.

Excuses for Missing Congregational Prayer in the Hanafi School
Listing valid excuses for missing jama'ah and its virtues

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position that congregational prayer is wajib and list at least five valid excuses for missing it.

Core Idea
Congregational prayer is wajib but excused for genuine hardship—twenty excuses listed by Hanafi scholars.

Congregational prayer (jama'ah) is a highly emphasized act in the Hanafi school, considered wajib (obligatory) upon men. However, the school recognizes that life brings genuine hardships. This lesson examines the legal excuses that lift the obligation, the wisdom behind congregation, and its immense reward. You will learn to distinguish between valid and invalid excuses and understand the practical rulings for the mufti and the layperson.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling
What is the hukm of jama'ah for men? The passage confirms it is wajib, not fard, based on ahad hadith and the Quranic command.
The Hanafi position is that it is wajib; other schools differ.
2
Recognize the excusing factors
List the excuses mentioned: extreme cold, darkness, rain at night, illness, fear of creditor, etc. Understand that the list is a sample of the principle of hardship.
The commentator versifies twenty excuses from al-Tanwir.
3
Understand the wisdom and virtue
The passage explains three wisdoms: fostering community, relieving loneliness, and enabling learning. The virtue is a reward of 20+ degrees.
This shows the high merit of congregation.
4
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Using the excuses, determine when it is permissible to pray alone. Also note additional rulings on choosing mosques and gathering family.
The passage provides a rule for choosing between mosques.
5
Note cross-madhhab differences
Compare with other schools (Shafi'i, Maliki, Hanbali) who differ on the obligation level.
The Hanafi position is mukhtalaf fih.

يختار أقدمهما، فإن استويا فالأقرب، فإن صلوا في الأقرب وسمع إقامة غيره فإن كان دخل فيه لا يخرج وإلا فيذهب إليه. وهذا على الإطلاق تفريع على أفضلية الأقرب على من فضل الجامع، فلو كان الرجل متفقهاً فمجلس أستاذه لدرسه أو مجلس العامة أفضل بالاتفاق .اهـ. وأما حكمة مشروعيتها فقد ذكر في ذلك وجوه : أحدها قيام نظام الألفة بين المصلين ولهذه الحكمة شرعت المساجد في المحال لتحصيل التعاهد باللقاء في أوقات الصلوات It is led. And he carries it according to Abu Hanifa because it is known that there is no consideration for the ability of another, and it is verified in Fath al-Qadir that it is agreement, and the disagreement is in Jumu'ah, not congregation. And it is excused due to extreme cold and intense darkness. And it is mentioned in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj that among them are rain and wind in a dark night; but in the daytime wind is not an excuse. Likewise if he is suppressing the two impurities or one of them, or if he fears that when he goes out his debtor would imprison him for debt, or he fears the dark, or he wants to travel and prayer is established and he fears missing the caravan, or he is attending to a patient or fears losing his property, and likewise if dinner is present and the 'Isha prayer is established and his soul yearns for it, and likewise if food is present at other than 'Isha time and his soul yearns for it. In Fath al-Qadir: If he misses it, he is not obligated to seek it in mosques without dispute among our companions; rather if he goes to another mosque for congregation that is good, and if he prays alone in his neighborhood mosque that is good. Al-Quduri mentioned: He gathers his family and prays with them, meaning he attains the reward of congregation. Shams al-A'immah said: The better in our time is to follow it. Al-Halwani was asked: Whoever gathers his family sometimes, does he attain the reward of congregation or not? He said: No, and it is innovation and disliked without excuse. So if a man is a scholar, then the gathering of his teacher for his lesson or the gathering of the public is better by agreement. End quote. As for the wisdom of its legislation, there are aspects: First, establishing the system of affection among the worshippers; for this wisdom mosques were legislated in the districts to achieve mutual care by meeting at prayer times among neighbors. Second, dispelling the constriction of the soul that engages in this worship alone. Third, the ignorant person learns from the scholar the actions of prayer. And some mentioned that it is established by the Book, namely His statement: 'And bow with those who bow' [al-Baqarah 2:43]; so it is by the Book and the Sunnah. As for its virtues, in the authentic Sunnah the prayer in congregation is more excellent than the prayer of the individual by twenty-some degrees. And in al-Mudmarat: It is written in the Torah the description of the nation of Muhammad and their congregation, and that for every man in their rows an extra prayer is added to his prayer, meaning if they are a thousand men, a thousand prayers are recorded for each man. Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq is a commentary on the text of Kanz al-Daqaiq regarding the excuses for missing congregational prayer. It begins by clarifying a previous point about leading and carrying, then lists numerous excuses that make it permissible to miss the obligatory (wajib) congregational prayer. The author draws from Fath al-Qadir, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, and other sources. Excuses include extreme cold, intense darkness, rain and wind at night (but not wind alone in daytime), needing to relieve oneself, fear of imprisonment, fear of missing a caravan, attending a patient, fear of losing property, and craving for food or drink at the time of prayer. After listing the excuses, the passage discusses the ruling on missing congregation: one is not obligated to search for another mosque; praying alone in one's neighborhood mosque is acceptable, though going to another mosque is better. It also addresses gathering one's family at home for prayer, with al-Halwani ruling it a disliked innovation without excuse. The passage then discusses the relative virtue of neighborhood mosque versus Friday mosque, and provides guidance on choosing between two mosques. Finally, it elaborates on the wisdom behind congregational prayer—fostering affection, relieving loneliness, and enabling learning—and its virtues, including the hadith of twenty-some degrees and a report from the Torah. The commentator concludes with a poetic verse summarizing twenty excuses, drawing from al-Tanwir and al-Durr al-Mukhtar.

Key Terms
الجماعة (al-jama'ah): Congregational prayer performed by at least two people (imam and follower) in the Hanafi school.
عذر (udhr): A legal excuse that allows missing an obligatory act, such as extreme cold, illness, fear, etc.
البرد الشديد (al-bard al-shadid): Extreme cold that causes hardship in attending congregation.

Prefeering Knowledge over Recitation for Imamah: The Hanafi Position
Intra-madhhab dispute over imamah qualifications

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on who is most qualified to lead prayer, explain the basis for preferring knowledge (a'lam) over recitation (aqra'), and apply the ruling to a contemporary scenario.

Core Idea
The imam's knowledge of prayer rulings outweighs perfect recitation – because one pillar needs recitation, but all need correct fiqh.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq, we examine the qualifications for leading the prayer. The matn states that the most knowledgeable (a'lam) is most entitled, followed by the best reciter. This order reflects a key intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf argued for the reciter, citing the famous hadith 'the most reciter should lead.' Abu Hanifa and the majority countered with evidence from the practice of the Companions and the scope of duties. The lesson unravels the proofs and establishes the mufta bihi position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling in the matn
The matn says: the most knowledgeable (a'lam) is most entitled, then the best reciter (aqra'), then the most pious (awra'), then the oldest (asann). This is the hierarchy.
The ruling is about preference (mandub), not obligation.
2
Understand what 'a'lam' specifically means
The commentator explains that 'a'lam' here means knowledge of the rulings of prayer (fiqh of salah) – what corrects and invalidates it. It does not mean general knowledge.
Some interpretations expand to 'most knowledgeable of the Sunnah' since salah rulings derive from Sunnah.
3
Contrast Abu Yusuf's objection
Abu Yusuf preferred the best reciter (aqra') based on the hadith in the Two Sahihs: 'The people should be led by the most reciter of the Book of Allah…'
This hadith is also followed by the Shafi'i school.
4
Analyze the Hanafi response from al-Hidayah
The response: The companions were simultaneously reciters and knowledgeable – the hadith applied to them. Today, a person may be a great reciter but lack fiqh. Also, recitation is only for one rukn (qira'ah) while knowledge covers all arkan and conditions.
Additional evidence: the hadith of Abu Bakr (who was less reciter but more knowledgeable) being ordered to lead.
5
Note the conditions and exceptions
The a'lam must avoid manifest sins, and the preference applies when the imam is not the resident imam (imam ratib). The a'lam should also have memorized at least the fard amount of Quran.
Opinions differ on minimum Quran memorization – some say sunnah amount, others say fard and wajib.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والأعلم أحق بالإمامة ثم الأقرأ ثم الأورع ثم الأسن وكره إمامة العبد والأعرابي قوله : (والأعلم أحق بالإمامة) أي أولى بها ولم يبين المعلوم، وفسره في المضمرات بأحكام الصلاة، وفي السراج الوهاج بما يصلح الصلاة ويفسدها، وفي غاية البيان بالفقه وأحكام الشريعة، والظاهر هو الأول ويقرب منه الثاني. وأما الثالث فمحمول على الأول لظهور أنه ليس المراد من الفقه غير أحكام الصلاة، ولهذا وقع في عبارة أكثرهم الأعلم بالسنة باعتبار أن أحكام الصلاة لم تستفد إلا من السنة . وأما الصلاة في الكتاب فمجملة، وقدم أبو يوسف الأقرأ لحديث الصحيحين «يؤم القوم اقرؤهم لكتاب الله، فإن كانوا في القراءة سواء فأعلمهم بالسنة، فإن كانوا في السنة سواء فأقدمهم هجرة، فإن كانوا في الهجرة سواء فأقدمهم إسلاماً، ولا يؤم الرجل في سلطانه ولا يقعد في بيته على تكرمته إلا بإذنه» وأجاب عنه في الهداية بأن اقرأهم كان أعلمهم لأنهم كانوا يتلقونه بأحكامه فقدم في الحديث ولا كذلك في زماننا فقدمنا الأعلم، ولأن القراءة يفتقر إليها الركن واحد والعلم لسائر الأركان وفي فتح القدير وأحسن ما يستدل به للمذهب حديث «مروا أبا بكر فليصل بالناس وكان ثمة من هو أقرأ منه بدليل قوله عليه الصلاة والسلام «اقرؤكم أبي» وكان أبو بكر أعلمهم بدليل قول أبي سعيد كان أبو بكر أعلمنا وهذا آخر الأمر من رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم. وفي الخلاصة : الأكثر على تقديم الأعلم فإن كان متبحراً في علم الصلاة لكن لم يكن له حظ في غيره من العلوم فهو أولى .اهـ. وقيد في المجتبى الأعلم بأن يكون مجتنباً للفواحش الظاهرة وإن لم يكن ورعاً. وقيد في السراج الوهاج تقديم الأعلم بغير الإمام الراتب، وأما الإمام الراتب فهو أحق من غيره وإن كان غيره أفقه منه . وقيد الشارح وجماعة تقديم الأعلم بأن يكون حافظاً من القرآن قدر ما تقوم به سنة القراءة، وقيده المصنف في الكافي بأن يكون حافظاً قدر ما تجوز به الصلاة، وينبغي أن يكون المختار قولاً ثالثاً وهو يكون حافظاً للقدر المفروض والواجب ولم أره منقولاً لكن القواعد لا تأباه لأن الواجب مقتضاه الإثم بالترك ويورث النقصان في الصلاة. أن والريح ليلاً ظلمة تمريض ذي ألم مدافعة لبول أو قذر ثم اشتغال لا بغير الفقه في بعض من الأوقات عذر معتبر قوله : (الحديث الصحيحين) أي البخاري ومسلم وهو مخالف لما في تخريج أحاديث الهداية للحافظ ابن حجر وإنه لم يعزه إلا لمسلم والأربعة، وكذا في فتح القدير قال : أخرجه الجماعة إلا البخاري واللفظ لمسلم. قوله : وأجاب عنه في الهداية (الخ) قال في فتح القدير : نظر فيه برواية الحاكم عوض «فاعلمهم بالسنة» (۱) رواه البخاري في كتاب الأذان باب ٥٤. أبو داود في كتاب الصلاة باب ٦٠. الترمذي في كتاب الصلاة باب ٦٠. النسائي في كتاب الإمامة باب ٣ ٥ ابن ماجه في كتاب الإقامة باب ٤٦. أحمد في مسنده (٤٨/٣، ٥١) (١١٨/٤، ١٢١).
And the most knowledgeable is most entitled to leadership, then the best reciter, then the most pious, then the oldest; and the imamah of a slave and a Bedouin is disliked. His statement: (And the most knowledgeable is most entitled to leadership) meaning he is most deserving of it. He did not specify what knowledge; and he interpreted it in al-Mudmarat as knowledge of the rulings of prayer, and in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj as what corrects prayer and invalidates it, and in Ghayat al-Bayan as fiqh and the rulings of the Shari'ah. The first is apparent and the second is close to it. As for the third, it is carried on the first because it is clear that by fiqh nothing other than the rulings of prayer is meant; for this reason the expression of most of them is 'most knowledgeable of the Sunnah' considering that the rulings of prayer are derived only from the Sunnah. As for prayer in the Book, it is summary. Abu Yusuf preferred the best reciter based on the hadith of the Two Sahihs: 'The people should be led by the most reciter of the Book of Allah; if they are equal in recitation, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah; if they are equal in Sunnah, then the earliest in hijrah; if they are equal in hijrah, then the earliest in Islam. And a man should not lead in his area of authority, nor sit in his house on his cushion of honour without permission.' Al-Hidayah responded that the most reciter among them was the most knowledgeable because they used to learn its rulings from it; thus the hadith gave precedence to them, but it is not so in our time, so we give precedence to the most knowledgeable. Also because recitation is needed for one pillar only, while knowledge is needed for all other pillars. In Fath al-Qadir, the best evidence for the madhhab is the hadith: 'Have Abu Bakr lead the people in prayer' when there was someone more reciter than him, evidenced by his statement 'the most reciter among you is Ubayy', and Abu Bakr was the most knowledgeable among them as evidenced by Abu Sa'id's statement that Abu Bakr was the most knowledgeable of them, and this was the last matter from the Messenger of Allah. In al-Khulasa: The majority prefer the most knowledgeable; if he is deeply versed in the science of prayer but has no share in other sciences, he is still preferable. End quote. In al-Mujtaba it is conditioned that the most knowledgeable must avoid manifest sins even if not pious. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, giving precedence to the most knowledgeable is restricted to other than the resident imam; the resident imam is more entitled than others even if others are more learned. The commentator and a group conditioned that the most knowledgeable should be a memorizer of the Qur'an to the extent of the sunnah amount of recitation, and the author in al-Kafi conditioned that he should memorize to the extent that prayer is valid with it. It should be that the chosen opinion is a third: that he memorizes the amount that is obligatory (fard and wajib); I have not seen it transmitted but the principles do not reject it because the obligatory requires sin for leaving and causes deficiency in prayer. That: and wind at night, darkness, nursing of a person in pain, suppression of urine or filth, then occupation not with other than fiqh in some times is a valid excuse. His statement: (the hadith of the two Sahihs) meaning Bukhari and Muslim, and it contradicts what is in Takhrij Ahadith al-Hidayah of al-Hafiz Ibn Hajar, that he only attributed it to Muslim and the four; likewise in Fath al-Qadir he said: The group recorded it except Bukhari, and the wording is Muslim's. His statement: And he responded in al-Hidayah (etc.). He said in Fath al-Qadir: He considered it with the narration of al-Hakim instead of 'the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah' (1). Recorded by Bukhari in the Book of Adhan, chapter 54; Abu Dawud in the Book of Salah, chapter 60; al-Tirmidhi in the Book of Salah, chapter 60; al-Nasa'i in the Book of Imamah, chapters 3, 5; Ibn Majah in the Book of Iqamah, chapter 46; Ahmad in his Musnad (3/48, 51) (4/118, 121).
Source pages p. 607

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Raiq deals with the qualifications for imamah. The matn states: the most knowledgeable (in fiqh of salah) is most entitled, followed by the best reciter, then the most pious, then the oldest. It also disapproves of a slave or Bedouin leading. The commentator explains what 'knowledgeable' means: knowledge of salah rulings, or of what corrects and invalidates salah, or fiqh generally. He clarifies that the term 'most knowledgeable of the Sunnah' is used because salah rulings come from Sunnah, not directly from the Quran. The central dispute is between Abu Hanifa (preferring the most knowledgeable) and Abu Yusuf (preferring the best reciter) based on the hadith 'the most reciter should lead'. Al-Hidayah responds that the companions were both reciters and knowledgeable, but today knowledge is separate, so we prefer the knowledgeable. Also, recitation is only one pillar while knowledge covers all. Further evidence is the hadith of Abu Bakr being preferred despite others being more reciter. Conditions are added: the knowledgeable person must avoid major sins, and the ruling applies to non-resident imams (the resident imam is always entitled). There is a discussion about the minimum Quran memorization required. An opinion suggests memorizing the fard and wajib portions. The passage ends with a note about excuses (probably a continuation from the previous lesson) and hadith references.

Key Terms
الأعلم (al-a'lam): The most knowledgeable in the rulings of prayer (specifically fiqh of salah), not necessarily general knowledge.
الأقرأ (al-aqra'): The best reciter of the Quran, i.e., one with superior tajweed and memorization.
الإمام الراتب (al-imam al-ratib): The permanent imam of a mosque who is entitled to lead regardless of others' qualifications.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is the primary qualification for leading the prayer?
A) Best recitation
B) Most knowledge of salah rulings (a'lam)
C) Earliest in hijrah
D) Most pious

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prefers the most knowledgeable in salah fiqh over the best reciter because knowledge covers all pillars, and the hadith of the most reciter is interpreted contextually.
