Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
The Order of Priority: Best Reciter, Most Pious, Oldest in Islam
Explaining the primary criteria and their order

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi order of priority for leading prayer (imamah) and explain the reasoning behind each criterion.

Core Idea
The imam should be chosen first for Quran recitation, then piety, then seniority in Islam — not for worldly knowledge or age alone.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains the criteria for who is most entitled to lead the congregation in prayer. The text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq lists four primary attributes: knowledge of rulings, good recitation, piety, and age. However, the commentary focuses on the order: first the best reciter (aqra'), then the most pious (awra'), then the oldest in Islam (asan). In this lesson, you will learn the precise definitions and the legal evidence for this order.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four criteria from the matn and their order as explained by the commentator.
Read the passage carefully to note that the order is aqra' (best reciter), then awra' (most pious), then asan (oldest in Islam). Knowledge (al-„ilm) is mentioned as a separate criterion earlier.
The matn itself lists knowledge first, but the commentary reorders based on the hadith.
2
Define each term: aqra', awra', asan — note the special meanings.
Aqra' can mean either most memorized or best reciter; Hanafi preferred is best reciter. Awra' means avoiding ambiguities (shubuhat), not just avoiding haram. Asan means earliest in Islam, not biological age.
The distinction between wara' and taqwa is important.
3
Locate the primary hadith (Malik ibn al-Huwairith) and understand how it proves the priority of the older in Islam when equal in other qualities.
The hadith says 'let the older of you lead' when the companions were equal in hijra, knowledge, and recitation. The commentary interprets 'older' as senior in Islam.
The hadith is the basis for asan criterion.
4
Note the displacement of hijra by wara' after the conquest of Makkah.
Hijra was originally a criterion but was abrogated; wara' takes its place. However, for a new Muslim in dar al-harb, hijra is still obligatory and may be considered.
This shows the evolution of criteria in early Islam.
5
Understand the distinction between wara' (avoiding ambiguities) and taqwa (avoiding prohibitions).
Wara' is a higher level of piety. The imam should avoid even doubtful matters to be safe.
This distinction is Hanafi-specific.

كتاب الصلاة - باب الإمامة
(ثم الأقرأ) محتمل لشيئين: أحدهما أن يكون المراد به أحفظهم للقرآن وهو المتبادر . الثاني أحسنهم تلاوة للقرآن باعتبار تجويد قراءته وترتيلها، وقد اقتصر العلامة تلميذ المحقق ابن الهمام في شرح زاد الفقير عليه قوله : (ثم الأورع أي الأكثر اجتناباً للشبهات . والفرق بين الورع والتقوى أن الورع اجتناب الشبهات والتقوى اجتناب المحرمات، ولم يذكر الورع في الحديث السابق وإنما ذكر فيه بعد القراءة الهجرة لأنها كانت واجبة في ابتداء الإسلام قبل الفتح، فلما انتسخت بعده أقمنا الورع مقامها . واستثنى في معراج الدراية من نسخ وجوبها بعده ما إذا أسلم في دار الحرب فإنه تلزمه الهجرة إلى دار الإسلام لكن الذي نشأ في دار الإسلام أولى منه إذا استويا فيما قبلها.

قوله : (ثم الأسن) لحديث مالك بن الحويرث أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال له ولصاحب له : إذا حضرت الصلاة فأذنا ثم أقيما ثم ليؤمكما أكبر كما وقد استويا في الهجرة والعلم والقراءة. وعلل له في البدائع بأن من امتد عمره في الإسلام كان أكثر طاعة، وهو يدل على أن المراد بالأسن الأقدم إسلاماً، ويشهد له حديث الصحيحين المتقدم من قوله «فإن كانوا في الهجرة سواء فأقدمهم إسلاماً» فعلى هذا لا يقدم شيخ أسلم قريباً على شاب نشأ في الإسلام أو أسلم قبله وكلام المصنف ظاهر في تقدم الأورع على الأسن، وهكذا في كثير من الكتب، وفي المحيط ما يخالفه فإنه قال : وإن كان أحدهما أكبر والآخر أورع فالأكبر أولى إذا ساكتاً الحال فأفقههم فقها وإن كانوا في الفقه سواء فاكبرهم سناً . ولو صح فإنما مفاده أن الأقرأ أعلم بأحكام الكتاب فصار الحاصل يؤم القوم اقرؤهم أي أعلمهم بالقراءة وأحكام الكتاب فإنهما متلازمان على ما ادعى، وإن كانوا في القراءة والعلم بأحكام الكتاب سواء فأعلمهم بالسنة، وهذا أولاً يقتضي في رجلين أحدهما متبحر في مسائل الصلاة والآخر متبحر في القراءة وسائر العلوم ومنها أحكام الكتاب إن التقدمة للثاني لكن المصرح في الفروع عكسه بعد إحسان القدر المسنون، والتعليل الذي ذكره المصنف يفيده حيث قال : لأن العلم يحتاج في سائر الأركان والقراءة لركن واحد، وثانياً يكون النص عن بين من انفرد بالعلم عن الأقرئية بعد إحسان المسنون ومن انفرد بالأقرئية عن العلم لا كما ظن المصنف فإنه لم يقدم الأعلم مطلقاً في الحديث على ذلك التقدير بل من اجتمع فيه الأقرئية والأعلمية اللهم إلا أن يدعي أنه أراد بلفظ الأقرأ الأعلم فقط أي الذي ليس بأقرأ مجازاً فيكون خلاف الظاهر، بل الظاهر أنه أراد الأقرأ غير أن الأقرأ يكون أعلم باتفاق الحال إذ ذاك، فأما المنفرد بالأقرئية والمنفرد بالأعلمية فلم يتناولهما النص فلا يجوز الاستدلال به على الحال بينهما كما فعل المصنف. قوله : (ولم أره منقولاً) قال في النهر أقول : ذكر في الدراية معزياً إلى المبسوط : الأعلم أولى إذا قدر على القراءة قدر ما يحتاج إليه، وهذا كما ترى صريح في اشتراط كونه حافظاً لمقدار الواجب أيضاً لظهور أنه يحتاج إليه في تكميل صلاته بل حفظ المسنون يحتاج إليه، أيضاً اهـ. أقول: باعترافه

كتاب الصلاة - باب الإمامة
لم يكن فيه فسق ظاهر .اهـ. وأشار المصنف إلى أنهما لو استويا في سائر الفضائل إلا أن أحدهما أقدم ورعاً ،قدم وقد صرح به في فتح القدير. ثم اقتصر المصنف على هذه الأوصاف الأربعة أعني العلم والقراءة والورع والسن، وقد ذكروا أوصافاً آخر. ففي المحيط : فإن استويا في السن قالوا أحسنهما خلقاً ،أولى، فإن استويا فأحسنهما وجهاً أولى. وفسر الشمني الخلق بالألف بين الناس، وفسر المصنف في الكافي أحسنهم وجهاً بأكثرهم صلاة بالليل للحديث من كثرت صلاته بالليل حسن وجهه «بالنهار وإن كان ضعيفاً عند المحدثين. وذكر في البدائع أنه لا حاجة إلى هذا التكلف بل يبقى على ظاهره لأنه صباحة الوجه سبب لكثرة الجماعة خلفه. وقدم في فتح القدير الحسب على صباحة الوجه، فإن استووا فأشرفهم نسباً . وزاد الإمام الاسبيجابي على ذلك أوصافاً ثلاثة أخرى وهي : فإن استووا فأكبرهم رأساً وأصغرهم عضواً، فإن استووا فأكثرهم مالاً أولى حتى لا يطلع على الناس، فإن استووا في ذلك فأكثرهم جاهاً أولى. وزاد في المعراج ثاني عشر وهو أنظفهم ثوباً. واختلف في المسافر مع المقيم قيل هما سواء وقيل المقيم أولى، وينبغي ترجيحه كما لا يخفى. وفي الخلاصة : وإن اجتمعت هذه الخصال في رجلين فإنه يقرع بينهما أو الخيار إلى القوم. وأشار المصنف بالأحقية إلى أن القوم لو قدموا غير الأقرأ مع وجوده فإنهم قد أساءوا ولكن لا يأثمون كما في التنجيس وغيره. وهذا كله فيما إذا لم يكونا في بيت شخص، أما إذا كانا في بيت إنسان فإنه يكره أن يؤم ويؤذن . وصاحب البيت أولى بالإمامة إلا أن يكون معه سلطان أو قاض فهو أولى لأن ولايتهما عامة كذا ذكر الاسبيجابي، ويشهد له حديث الصحيحين السابق. وفي السراج الوهاج : ويقدم الوالي على الجميع وعلى إمام المسجد، وصاحب البيت والمستأجر من المالك لأنه أحق بمنافعه وكذا المستعير أولى من المعير .اهـ. وفي تقديم المستعير نظر لأن للمعير أن يرجع أي وقت شاء بخلاف المؤجر. وفي الخلاصة وغيرها : رجل أم قوماً وهم له كارهون إن كانت الكراهية لفساد فيه أو لأنهم أحق بالإمامة يكره له ذلك، وإن كان هو حق بالإمامة لا يكره له ذلك .اهـ. وفي بعض الكتب والكراهة على القوم وهو ظاهر لأنها ناشئة عن الأخلاق الذميمة. وينبغي أن تكون تحريمية في حق الإمام في صورة الكراهة لحديث أبي داود عن ابن عمر مرفوعاً «ثلاثة لا يقبل الله منهم صلاة: من تقدم قوماً وهم له كارهون، ورجل أتى الصلاة دباراً. والدبار أن يأتيها بعد أن تفوته - ورجل اعتبد محوره» .
This is the chapter on prayer and the section on imamah. (Then the best reciter) can mean two things: one is the most memorizer of Quran, which is the apparent meaning; the second is the best in recitation in terms of tajweed and tartil. The scholar, student of Ibn al-Humam, limited it in Sharh Zad al-Faqir. He said: (Then the most pious) i.e., the one who avoids ambiguities most. The difference between wara' and taqwa is that wara' is avoiding ambiguities and taqwa is avoiding prohibitions. Wara' was not mentioned in the previous hadith; after recitation, hijra was mentioned because it was obligatory at the beginning of Islam before the conquest. When it was abrogated after that, we placed wara' in its place. An exception was made in Mi'raj al-Diraya from the abrogation of its obligation after that for one who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb, for hijra to dar al-Islam is obligatory on him, but one who grew up in dar al-Islam is more entitled if they are equal in what precedes.

His statement: (Then the oldest) due to the hadith of Malik b. al-Huwairith that the Prophet ﷺ said to him and his companion: 'When the time for prayer comes, give the adhan, then the iqama, then let the older of you lead the prayer,' and they were equal in hijra, knowledge, and recitation. It is explained in al-Bada'i' that whoever's life in Islam is long is more obedient, and this indicates that the intended meaning of 'oldsest' is the earliest in Islam. This is supported by the earlier hadith in the two Sahihs: 'If they are equal in hijra, then the most advanced in Islam.' Based on this, an old man who recently became Muslim is not preferred over a youth who grew up in Islam or became Muslim earlier. The author's statement is apparent in preferring the most pious over the oldest, and so in many books. But in al-Muhit there is something contradictory: it says if one is older and the other more pious, the older is more entitled if the situation is silent, then the most knowledgeable in fiqh, and if they are equal in fiqh then the oldest in age. If this is correct, it implies that al-aqra' is most knowledgeable of the rulings of the Book, so the result is: the people should be led by their best reciter i.e., the most knowledgeable of recitation and rulings of the Book, for they are inseparable as claimed. If they are equal in recitation and knowledge of the rulings of the Book, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah. This first of all would require that if there are two men, one proficient in matters of prayer and the other proficient in recitation and other sciences including rulings of the Book, the second is preferred; but the explicit position in al-Furu' is the opposite after performing the prescribed amount of recitation. The reasoning the author mentioned indicates it: he said because knowledge is needed for all pillars while recitation is for one pillar. Secondly, the text distinguishes between one who is exclusively knowledgeable without being a best reciter after performing the prescribed recitation, and one exclusively a best reciter without knowledge—not as the author thought, for he did not absolutely prefer the most knowledgeable in the hadith on that estimation; rather, one in whom both best recitation and knowledge are combined. Unless he claims that by 'aqra' he meant 'most knowledgeable' only, i.e., one who is not a best reciter metaphorically, which contradicts the apparent meaning. Rather, the apparent meaning is that he intended the best reciter, but the best reciter is knowledgeable by agreement at that time. As for one exclusively a best reciter and one exclusively knowledgeable, the text does not cover them, so one may not use it to deduce the ruling between them as the author did. His statement: (I did not see it transmitted) Al-Nahr says: It is mentioned in al-Diraya attributed to al-Mabsut: The most knowledgeable is more entitled if he can recite as much as needed. This, as you see, is explicit in requiring that he also memorize the obligatory amount, because he needs it to complete his prayer; even memorizing the sunna is needed. End. I say: By his admission...

Chapter: Prayer - Section on Imamah. There was no apparent sin in it. End. The author indicated that if they are equal in all other virtues except that one is more advanced in piety, he is preferred, and it is explicitly stated in Fath al-Qadir. Then the author limited it to these four attributes: knowledge, recitation, piety, and age. Others mentioned additional attributes: In al-Muhit: If they are equal in age, then the best in character is more entitled; then the best in face. Al-Shamni interpreted character as harmony among people. The author in al-Kafi interpreted 'best in face' as most in night prayer due to the hadith: 'One who prays much at night will have a beautiful face by day,' although it is weak according to hadith scholars. In al-Bada'i', it is said there is no need for this elaboration; rather, it remains on its apparent meaning because beauty of face causes many people to pray behind him. In Fath al-Qadir, lineage is given precedence over beauty of face; then if equal, the noblest in lineage. Imam al-Isbijabi added three more: if equal, then the largest head and smallest limbs; then the wealthiest, so that he does not look to the people; then the most influential. Al-Mi'raj added a twelfth: the cleanest in garment. There is difference regarding the traveler and the resident: some say they are equal, others say the resident is more entitled, and it should be preferred as is obvious. In al-Khulasa: If these characteristics are present in two men, then lots are drawn or the choice is left to the people. The author indicated by 'entitlement' that if the people advance someone other than the best reciter when he is present, they have done wrong but do not sin, as in al-Tanjis and others. This applies when they are not in someone's house. If they are in a man's house, it is disliked for him to lead and give adhan without permission. The owner of the house is more entitled to lead, unless there is a ruler or judge with him, for their authority is general. This is supported by the earlier hadith in the two Sahihs. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The ruler is given priority over all, including the mosque imam, the house owner, and the tenant from the owner, because he has more right to its benefits; similarly, the borrower is more entitled than the lender. The preference of the borrower is debatable because the lender can reclaim anytime unlike the lessor. In al-Khulasa and others: If a man leads people who dislike him: if the dislike is due to corruption in him or because they are more entitled to lead, it is disliked for him; if he is entitled to lead, it is not disliked. In some books, the dislike is on the people, which is apparent because it arises from blameworthy character. It should be considered prohibitively disliked (haram) for the imam in the case of dislike due to the hadith of Abu Dawud from Ibn Umar marfu': 'Three whose prayer Allah does not accept: one who leads people while they dislike him, one who comes to prayer after it is missed (dibar), and one who enslaves a free man.'
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the criteria for who is most deserving to lead the prayer (imamah). The author first discusses the meaning of 'al-aqra'' (the best reciter). Two interpretations are given: (1) the one who has memorized the most Quran, and (2) the one who recites best with tajweed and tartil. The commentator notes that the first is more apparent. Then he defines 'al-awra'' (the most pious) as one who avoids ambiguities (shubuhat), distinguishing wara' from taqwa (avoiding prohibitions). He explains that in earlier times, after recitation, hijrah was considered, but after the conquest of Makkah when hijrah was abrogated, wara' took its place. An exception remains for one who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb. Next, 'al-asan' (the oldest) is discussed with the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwairith that the older of two companions should lead if equal in hijrah, knowledge, and recitation. The commentator clarifies that 'oldest' here means the earliest in Islam, not in age, as supported by a hadith in the Sahihayn. The author of Kanz prioritizes piety over age, but al-Muhit contradicts this, stating that if one is older and the other more pious, the older should lead. A lengthy debate follows about whether 'al-aqra'' means best reciter or most knowledgeable of Quranic rulings. The commentator critiques the author of a prior work (possibly al-Marghinani) for incorrectly applying the hadith to prefer the most knowledgeable in all cases, arguing that the hadith only applies when a person combines both good recitation and knowledge. If a person is only knowledgeable without good recitation, he is not covered by the text. The passage then transitions to additional criteria beyond the four (knowledge, recitation, piety, age) that some scholars have mentioned, such as good character, handsome face, lineage, wealth, etc. It also discusses the traveler vs. resident priority and the ruling if the congregation dislikes the imam. According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if the people advance someone other than the most deserving, they have done wrong (asa'u) but do not sin. The imam should not lead if the dislike is due to his own deficiency or if others are more entitled. The hadith from Abu Dawud warns of severe consequences for those who lead while disliked. The overall lesson is that the criteria for imamah are detailed and intended to ensure the most qualified person leads, but the prayer remains valid even if a less qualified person leads, though it is disapproved.

Key Terms
الأقرأ (al-aqra'): The one who is best at reciting the Quran, either through memorization or quality of recitation (tajweed).
الأورع (al-awra'): The one who is most pious in avoiding ambiguous matters (shubuhat).
الأسن (al-asan): The one who is oldest in Islam (overall seniority in faith, not necessarily biological age).
الهجرة (al-hijra): Migration from dar al-harb to dar al-Islam, which was obligatory before the conquest of Makkah and later abrogated except for new converts in enemy territory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school as explained in this passage, who is given priority to lead the prayer after the one with the best Quran recitation (al-aqra')?
A) The most knowledgeable in fiqh (al-alam)
B) The most pious (al-awra')
C) The oldest in biological age
D) The one with the best character

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school prioritizes Quran recitation ability, then piety (avoiding ambiguities), then seniority in Islam for selecting the prayer leader.

The Meaning of Al-Aqra': Best Reciter or Most Knowledgeable?
Analyzing the intra-Hanafi dispute on the meaning of aqra'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to evaluate the Hanafi dispute on the interpretation of al-aqra' and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
The Hanafi school favours the best reciter as the primary imam, not the most knowledgeable of fiqh — knowledge can be supplemented.

This passage delves into a significant intra-Hanafi disagreement: does 'al-aqra'' mean the one with the best Quran recitation or the one most knowledgeable of the Quran's rulings? The author of Kanz al-Daqa'iq assumed the latter, but the commentator of Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq critiques this and reasserts the literal meaning. By studying this debate, you will sharpen your understanding of how Hanafi jurists derive rulings from textual evidence.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two interpretations of al-aqra' from the passage.
One interpretation is 'the one who memorizes the most Quran'; the other is 'the one who recites best with tajweed'. The commentator notes that the first is more apparent.
The passage also mentions a related debate: whether aqra' means best reciter or most knowledgeable of Quranic rulings.
2
Understand the author of Kanz's apparent view that aqra' means most knowledgeable.
The author (likely al-Marghinani) argued that aqra' includes knowledge of rulings, as recitation and knowledge are inseparable. He then used this to prefer the most knowledgeable imam.
This view is presented as the target of critique in the passage.
3
Follow the commentator's critique using the hadith and reasoning.
The commentator argues that the hadith literally refers to recitation ability. He points out that the author's reasoning would require that one who is only knowledgeable (but not a good reciter) is not covered by the hadith, so the hadith cannot be used to prefer him over a better reciter.
This is a classic example of distinguishing between the literal meaning (dalala) and an inferred meaning.
4
Recognize the thamarah al-khilaf: practical difference of this dispute.
If the best reciter is weak in fiqh, does he still lead? According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, yes. The opponent's view would prefer a fiqh scholar even if his recitation is poor.
The difference matters when choosing an imam for a community.
5
Determine which view is mufta bihi and why.
The commentator favors the literal interpretation (best reciter), and this is the relied-upon position in the school. The text explains that the author of Kanz's view is a departure from the apparent meaning.
The mufta bihi is also supported by the majority of Hanafi books.

كتاب الصلاة - باب الإمامة
(ثم الأقرأ) محتمل لشيئين: أحدهما أن يكون المراد به أحفظهم للقرآن وهو المتبادر . الثاني أحسنهم تلاوة للقرآن باعتبار تجويد قراءته وترتيلها، وقد اقتصر العلامة تلميذ المحقق ابن الهمام في شرح زاد الفقير عليه قوله : (ثم الأورع أي الأكثر اجتناباً للشبهات . والفرق بين الورع والتقوى أن الورع اجتناب الشبهات والتقوى اجتناب المحرمات، ولم يذكر الورع في الحديث السابق وإنما ذكر فيه بعد القراءة الهجرة لأنها كانت واجبة في ابتداء الإسلام قبل الفتح، فلما انتسخت بعده أقمنا الورع مقامها . واستثنى في معراج الدراية من نسخ وجوبها بعده ما إذا أسلم في دار الحرب فإنه تلزمه الهجرة إلى دار الإسلام لكن الذي نشأ في دار الإسلام أولى منه إذا استويا فيما قبلها.

قوله : (ثم الأسن) لحديث مالك بن الحويرث أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال له ولصاحب له : إذا حضرت الصلاة فأذنا ثم أقيما ثم ليؤمكما أكبر كما وقد استويا في الهجرة والعلم والقراءة. وعلل له في البدائع بأن من امتد عمره في الإسلام كان أكثر طاعة، وهو يدل على أن المراد بالأسن الأقدم إسلاماً، ويشهد له حديث الصحيحين المتقدم من قوله «فإن كانوا في الهجرة سواء فأقدمهم إسلاماً» فعلى هذا لا يقدم شيخ أسلم قريباً على شاب نشأ في الإسلام أو أسلم قبله وكلام المصنف ظاهر في تقدم الأورع على الأسن، وهكذا في كثير من الكتب، وفي المحيط ما يخالفه فإنه قال : وإن كان أحدهما أكبر والآخر أورع فالأكبر أولى إذا ساكتاً الحال فأفقههم فقها وإن كانوا في الفقه سواء فاكبرهم سناً . ولو صح فإنما مفاده أن الأقرأ أعلم بأحكام الكتاب فصار الحاصل يؤم القوم اقرؤهم أي أعلمهم بالقراءة وأحكام الكتاب فإنهما متلازمان على ما ادعى، وإن كانوا في القراءة والعلم بأحكام الكتاب سواء فأعلمهم بالسنة، وهذا أولاً يقتضي في رجلين أحدهما متبحر في مسائل الصلاة والآخر متبحر في القراءة وسائر العلوم ومنها أحكام الكتاب إن التقدمة للثاني لكن المصرح في الفروع عكسه بعد إحسان القدر المسنون، والتعليل الذي ذكره المصنف يفيده حيث قال : لأن العلم يحتاج في سائر الأركان والقراءة لركن واحد، وثانياً يكون النص عن بين من انفرد بالعلم عن الأقرئية بعد إحسان المسنون ومن انفرد بالأقرئية عن العلم لا كما ظن المصنف فإنه لم يقدم الأعلم مطلقاً في الحديث على ذلك التقدير بل من اجتمع فيه الأقرئية والأعلمية اللهم إلا أن يدعي أنه أراد بلفظ الأقرأ الأعلم فقط أي الذي ليس بأقرأ مجازاً فيكون خلاف الظاهر، بل الظاهر أنه أراد الأقرأ غير أن الأقرأ يكون أعلم باتفاق الحال إذ ذاك، فأما المنفرد بالأقرئية والمنفرد بالأعلمية فلم يتناولهما النص فلا يجوز الاستدلال به على الحال بينهما كما فعل المصنف. قوله : (ولم أره منقولاً) قال في النهر أقول : ذكر في الدراية معزياً إلى المبسوط : الأعلم أولى إذا قدر على القراءة قدر ما يحتاج إليه، وهذا كما ترى صريح في اشتراط كونه حافظاً لمقدار الواجب أيضاً لظهور أنه يحتاج إليه في تكميل صلاته بل حفظ المسنون يحتاج إليه، أيضاً اهـ. أقول: باعترافه

This is the chapter on prayer and the section on imamah. (Then the best reciter) can mean two things: one is the most memorizer of Quran, which is the apparent meaning; the second is the best in recitation in terms of tajweed and tartil. The scholar, student of Ibn al-Humam, limited it in Sharh Zad al-Faqir. He said: (Then the most pious) i.e., the one who avoids ambiguities most. The difference between wara' and taqwa is that wara' is avoiding ambiguities and taqwa is avoiding prohibitions. Wara' was not mentioned in the previous hadith; after recitation, hijra was mentioned because it was obligatory at the beginning of Islam before the conquest. When it was abrogated after that, we placed wara' in its place. An exception was made in Mi'raj al-Diraya from the abrogation of its obligation after that for one who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb, for hijra to dar al-Islam is obligatory on him, but one who grew up in dar al-Islam is more entitled if they are equal in what precedes.

His statement: (Then the oldest) due to the hadith of Malik b. al-Huwairith that the Prophet ﷺ said to him and his companion: 'When the time for prayer comes, give the adhan, then the iqama, then let the older of you lead the prayer,' and they were equal in hijra, knowledge, and recitation. It is explained in al-Bada'i' that whoever's life in Islam is long is more obedient, and this indicates that the intended meaning of 'oldsest' is the earliest in Islam. This is supported by the earlier hadith in the two Sahihs: 'If they are equal in hijra, then the most advanced in Islam.' Based on this, an old man who recently became Muslim is not preferred over a youth who grew up in Islam or became Muslim earlier. The author's statement is apparent in preferring the most pious over the oldest, and so in many books. But in al-Muhit there is something contradictory: it says if one is older and the other more pious, the older is more entitled if the situation is silent, then the most knowledgeable in fiqh, and if they are equal in fiqh then the oldest in age. If this is correct, it implies that al-aqra' is most knowledgeable of the rulings of the Book, so the result is: the people should be led by their best reciter i.e., the most knowledgeable of recitation and rulings of the Book, for they are inseparable as claimed. If they are equal in recitation and knowledge of the rulings of the Book, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah. This first of all would require that if there are two men, one proficient in matters of prayer and the other proficient in recitation and other sciences including rulings of the Book, the second is preferred; but the explicit position in al-Furu' is the opposite after performing the prescribed amount of recitation. The reasoning the author mentioned indicates it: he said because knowledge is needed for all pillars while recitation is for one pillar. Secondly, the text distinguishes between one who is exclusively knowledgeable without being a best reciter after performing the prescribed recitation, and one exclusively a best reciter without knowledge—not as the author thought, for he did not absolutely prefer the most knowledgeable in the hadith on that estimation; rather, one in whom both best recitation and knowledge are combined. Unless he claims that by 'aqra' he meant 'most knowledgeable' only, i.e., one who is not a best reciter metaphorically, which contradicts the apparent meaning. Rather, the apparent meaning is that he intended the best reciter, but the best reciter is knowledgeable by agreement at that time. As for one exclusively a best reciter and one exclusively knowledgeable, the text does not cover them, so one may not use it to deduce the ruling between them as the author did. His statement: (I did not see it transmitted) Al-Nahr says: It is mentioned in al-Diraya attributed to al-Mabsut: The most knowledgeable is more entitled if he can recite as much as needed. This, as you see, is explicit in requiring that he also memorize the obligatory amount, because he needs it to complete his prayer; even memorizing the sunna is needed. End. I say: By his admission...

Chapter: Prayer - Section on Imamah. There was no apparent sin in it. End. The author indicated that if they are equal in all other virtues except that one is more advanced in piety, he is preferred, and it is explicitly stated in Fath al-Qadir. Then the author limited it to these four attributes: knowledge, recitation, piety, and age. Others mentioned additional attributes: In al-Muhit: If they are equal in age, then the best in character is more entitled; then the best in face. Al-Shamni interpreted character as harmony among people. The author in al-Kafi interpreted 'best in face' as most in night prayer due to the hadith: 'One who prays much at night will have a beautiful face by day,' although it is weak according to hadith scholars. In al-Bada'i', it is said there is no need for this elaboration; rather, it remains on its apparent meaning because beauty of face causes many people to pray behind him. In Fath al-Qadir, lineage is given precedence over beauty of face; then if equal, the noblest in lineage. Imam al-Isbijabi added three more: if equal, then the largest head and smallest limbs; then the wealthiest, so that he does not look to the people; then the most influential. Al-Mi'raj added a twelfth: the cleanest in garment. There is difference regarding the traveler and the resident: some say they are equal, others say the resident is more entitled, and it should be preferred as is obvious. In al-Khulasa: If these characteristics are present in two men, then lots are drawn or the choice is left to the people. The author indicated by 'entitlement' that if the people advance someone other than the best reciter when he is present, they have done wrong but do not sin, as in al-Tanjis and others. This applies when they are not in someone's house. If they are in a man's house, it is disliked for him to lead and give adhan without permission. The owner of the house is more entitled to lead, unless there is a ruler or judge with him, for their authority is general. This is supported by the earlier hadith in the two Sahihs. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The ruler is given priority over all, including the mosque imam, the house owner, and the tenant from the owner, because he has more right to its benefits; similarly, the borrower is more entitled than the lender. The preference of the borrower is debatable because the lender can reclaim anytime unlike the lessor. In al-Khulasa and others: If a man leads people who dislike him: if the dislike is due to corruption in him or because they are more entitled to lead, it is disliked for him; if he is entitled to lead, it is not disliked. In some books, the dislike is on the people, which is apparent because it arises from blameworthy character. It should be considered prohibitively disliked (haram) for the imam in the case of dislike due to the hadith of Abu Dawud from Ibn Umar marfu': 'Three whose prayer Allah does not accept: one who leads people while they dislike him, one who comes to prayer after it is missed (dibar), and one who enslaves a free man.'
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the criteria for who is most deserving to lead the prayer (imamah). The author first discusses the meaning of 'al-aqra'' (the best reciter). Two interpretations are given: (1) the one who has memorized the most Quran, and (2) the one who recites best with tajweed and tartil. The commentator notes that the first is more apparent. Then he defines 'al-awra'' (the most pious) as one who avoids ambiguities (shubuhat), distinguishing wara' from taqwa (avoiding prohibitions). He explains that in earlier times, after recitation, hijrah was considered, but after the conquest of Makkah when hijrah was abrogated, wara' took its place. An exception remains for one who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb. Next, 'al-asan' (the oldest) is discussed with the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwairith that the older of two companions should lead if equal in hijrah, knowledge, and recitation. The commentator clarifies that 'oldest' here means the earliest in Islam, not in age, as supported by a hadith in the Sahihayn. The author of Kanz prioritizes piety over age, but al-Muhit contradicts this, stating that if one is older and the other more pious, the older should lead. A lengthy debate follows about whether 'al-aqra'' means best reciter or most knowledgeable of Quranic rulings. The commentator critiques the author of a prior work (possibly al-Marghinani) for incorrectly applying the hadith to prefer the most knowledgeable in all cases, arguing that the hadith only applies when a person combines both good recitation and knowledge. If a person is only knowledgeable without good recitation, he is not covered by the text. The passage then transitions to additional criteria beyond the four (knowledge, recitation, piety, age) that some scholars have mentioned, such as good character, handsome face, lineage, wealth, etc. It also discusses the traveler vs. resident priority and the ruling if the congregation dislikes the imam. According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if the people advance someone other than the most deserving, they have done wrong (asa'u) but do not sin. The imam should not lead if the dislike is due to his own deficiency or if others are more entitled. The hadith from Abu Dawud warns of severe consequences for those who lead while disliked. The overall lesson is that the criteria for imamah are detailed and intended to ensure the most qualified person leads, but the prayer remains valid even if a less qualified person leads, though it is disapproved.

Key Terms
الأقرأ (al-aqra'): The one who is best at reciting the Quran, either through memorization or quality of recitation (tajweed).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the commentator's critique, why cannot the hadith 'yauummu al-qawma aqra'uhum' be used to prefer a person who is only knowledgeable (but not a good reciter) over a good reciter (who is less knowledgeable)?
A) Because the hadith is weak in transmission.
B) Because the hadith only applies to those who combine both qualities.
C) Because the hadith was abrogated.
D) Because the hadith refers to knowledge of fiqh, not recitation.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi interprets al-aqra' as the best reciter, overruling a minority interpretation that prioritizes knowledge of Quranic rulings.

Additional Criteria and Practical Rulings for Imamah
Discussing additional criteria and situational rulings for imamah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list additional criteria for imamah beyond the primary four and apply the rulings on who has priority in specific contexts (house, mosque, traveler).

Core Idea
After the primary criteria, many secondary qualities can tip the scale; the ultimate mufta bihi is to choose the best reciter with good character.

This passage expands beyond the four basic criteria to mention various additional attributes that scholars have considered, such as good character, handsome face, noble lineage, wealth, and even the size of one's head! It also addresses specific situations like the right of the house owner, the traveler vs. resident, and the serious issue of leading people who dislike the imam. This lesson will help you navigate the rich tapestry of criteria and apply them in real-world scenarios.

Guided Path
1
List the additional criteria mentioned by different scholars beyond the primary four.
From the passage, scholars added: good character (khuluq), handsome face (husn al-wajh), lineage (hasab), wealth (mal), influence (jah), cleanliness of garment, etc. Note the disagreement on the interpretation of 'handsome face'.
These are secondary and considered when primary criteria are equal.
2
Understand the ruling on the house owner's priority and the exception for the ruler.
The owner of the house where prayer is held is more entitled to lead, but a ruler or judge has general priority over everyone. The borrower vs. lender issue is also discussed.
This is based on hadith and the owner's right over his property.
3
Analyze the hadith on leading people who dislike the imam.
The hadith states that three types of people's prayers are not accepted, including one who leads a congregation that dislikes him. The dislike must be for a valid reason (such as the imam being corrupt or someone else more entitled).
The ruling is makruh tahrimi for the imam if he knows they dislike him without valid reason.
4
Note that if the congregation advances someone less entitled, they have done wrong but do not sin.
The author indicates that if the people choose a non-aqra' when aqra' is present, they have done wrong (asa'u) but do not sin, meaning it is makruh but not haram.
This shows the sunnah nature of the order.
5
Recognize that if all criteria fail, lots can be drawn or the people choose.
Al-Khulasa states that if all these qualities are present in two men, lots are drawn or the choice is left to the people.
This ensures fairness when distinction is impossible.

Source Text

كتاب الصلاة - باب الإمامة
(ثم الأقرأ) محتمل لشيئين: أحدهما أن يكون المراد به أحفظهم للقرآن وهو المتبادر . الثاني أحسنهم تلاوة للقرآن باعتبار تجويد قراءته وترتيلها، وقد اقتصر العلامة تلميذ المحقق ابن الهمام في شرح زاد الفقير عليه قوله : (ثم الأورع أي الأكثر اجتناباً للشبهات . والفرق بين الورع والتقوى أن الورع اجتناب الشبهات والتقوى اجتناب المحرمات، ولم يذكر الورع في الحديث السابق وإنما ذكر فيه بعد القراءة الهجرة لأنها كانت واجبة في ابتداء الإسلام قبل الفتح، فلما انتسخت بعده أقمنا الورع مقامها . واستثنى في معراج الدراية من نسخ وجوبها بعده ما إذا أسلم في دار الحرب فإنه تلزمه الهجرة إلى دار الإسلام لكن الذي نشأ في دار الإسلام أولى منه إذا استويا فيما قبلها.

قوله : (ثم الأسن) لحديث مالك بن الحويرث أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال له ولصاحب له : إذا حضرت الصلاة فأذنا ثم أقيما ثم ليؤمكما أكبر كما وقد استويا في الهجرة والعلم والقراءة. وعلل له في البدائع بأن من امتد عمره في الإسلام كان أكثر طاعة، وهو يدل على أن المراد بالأسن الأقدم إسلاماً، ويشهد له حديث الصحيحين المتقدم من قوله «فإن كانوا في الهجرة سواء فأقدمهم إسلاماً» فعلى هذا لا يقدم شيخ أسلم قريباً على شاب نشأ في الإسلام أو أسلم قبله وكلام المصنف ظاهر في تقدم الأورع على الأسن، وهكذا في كثير من الكتب، وفي المحيط ما يخالفه فإنه قال : وإن كان أحدهما أكبر والآخر أورع فالأكبر أولى إذا ساكتاً الحال فأفقههم فقها وإن كانوا في الفقه سواء فاكبرهم سناً . ولو صح فإنما مفاده أن الأقرأ أعلم بأحكام الكتاب فصار الحاصل يؤم القوم اقرؤهم أي أعلمهم بالقراءة وأحكام الكتاب فإنهما متلازمان على ما ادعى، وإن كانوا في القراءة والعلم بأحكام الكتاب سواء فأعلمهم بالسنة، وهذا أولاً يقتضي في رجلين أحدهما متبحر في مسائل الصلاة والآخر متبحر في القراءة وسائر العلوم ومنها أحكام الكتاب إن التقدمة للثاني لكن المصرح في الفروع عكسه بعد إحسان القدر المسنون، والتعليل الذي ذكره المصنف يفيده حيث قال : لأن العلم يحتاج في سائر الأركان والقراءة لركن واحد، وثانياً يكون النص عن بين من انفرد بالعلم عن الأقرئية بعد إحسان المسنون ومن انفرد بالأقرئية عن العلم لا كما ظن المصنف فإنه لم يقدم الأعلم مطلقاً في الحديث على ذلك التقدير بل من اجتمع فيه الأقرئية والأعلمية اللهم إلا أن يدعي أنه أراد بلفظ الأقرأ الأعلم فقط أي الذي ليس بأقرأ مجازاً فيكون خلاف الظاهر، بل الظاهر أنه أراد الأقرأ غير أن الأقرأ يكون أعلم باتفاق الحال إذ ذاك، فأما المنفرد بالأقرئية والمنفرد بالأعلمية فلم يتناولهما النص فلا يجوز الاستدلال به على الحال بينهما كما فعل المصنف. قوله : (ولم أره منقولاً) قال في النهر أقول : ذكر في الدراية معزياً إلى المبسوط : الأعلم أولى إذا قدر على القراءة قدر ما يحتاج إليه، وهذا كما ترى صريح في اشتراط كونه حافظاً لمقدار الواجب أيضاً لظهور أنه يحتاج إليه في تكميل صلاته بل حفظ المسنون يحتاج إليه، أيضاً اهـ. أقول: باعترافه

كتاب الصلاة - باب الإمامة
لم يكن فيه فسق ظاهر .اهـ. وأشار المصنف إلى أنهما لو استويا في سائر الفضائل إلا أن أحدهما أقدم ورعاً ،قدم وقد صرح به في فتح القدير. ثم اقتصر المصنف على هذه الأوصاف الأربعة أعني العلم والقراءة والورع والسن، وقد ذكروا أوصافاً آخر. ففي المحيط : فإن استويا في السن قالوا أحسنهما خلقاً ،أولى، فإن استويا فأحسنهما وجهاً أولى. وفسر الشمني الخلق بالألف بين الناس، وفسر المصنف في الكافي أحسنهم وجهاً بأكثرهم صلاة بالليل للحديث من كثرت صلاته بالليل حسن وجهه «بالنهار وإن كان ضعيفاً عند المحدثين. وذكر في البدائع أنه لا حاجة إلى هذا التكلف بل يبقى على ظاهره لأنه صباحة الوجه سبب لكثرة الجماعة خلفه. وقدم في فتح القدير الحسب على صباحة الوجه، فإن استووا فأشرفهم نسباً . وزاد الإمام الاسبيجابي على ذلك أوصافاً ثلاثة أخرى وهي : فإن استووا فأكبرهم رأساً وأصغرهم عضواً، فإن استووا فأكثرهم مالاً أولى حتى لا يطلع على الناس، فإن استووا في ذلك فأكثرهم جاهاً أولى. وزاد في المعراج ثاني عشر وهو أنظفهم ثوباً. واختلف في المسافر مع المقيم قيل هما سواء وقيل المقيم أولى، وينبغي ترجيحه كما لا يخفى. وفي الخلاصة : وإن اجتمعت هذه الخصال في رجلين فإنه يقرع بينهما أو الخيار إلى القوم. وأشار المصنف بالأحقية إلى أن القوم لو قدموا غير الأقرأ مع وجوده فإنهم قد أساءوا ولكن لا يأثمون كما في التنجيس وغيره. وهذا كله فيما إذا لم يكونا في بيت شخص، أما إذا كانا في بيت إنسان فإنه يكره أن يؤم ويؤذن . وصاحب البيت أولى بالإمامة إلا أن يكون معه سلطان أو قاض فهو أولى لأن ولايتهما عامة كذا ذكر الاسبيجابي، ويشهد له حديث الصحيحين السابق. وفي السراج الوهاج : ويقدم الوالي على الجميع وعلى إمام المسجد، وصاحب البيت والمستأجر من المالك لأنه أحق بمنافعه وكذا المستعير أولى من المعير .اهـ. وفي تقديم المستعير نظر لأن للمعير أن يرجع أي وقت شاء بخلاف المؤجر. وفي الخلاصة وغيرها : رجل أم قوماً وهم له كارهون إن كانت الكراهية لفساد فيه أو لأنهم أحق بالإمامة يكره له ذلك، وإن كان هو حق بالإمامة لا يكره له ذلك .اهـ. وفي بعض الكتب والكراهة على القوم وهو ظاهر لأنها ناشئة عن الأخلاق الذميمة. وينبغي أن تكون تحريمية في حق الإمام في صورة الكراهة لحديث أبي داود عن ابن عمر مرفوعاً «ثلاثة لا يقبل الله منهم صلاة: من تقدم قوماً وهم له كارهون، ورجل أتى الصلاة دباراً. والدبار أن يأتيها بعد أن تفوته - ورجل اعتبد محوره» .
This is the chapter on prayer and the section on imamah. (Then the best reciter) can mean two things: one is the most memorizer of Quran, which is the apparent meaning; the second is the best in recitation in terms of tajweed and tartil. The scholar, student of Ibn al-Humam, limited it in Sharh Zad al-Faqir. He said: (Then the most pious) i.e., the one who avoids ambiguities most. The difference between wara' and taqwa is that wara' is avoiding ambiguities and taqwa is avoiding prohibitions. Wara' was not mentioned in the previous hadith; after recitation, hijra was mentioned because it was obligatory at the beginning of Islam before the conquest. When it was abrogated after that, we placed wara' in its place. An exception was made in Mi'raj al-Diraya from the abrogation of its obligation after that for one who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb, for hijra to dar al-Islam is obligatory on him, but one who grew up in dar al-Islam is more entitled if they are equal in what precedes.

His statement: (Then the oldest) due to the hadith of Malik b. al-Huwairith that the Prophet ﷺ said to him and his companion: 'When the time for prayer comes, give the adhan, then the iqama, then let the older of you lead the prayer,' and they were equal in hijra, knowledge, and recitation. It is explained in al-Bada'i' that whoever's life in Islam is long is more obedient, and this indicates that the intended meaning of 'oldsest' is the earliest in Islam. This is supported by the earlier hadith in the two Sahihs: 'If they are equal in hijra, then the most advanced in Islam.' Based on this, an old man who recently became Muslim is not preferred over a youth who grew up in Islam or became Muslim earlier. The author's statement is apparent in preferring the most pious over the oldest, and so in many books. But in al-Muhit there is something contradictory: it says if one is older and the other more pious, the older is more entitled if the situation is silent, then the most knowledgeable in fiqh, and if they are equal in fiqh then the oldest in age. If this is correct, it implies that al-aqra' is most knowledgeable of the rulings of the Book, so the result is: the people should be led by their best reciter i.e., the most knowledgeable of recitation and rulings of the Book, for they are inseparable as claimed. If they are equal in recitation and knowledge of the rulings of the Book, then the most knowledgeable of the Sunnah. This first of all would require that if there are two men, one proficient in matters of prayer and the other proficient in recitation and other sciences including rulings of the Book, the second is preferred; but the explicit position in al-Furu' is the opposite after performing the prescribed amount of recitation. The reasoning the author mentioned indicates it: he said because knowledge is needed for all pillars while recitation is for one pillar. Secondly, the text distinguishes between one who is exclusively knowledgeable without being a best reciter after performing the prescribed recitation, and one exclusively a best reciter without knowledge—not as the author thought, for he did not absolutely prefer the most knowledgeable in the hadith on that estimation; rather, one in whom both best recitation and knowledge are combined. Unless he claims that by 'aqra' he meant 'most knowledgeable' only, i.e., one who is not a best reciter metaphorically, which contradicts the apparent meaning. Rather, the apparent meaning is that he intended the best reciter, but the best reciter is knowledgeable by agreement at that time. As for one exclusively a best reciter and one exclusively knowledgeable, the text does not cover them, so one may not use it to deduce the ruling between them as the author did. His statement: (I did not see it transmitted) Al-Nahr says: It is mentioned in al-Diraya attributed to al-Mabsut: The most knowledgeable is more entitled if he can recite as much as needed. This, as you see, is explicit in requiring that he also memorize the obligatory amount, because he needs it to complete his prayer; even memorizing the sunna is needed. End. I say: By his admission...

Chapter: Prayer - Section on Imamah. There was no apparent sin in it. End. The author indicated that if they are equal in all other virtues except that one is more advanced in piety, he is preferred, and it is explicitly stated in Fath al-Qadir. Then the author limited it to these four attributes: knowledge, recitation, piety, and age. Others mentioned additional attributes: In al-Muhit: If they are equal in age, then the best in character is more entitled; then the best in face. Al-Shamni interpreted character as harmony among people. The author in al-Kafi interpreted 'best in face' as most in night prayer due to the hadith: 'One who prays much at night will have a beautiful face by day,' although it is weak according to hadith scholars. In al-Bada'i', it is said there is no need for this elaboration; rather, it remains on its apparent meaning because beauty of face causes many people to pray behind him. In Fath al-Qadir, lineage is given precedence over beauty of face; then if equal, the noblest in lineage. Imam al-Isbijabi added three more: if equal, then the largest head and smallest limbs; then the wealthiest, so that he does not look to the people; then the most influential. Al-Mi'raj added a twelfth: the cleanest in garment. There is difference regarding the traveler and the resident: some say they are equal, others say the resident is more entitled, and it should be preferred as is obvious. In al-Khulasa: If these characteristics are present in two men, then lots are drawn or the choice is left to the people. The author indicated by 'entitlement' that if the people advance someone other than the best reciter when he is present, they have done wrong but do not sin, as in al-Tanjis and others. This applies when they are not in someone's house. If they are in a man's house, it is disliked for him to lead and give adhan without permission. The owner of the house is more entitled to lead, unless there is a ruler or judge with him, for their authority is general. This is supported by the earlier hadith in the two Sahihs. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The ruler is given priority over all, including the mosque imam, the house owner, and the tenant from the owner, because he has more right to its benefits; similarly, the borrower is more entitled than the lender. The preference of the borrower is debatable because the lender can reclaim anytime unlike the lessor. In al-Khulasa and others: If a man leads people who dislike him: if the dislike is due to corruption in him or because they are more entitled to lead, it is disliked for him; if he is entitled to lead, it is not disliked. In some books, the dislike is on the people, which is apparent because it arises from blameworthy character. It should be considered prohibitively disliked (haram) for the imam in the case of dislike due to the hadith of Abu Dawud from Ibn Umar marfu': 'Three whose prayer Allah does not accept: one who leads people while they dislike him, one who comes to prayer after it is missed (dibar), and one who enslaves a free man.'
Source pages p. 608

Commentary
This passage is an expansion (sharh) of the text of Kanz al-Daqa'iq on the criteria for who is most deserving to lead the prayer (imamah). The author first discusses the meaning of 'al-aqra'' (the best reciter). Two interpretations are given: (1) the one who has memorized the most Quran, and (2) the one who recites best with tajweed and tartil. The commentator notes that the first is more apparent. Then he defines 'al-awra'' (the most pious) as one who avoids ambiguities (shubuhat), distinguishing wara' from taqwa (avoiding prohibitions). He explains that in earlier times, after recitation, hijrah was considered, but after the conquest of Makkah when hijrah was abrogated, wara' took its place. An exception remains for one who becomes Muslim in dar al-harb. Next, 'al-asan' (the oldest) is discussed with the hadith of Malik ibn al-Huwairith that the older of two companions should lead if equal in hijrah, knowledge, and recitation. The commentator clarifies that 'oldest' here means the earliest in Islam, not in age, as supported by a hadith in the Sahihayn. The author of Kanz prioritizes piety over age, but al-Muhit contradicts this, stating that if one is older and the other more pious, the older should lead. A lengthy debate follows about whether 'al-aqra'' means best reciter or most knowledgeable of Quranic rulings. The commentator critiques the author of a prior work (possibly al-Marghinani) for incorrectly applying the hadith to prefer the most knowledgeable in all cases, arguing that the hadith only applies when a person combines both good recitation and knowledge. If a person is only knowledgeable without good recitation, he is not covered by the text. The passage then transitions to additional criteria beyond the four (knowledge, recitation, piety, age) that some scholars have mentioned, such as good character, handsome face, lineage, wealth, etc. It also discusses the traveler vs. resident priority and the ruling if the congregation dislikes the imam. According to the relied-upon Hanafi position, if the people advance someone other than the most deserving, they have done wrong (asa'u) but do not sin. The imam should not lead if the dislike is due to his own deficiency or if others are more entitled. The hadith from Abu Dawud warns of severe consequences for those who lead while disliked. The overall lesson is that the criteria for imamah are detailed and intended to ensure the most qualified person leads, but the prayer remains valid even if a less qualified person leads, though it is disapproved.

Key Terms
الخُلُق (khuluq): Character; specifically interpreted by al-Shamni as harmony/interpersonal skill.
الجاه (jah): Influence or social standing; mentioned by al-Isbijabi.
المستعير (al-musta'ir): The borrower; in context of borrowed house, he may lead over the lender.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, if a congregation dislikes their imam due to his bad character (fasid), what is the ruling for the imam?
A) It is sunnah for him to lead to reform them.
B) It is disliked (makruh) and may be prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi).
C) It is permissible and he should ignore them.
D) The prayer is invalid if he leads.

Key Takeaway
Beyond the primary four criteria, many secondary attributes can determine the imam, but the overriding principle is that the imam should lead willingly accepted by the congregation.

Salah — Prayer
beginner
8 min
Primary Criteria for the Most Entitled Imam
Ruling statement on imamate criteria

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the four primary Hanafi criteria for preferring an imam and apply the hierarchy to determine who should lead the prayer.

Core Idea
Knowledge, recitation, piety, age – the order is fixed; deviation is wrong but not sinful.

When choosing an imam for congregational prayer, the Hanafi school establishes a clear hierarchy of qualifications. The primary attributes are knowledge of rulings, best recitation of the Quran, piety, and age. This lesson examines the order and the legal effect of not following it.

Guided Path
1
Identify the four primary attributes
From the text, the author limited to four: knowledge (علم), recitation (قراءة), piety (ورع), and age (سن). List them in order.
Knowledge of fiqh rulings takes precedence.
2
Understand the basis for the order
Knowledge is first because the imam needs to know the rulings of prayer to correct errors. Then recitation because the Quran is a pillar. Then piety ensures the imam is a good role model. Age is a sign of maturity and respect.
This is the Hanafi position.
3
Recognize the ruling when the hierarchy is ignored
If the congregation chooses someone less qualified, they have done wrong (أساءوا) but do not sin (لا يأثمون). The prayer is still valid.
The act is makruh tanzihiy, not haram.
4
Apply to a scenario
Given two candidates: one is knowledgeable but less pious, the other is pious but less knowledgeable. Who should lead? Apply the hierarchy: knowledge first, so the knowledgeable one is preferred.
Unless the congregation unanimously agrees on the other.

There was no apparent sin. End. The author indicated that if two are equal in all virtues except one has more advanced piety, he is preferred, and this is stated in Fath al-Qadir. Then the author limited to these four attributes: knowledge, recitation, piety, and age. Others have mentioned additional attributes. In al-Muhit: if equal in age, they said the one with better character is preferred; if equal, the one with a better face is preferred. Al-Shumniyy interpreted character as affection among people. The author in al-Kafi interpreted 'best face' as one who prays more at night due to the hadith 'whoever prays a lot at night, his face becomes beautiful during the day' even if weak among hadith scholars. In al-Bada'i', it is said there is no need for this effort; rather it remains on its apparent meaning because beauty of face causes a large congregation behind him. In Fath al-Qadir, lineage is given precedence over beauty of face; if equal, then the most noble in ancestry. Imam al-Isbijabi added three more attributes: if equal, then the largest in head and smallest in limb; if equal, then the most wealthy to avoid looking at people; if equal, then the most prestigious. In al-Mi'raj, a twelfth is added: the cleanest in garment. There is disagreement regarding a traveler and a resident: some say they are equal, others say the resident is preferred, and preference should be given as is not hidden. In al-Khulasa: if all these characteristics are found in two men, then lots are drawn or the choice is left to the people. The author indicated by 'most entitled' that if the people bring forward someone other than the best reciter despite his presence, they have done wrong but do not sin, as in al-Tanqih and others. All this is regarding when they are not in someone's house. However, if they are in a person's house, it is disliked for him to lead and give adhan. The owner of the house has more right to lead unless there is a ruler or judge with him, for their authority is general, so mentioned al-Isbijabi, and the previous hadith from the two Sahihs witnesses it. In al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: The governor is given precedence over everyone and over the imam of the mosque, the owner of the house, and the tenant from the owner because he is more entitled to its benefits, and similarly the borrower is more entitled than the lender. End. Preferring the borrower is questionable because the lender can revoke at any time unlike the lessor. In al-Khulasa and others: If a man leads a people while they dislike him, if the dislike is due to corruption in him or because they are more entitled to lead, it is disliked for him; if he is entitled to lead, it is not disliked. End. In some books, the dislike is upon the people, which is apparent because it stems from blameworthy morals. It should be prohibitively disliked for the imam in cases of dislike due to the hadith of Abu Dawud from Ibn Marwi' raised: 'Three whose prayer Allah does not accept: one who leads a people while they dislike him, a man who comes to prayer after it is missed (dabar: coming after it is missed), and a man who enslaved his muhur (?)' as in Sharh al-Munyah.
Source pages p. 609

Commentary
This passage is part of the commentary on the chapter of Imamate. It discusses the criteria for determining who is most entitled to lead prayer. The author (Ibn al-Humam, the commentator on Kanz al-Daqa'iq) explains that the preferred imam is the one with knowledge of rulings, then the best reciter of Quran, then the most pious, then the oldest. However, other scholars added further criteria: good character, handsome face, noble lineage, large head, small limbs? (this last is obscure), wealth, prestige, cleanliness. There is also a discussion on traveler vs resident, and the case when the people choose someone less qualified – they do wrong but the prayer is valid and they are not sinful. The passage also covers the rule that the owner of a house is more entitled to lead in his house, unless a ruler or judge is present. It also discusses the situation where the congregation dislikes the imam: if the dislike is justified, it is disliked for the imam to lead; if the imam is entitled, the dislike is upon the congregation. The commentator suggests that leading in such a case is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) based on a hadith.

Key Terms
الأحق (al-ahaqq): The most entitled or most deserving person to lead prayer based on specific criteria.
الورع (al-wara'): Piety and scrupulousness in avoiding sins and doubtful matters.
الكراهة (al-karahah): Dislike; in this context it is typically tanzihiy (disliked) but in some cases tahrimiy (prohibitively disliked) if the dislike is based on valid grounds.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the primary Hanafi criteria for preferring an imam, which attribute takes precedence?
A) Age (سن)
B) Lineage (حسب)
C) Knowledge (علم)
D) Beauty of face (صباحة الوجه)

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi imamate hierarchy is fixed: knowledge, recitation, piety, age; deviation is wrong but not sinful and the prayer remains valid.

Additional Considerations and Special Cases for Imamate
Expansion on additional imamate criteria and special rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the secondary attributes for imamate and apply the rulings for special cases such as house owner, ruler, and congregation’s dislike.

Core Idea
Beyond the four primary criteria, character, face, lineage, and other traits matter; the house owner is preferred unless a ruler is present, and leading a disliking congregation is prohibitively disliked.

The Hanafi jurists expanded the criteria for imamate beyond the basic four to include attributes like good character, handsome face, noble lineage, wealth, and cleanliness. There are also special cases: the owner of a house is most entitled in his home, a ruler or judge takes precedence, and leading a congregation that dislikes him is prohibited in some cases. This lesson explores these nuances.

Guided Path
1
List the additional attributes mentioned by scholars
After the four primary attributes, scholars added: good character (حسن الخلق), handsome face (صباحة الوجه), noble lineage (شرف النسب), large head and small limbs (obscure), wealth (كثرة المال), prestige (جاه), cleanliness (نظافة الثياب). Understand that these are secondary – only considered if the primary are equal.
There is disagreement on some, but they are all from Hanafi sources.
2
Apply the rule for house owner
In a private home, the owner of the house is entitled to lead, unless a ruler or judge is present, in which case they take precedence due to general authority. It is disliked for the owner to lead when a ruler is present.
The hadith 'a man should not lead in his own house' is interpreted as dislike, not prohibition.
3
Apply the rule for ruler and governor
The ruler (sultan) or judge is given precedence over everyone, including the mosque imam and house owner. Their authority is general.
This ensures unity and respect for authority.
4
Evaluate the case of congregation’s dislike
If the congregation dislikes the imam due to a valid reason (corruption in him or they are more entitled), it is disliked for him to lead. If the dislike is for no valid reason, the dislike is on the congregation, not the imam. The imam leading such a congregation is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) based on a hadith.
The commentator says the hadith indicates the prayer of such an imam is not accepted.

Ruling on the Imamate of Disliked Individuals: Validity and Karahah Tanzihiyyah
Ruling with proof on disliked imams

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imamate of a fasiq, slave, bedouin, innovator, blind man, and illegitimate child, and explain the evidence and rationale for the dislike.

Core Idea
The imamate of a fasiq is valid but disliked; the dislike is non-prohibitory and removed if the imam is the best present.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains a key ruling: the imamate of certain individuals is valid but disliked. The commentator first affirms validity based on the fulfilment of prayer conditions and pillars, then provides evidence from hadith and practice of the Companions. The dislike is due to potential discouragement of congregation and is non-prohibitory (tanzihi), with important qualifications when the imam is the best available.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six categories of disliked imams
List the six types mentioned: slave, bedouin (a'rabi), fasiq, innovator (mubtadi'), blind, and illegitimate child (walad zina). Note that the dislike applies to each, but not absolutely.
The term a'rabi refers specifically to desert-dwellers, not all Arabs.
2
Distinguish validity from dislike
The commentator separates the two: validity (sihha) is based on ability to perform the pillars; dislike (karahah) is due to secondary reasons like lack of knowledge or care that may reduce congregational attendance.
Validity is unconditional; dislike is conditional and can be removed.
3
Examine the proofs for validity
The hadith 'Pray behind every pious and sinful person' and the practice of Ibn Umar praying behind Hajjaj, a notorious fasiq, establish validity. Also, blind Companions like Ibn Umm Maktum led prayer.
These proofs show that sinfulness or imperfection does not invalidate imamate.
4
Understand the rationale for dislike and its qualification
The dislike (karahah tanzihiyyah) is based on potential reduction of congregational reward and the imam's likely negligence. However, if the person is the best present, the dislike drops, as in the case of the blind man who was the most qualified in Medina.
This qualification applies to all six categories, not just the blind.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والفاسق والمبتدع والأعمى وولد الزنا وتطويل الصلاة وجماعة النساء فإن فعلن يقف

قوله : (وكره إمامة العبد والأعرابي والفاسق والمبتدع والأعمى وولد الزنا) بيان للشيئين الصحة والكراهة أما الصحة فمبنية على وجود الأهلية للصلاة أداء الأركان وهما مع موجودان من غير نقص في الشرائط والأركان. ومن السنة حديث «صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر وفي صحيح البخاري أن ابن عمر كان يصلي خلف الحجاج وكفى به فاسقاً كما قاله الشافعي. وقال المصنف : إنه أفسق أهل زمانه وقال الحسن البصري : لو جاءت كل أمة بخبيئاتها وجئنا بأبي محمد لغلبناهم. وإمامة عتبان بن مالك الأعمى لقومه مشهورة في الصحيحين، واستخلاف ابن أم مكتوم الأعمى على المدينة كذلك في صحيح ابن حبان. وأما الكراهة فمبنية على قلة رغبة الناس في الاقتداء بهؤلاء فيؤدي إلى تقليل الجماعة المطلوب تكثيرها تكثيراً للأجر، ولأن العبد لا يتفرغ للتعلم والغالب على الأعراب الجهل، والفاسق لا لأمر دينه، والأعمى لا يتوقى النجاسة، وليس لولد الزنا أب يربيه ويؤد به ويعلمه فيغلب عليه الجهل. أطلق الكراهة في هؤلاء وقيد كراهة إمامة الأعمى في المحيط وغيره بأن لا يكون أفضل القوم، فإن كان أفضلهم فهو أولى. وعلى هذا يحمل تقديم ابن أم مكتوم لأنه لم يبق من الرجال الصالحين للإمامة في المدينة أحد أفضل منه حينئذ ، ولعل عتبان بن مالك كان أفضل من كان يؤمه أيضاً. وعلى قياس هذا إذا كان الأعرابي أفضل الحاضرين كان أولى، ولهذا قال في منية المصلي : أراد بالأعرابي الجاهل وهو ظاهر في كراهة إمامة العامي الذي لا علم عنده، وينبغي أن يكون كذلك في العبد وولد الزنا إذا كان أفضل القوم فلا كراهة إذا لم يكونا محتقرين بين الناس لعدم العلة للكراهة والأعرابي من يسكن البادية عربياً كان أو عجمياً، وأما من يسكن المدن فهو عربي وفي المجتبى : وهذه الكراهة تنزيهية لقوله في الأصل «إمامة غيرهم أحب إلي . وهكذا في معراج الدراية. وفي الفتاوى : لو صلى خلف فاسق أو مبتدع ينال فضل الجماعة لكن لا ينال كما ينال خلف تقي ورع لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «من صلى خلف عالم تقي فكأنما صلى على خلف نبي قال ابن أمير :حاج ولم يجده المخرجون. نعم أخرج الحاكم في مستدركه مرفوعاً إن سركم أن يقبل الله صلاتكم فليؤمكم خياركم فإنهم ..
(فاكبرهم رأساً وأصغرهم عضواً لينظر ما المراد بالعضو وقد قيل في تفسيره بما لا ينبغي أن يذكر. قوله : (لأن للمعير أن يرجع الخ قال في النهر : هذا لا أثر له يظهر وسيأتي أن العارية تمليك المنافع كالإجارة لكن بلا عوض بخلافها وإذا رجع خرج عن موضوع المسألة. قوله : (وعلى قياس هذا الخ) وقوله وينبغي أن يكون كذلك في العبد الخ» قال في النهر أقول : هذا مبني على أن علة الكراهة غلبة الجهل فيهم. قال في الهداية ولأن في تقديم هؤلاء تنفير الجماعة. قال في الفتح: وحاصل كلامه الكراهة فيمن سوى الفاسق للتنفير والجهل ظاهر، وفي الفاسق أولى لظهور تساهله في الطهارة ونحوها اهـ. والظاهر أنهما علتان ومقتضى الثانية ثبوت الكراهة مع انتفاء الجهل لكن ورد في
The fasiq, innovator, blind, illegitimate child, prolonging prayer, and congregation of women if they do... He said: (And disliked is the imamate of the slave, the bedouin, the fasiq, the innovator, the blind, and the illegitimate child) Explanation of both validity and dislike. As for validity, it is based on the existence of qualification for prayer performing the pillars; these are present without deficiency in conditions and pillars. From the Sunnah is the hadith 'Pray behind every pious and sinful person' and in Sahih al-Bukhari that Ibn Umar prayed behind al-Hajjaj, and he was a fasiq enough, as al-Shafi'i said. The author said: He was the most sinful of his time, and al-Hasan al-Basri said: If every nation brought its evils and we brought Abu Muhammad, we would overcome them. The imamate of Utban ibn Malik al-A'ma for his people is famous in the two Sahihs, and the appointment of Ibn Umm Maktum the blind over Medina likewise in Sahih Ibn Hibban. As for dislike, it is based on people's lack of desire to follow these, leading to decrease of the congregation which is desired to be increased for more reward; and because the slave is not free for learning, and the majority of bedouins are ignorant, and the fasiq does not care about his religion, and the blind cannot avoid impurity, and the illegitimate child has no father to raise, discipline, and teach him, so ignorance dominates him. He made the dislike general for these, but restricted the dislike of the imamate of the blind in al-Muhit and others to when he is not the best of the people; if he is the best, then he is preferred. Upon this is understood the preference of Ibn Umm Maktum because there remained no man fit for imamate in Medina better than him then, and perhaps Utban ibn Malik was better than those he led. By analogy, if the bedouin is the best of those present, he is preferred; hence it is said in Munyat al-Musalli: He meant by bedouin the ignorant one, and it is apparent in the dislike of the imamate of the common person who has no knowledge. Similarly should be the case for the slave and illegitimate child: if they are the best of the people, there is no dislike as long as they are not looked down upon by people, due to absence of the cause for dislike. The bedouin is one who lives in the desert, Arab or non-Arab; those living in cities are 'Arabi. In al-Mujtaba: This dislike is tanzihi (non-prohibitory) because the original text says 'The imamate of others is more beloved to me'. Likewise in Mi'raj al-Diraya. In al-Fatawa: If one prays behind a fasiq or innovator, he obtains the virtue of congregation but not as much as behind a pious and scrupulous person, due to the hadith 'Whoever prays behind a learned and pious imam is as if he prayed behind a prophet' says Ibn Amir Haj, but the mukhrijun did not find it. Yes, al-Hakim in his Mustadrak narrated as marfu': 'If you want Allah to accept your prayer, let your best ones lead you, for they...' (Large in head and small in limb: to consider what is meant by limb, and it has been interpreted as something not to be mentioned. He said: (Because the lender can revoke) said in al-Nahr: This has no apparent effect, and it will come that 'ariyah is a transfer of usufruct like ijarah except without compensation, and if he revokes it leaves the subject of the issue. He said: (By analogy to this) and his saying: similarly for the slave etc.' He said in al-Nahr: I say: This is based on the cause of dislike being the predominance of ignorance among them. He said in al-Hidaya: And because in giving precedence to these is repelling the congregation. He said in al-Fath: The gist of his words: dislike for other than the fasiq is due to repelling and ignorance apparent, and for the fasiq it is more appropriate due to his apparent carelessness in tahara etc. End. And apparently there are two causes; the implication of the second is the establishment of dislike even if ignorance is absent, but it has been reported in...
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the statement that it is disliked (makruh) for a slave, bedouin, fasiq, innovator, blind man, and illegitimate child to lead prayer, and similarly for prolonging prayer or women leading. The commentator first clarifies that such imamate is valid (sahih) because these individuals fulfill the basic conditions and pillars of prayer. Evidence includes the hadith 'Pray behind every pious and sinful person' and the practice of Ibn Umar praying behind Hajjaj, who was a notorious tyrant. Additionally, the blind companions Utban ibn Malik and Ibn Umm Maktum led prayers. The dislike (karahah) is due to the potential reduction of congregation attendance, as people may be less inclined to follow such imams. However, this dislike is not absolute: if the person is the most qualified among the present, then their imamate is not disliked; it may even be preferred. The commentator also notes that the karahah is tanzihi (non-prohibitory) according to al-Mujtaba, based on the original text 'Imamate of others is more beloved to me'. Later, the passage includes additional marginal notes discussing the interpretation of 'large head and small limb' and the ruling on lender revoking, which are digressions from the main topic.

Key Terms
الفاسق (al-fasiq): A person who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking religious integrity.
الكراهة التنزيهية (al-karahah al-tanzihiyyah): A non-prohibitory dislike; the act is valid but leaving it is better.
الأعرابي (al-a'rabi): A desert-dweller, often ignorant of Islamic rulings.

Key Takeaway
The imamate of a fasiq, slave, bedouin, innovator, blind man, and illegitimate child is valid but non-prohibitively disliked; this dislike is removed when the imam is the best available.
