Imamate of Six Disliked Categories: Validity and Dislike
States ruling of validity and dislike for six imam categories

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on imamate of the slave, Bedouin, sinful, innovator, blind, and child of adultery, explaining the basis for validity and the nature of dislike.

Core Idea
Imamate of these six is valid but disliked; if the person is the best available, there is no dislike.

In the Hanafi school, the imamate of certain individuals is valid because they meet the basic conditions of prayer, but it is disliked due to reasons that may reduce the congregation's reward. This lesson explores the ruling for six specific categories—slave, Bedouin, sinful, innovator, blind, and child of adultery—based on the text from Al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. We will examine the evidence from hadith and the practice of the Companions, and understand when the dislike is removed.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six categories and the dual ruling
List the six types: slave, Bedouin, fasiq, mubtadi', blind, and child of adultery. Note that the commentary states both validity (sahih) and dislike (karahah).
The dislike is tanzihi, not tahrimi.
2
Understand the basis for validity
Validity is based on the imam's ability to fulfill the conditions and pillars of prayer. The hadith 'صَلُّوا خَلْفَ كُلِّ بِرٍّ وَفَاجِرٍ' and the practice of Ibn Umar praying behind al-Hajjaj are cited as proof.
The imperative 'صلوا' indicates permissibility, making the imamate valid regardless of the imam's piety.
3
Analyze the reasons for dislike
The dislike is due to potential negative impact on the congregation: these individuals may lack knowledge (slave, Bedouin, child of adultery), religiosity (fasiq, mubtadi'), or ability to avoid impurity (blind), leading to reduced attendance.
The goal of congregational prayer is to have a large gathering; this is undermined if the imam is unqualified.
4
Note the exception: no dislike if they are the best
If any of these individuals is the most knowledgeable, pious, and suitable imam available, the dislike is removed. Evidence includes the blind Companions 'Itban ibn Malik and Ibn Umm Maktum leading prayer.
The term 'Bedouin' here means ignorant; if a Bedouin is the best, he may lead without karahah.
5
Confirm the level of dislike
The dislike is tanzihi (makruh tanzih), not tahrimi, as stated in al-Mujtaba and Mir'aj al-Dirayah. The hadith 'من صلى خلف عالم تقي' shows that praying behind a pious imam brings greater reward, but the congregation reward is still attained.
The mufta bihi position is that the imamate is valid and disliked only if a better alternative exists.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الصلاة - باب الإمامة
والفاسق والمبتدع والأعمى وولد الزنا وتطويل الصلاة وجماعة النساء فإن فعلن يقف
يهتم
قوله : (وكره إمامة العبد والأعرابي والفاسق والمبتدع والأعمى وولد الزنا) بيان للشيئين الصحة والكراهة أما الصحة فمبنية على وجود الأهلية للصلاة أداء الأركان وهما مع موجودان من غير نقص في الشرائط والأركان. ومن السنة حديث «صلوا خلف كل بر وفاجر» وفي صحيح البخاري أن ابن عمر كان يصلي خلف الحجاج وكفى به فاسقاً كما قاله الشافعي. وقال المصنف : إنه أفسق أهل زمانه وقال الحسن البصري : لو جاءت كل أمة بخبيئاتها وجئنا بأبي محمد لغلبناهم. وإمامة عتبان بن مالك الأعمى لقومه مشهورة في الصحيحين، واستخلاف ابن أم مكتوم الأعمى على المدينة كذلك في صحيح ابن حبان. وأما الكراهة فمبنية على قلة رغبة الناس في الاقتداء بهؤلاء فيؤدي إلى تقليل الجماعة المطلوب تكثيرها تكثيراً للأجر، ولأن العبد لا يتفرغ للتعلم والغالب على الأعراب الجهل، والفاسق لا لأمر دينه، والأعمى لا يتوقى النجاسة، وليس لولد الزنا أب يربيه ويؤدبه ويعلمه فيغلب عليه الجهل. أطلق الكراهة في هؤلاء وقيد كراهة إمامة الأعمى في المحيط وغيره بأن لا يكون أفضل القوم، فإن كان أفضلهم فهو أولى. وعلى هذا يحمل تقديم ابن أم مكتوم لأنه لم يبق من الرجال الصالحين للإمامة في المدينة أحد أفضل منه حينئذ ، ولعل عتبان بن مالك كان أفضل من كان يؤمه أيضاً. وعلى قياس هذا إذا كان الأعرابي أفضل الحاضرين كان أولى، ولهذا قال في منية المصلي : أراد بالأعرابي الجاهل وهو ظاهر في كراهة إمامة العامي الذي لا علم عنده، وينبغي أن يكون كذلك في العبد وولد الزنا إذا كان أفضل القوم فلا كراهة إذا لم يكونا محتقرين بين الناس لعدم العلة للكراهة والأعرابي من يسكن البادية عربياً كان أو عجمياً، وأما من يسكن المدن فهو عربي وفي المجتبى : وهذه الكراهة تنزيهية لقوله في الأصل «إمامة غيرهم أحب إلي». وهكذا في معراج الدراية. وفي الفتاوى : لو صلى خلف فاسق أو مبتدع ينال فضل الجماعة لكن لا ينال كما ينال خلف تقي ورع لقوله صلى الله عليه وسلم «من صلى خلف عالم تقي فكأنما صلى على خلف نبي» قال ابن أمير :حاج ولم يجده المخرجون. نعم أخرج الحاكم في مستدركه مرفوعاً «إن سركم أن يقبل الله صلاتكم فليؤمكم خياركم فإنهم وفدكم فيما بينكم وبين ربكم»
The Book of Prayer - Chapter of Imamate. And the sinful, the innovator, the blind, and the child of adultery, and lengthening the prayer, and the congregation of women—if they do, they stand... His statement: (And disliked is the imamate of the slave, the Bedouin, the sinful, the innovator, the blind, and the child of adultery) is an explanation of two things: validity and dislike. As for validity, it is based on the existence of legal capacity for prayer by performing the pillars, and these exist without deficiency in conditions and pillars. And from the Sunnah is the hadith 'Pray behind every righteous and sinful person.' And in Sahih al-Bukhari, Ibn Umar used to pray behind al-Hajjaj—and suffice him as a sinful person, as al-Shafi'i said. And the author said: He is the most sinful of his time. And Hasan al-Basri said: If every nation came with its evil deeds and we came with Abu Muhammad, we would overcome them. And the imamate of 'Itban ibn Malik al-A'ma over his people is famous in the two Sahihs, and the appointment of Ibn Umm Maktum al-A'ma over Madinah likewise in Sahih Ibn Hibban. As for dislike, it is based on the lack of desire of people to follow these, leading to a decrease in the congregation, which is desired to be numerous for greater reward. For the slave does not spare time to learn, the Bedouin is mostly ignorant, the sinful does not care for his religion, the blind does not avoid impurity, and the child of adultery has no father to raise him, discipline him, and teach him, so ignorance dominates him. He made the dislike absolute in these, but restricted the dislike of the imamate of the blind in al-Muhit and others to when he is not the best of the people; if he is their best, then he is more deserving. And upon this is based the preference of Ibn Umm Maktum, because there remained none of the righteous men fit for imamate in Madinah better than him at that time, and perhaps 'Itban ibn Malik was the best of those he led. And by analogy, if the Bedouin is the best of those present, he is more deserving. For this reason, the author of Munyat al-Musalli said: He meant by Bedouin the ignorant one, and it is apparent in the dislike of the imamate of the common person who has no knowledge. And it should be likewise for the slave and the child of adultery if they are the best of the people: there is no dislike if they are not despised among the people, due to the absence of the cause for dislike. The Bedouin is one who lives in the desert, whether Arab or non-Arab; as for one who lives in cities, he is an Arab. And in al-Mujtaba: This dislike is tanzihi (disliked but not prohibited) because of his statement in al-Asl 'Imamate of others is more beloved to me.' And likewise in Mir'aj al-Dirayah. And in al-Fatawa: If one prays behind a sinful or innovator, he attains the virtue of congregation, but not as he would attain behind a pious and righteous person, due to the hadith 'Whoever prays behind a knowledgeable and pious scholar is as if he prayed behind a prophet.' Ibn Amir said: [Haj] and the compilers did not find it. Indeed, al-Hakim narrated in his Mustadrak as a marfu' hadith: 'If you wish that Allah accepts your prayer, then let your best among you lead you, for they are your deputation between you and your Lord.'
Source pages p. 610

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling of imamate for six categories of people: the slave, the Bedouin, the sinful (fasiq), the innovator (mubtadi'), the blind, and the child of adultery. The commentator first establishes that the imamate of all these is valid (sahih) because they meet the basic conditions and pillars of prayer. He supports this with evidence from hadith ('Pray behind every righteous and sinful person') and the practice of the Companions: Ibn Umar prayed behind al-Hajjaj despite his notorious sinfulness, and the blind Companions 'Itban ibn Malik and Ibn Umm Maktum led prayer. Then he explains the dislike (karahah) is due to practical reasons: these individuals often lack knowledge or religiosity, leading to a diminished congregation. However, the dislike is not absolute; if such a person is the most knowledgeable and pious among the congregation, then his imamate is not disliked and may be preferable. For example, if a blind man is the best qualified, he should lead. The passage also clarifies that 'Bedouin' here means an ignorant person, not a resident of cities. The dislike is tanzihi (not tahrimi), as stated in al-Mujtaba and other sources: 'Imamate of others is more beloved to me.' Finally, the passage notes that praying behind a sinful or innovator still earns the reward of congregation, though less than behind a pious imam, citing relevant hadith.

Key Terms
كراهة تنزيهية (karāhat tanzīhiyyah): Dislike that is not prohibited; the act is valid but discouraged.
فاسق (fāsiq): Someone who commits major sins or persists in minor sins, lacking religious commitment.
أعرابي (aʿrābī): A Bedouin living in the desert, often ignorant of religious rulings.

Key Takeaway
Imamate of the six categories is valid but disliked (makruh tanzih); the dislike disappears if the individual is the best qualified imam available.

Imamate of Fasiq and Mubtadi': Ruling and Degree of Dislike
Explains the ruling and conditions for imamate of fasiq and mubtadi'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying behind a fasiq or mubtadi', distinguish when imamate is invalid due to kufr innovation, and apply the mufta bihi view on the degree of karahah.

Core Idea
Prayer behind a fasiq or mubtadi' is valid but disliked; the dislike is tanzihi unless the innovation is kufr.

This lesson dives into the practical details of imamate when the imam is sinful or an innovator. The Hanafi school permits following such imams under certain conditions, but the degree of dislike (karahah) has been a point of discussion among later scholars. We will clarify the ruling for Jumu'ah versus other prayers, the preference for congregation over solitude, and the key distinction between innovations that constitute disbelief and those that do not.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and ruling
The passage addresses the ruling of praying behind a fasiq (sinful person) and a mubtadi' (innovator). First, note that the default ruling is validity (sihhah) with dislike (karahah). The specific conditions for Jumu'ah and other prayers are discussed.
The ruling is not outright invalidity; it is a matter of choosing better alternatives.
2
Analyze the proof (dalil)
The Hanafi position is based on prophetic hadith and practice of the Companions. The key proof is the hadith 'صَلُّوا خَلْفَ كُلِّ بِرٍّ وَفَاجِرٍ' (Pray behind every righteous and sinful person). This indicates permissibility.
The proof is from Sunnah ahad, which gives zanni thubut but sufficient for permissibility.
3
Examine the intra-Hanafi dispute
Al-Halabi argued that the karahah is tahrimi (prohibitory), while the majority (including al-Ramli) hold it is tanzihi (disliked but not sinful). The passage sides with the majority, stating 'ما هنا أوجه' (what is here is more appropriate).
The thamarah al-khilaf: tahrimi would make avoiding such imams obligatory; tanzihi only recommends seeking better, but following is valid without sin.
4
Define bid'ah and its categories
The passage defines bid'ah as an innovation contrary to received truth. It then lists specific beliefs that amount to kufr (e.g., Jahmiyyah, denying intercession) and those that are only bid'ah (e.g., preferring Ali without denying caliphate).
The critical distinction: if the innovation is kufr, imamate is invalid (la tajuz); otherwise, it is valid but disliked.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
For Jumu'ah: if multiple Jumu'ahs exist and one can transfer, it is disliked to follow a fasiq (mufta bihi). For other prayers: if another imam is available, one should seek him; otherwise, praying behind the fasiq is better than praying alone.
This shows a gradation: preference for better imams, but congregation is still meritorious even with a fasiq.

And the commentator and others mentioned that if the sinful person cannot be prevented, one prays Jumu'ah behind him, and for other prayers one moves to another mosque. And he gave the reason in al-Mi'raj that in other than Jumu'ah he can find another imam. So in Fath al-Qadir it is said: Upon this, it is disliked to follow him in Jumu'ah if there are multiple Jumu'ah prayers in the city, according to the saying of Muhammad, and it is the operative fatwa, because he has the means to transfer then. Then in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If you ask what is better: to pray behind these or alone? It is said: As for the sinful, prayer behind him is preferable due to what was mentioned in al-Fatawa as we previously stated. As for others, it is possible that praying alone is better because of their ignorance of the conditions of prayer, and it is possible that it is analogous to prayer behind the sinful; and the best is to pray behind someone else. So the conclusion is that it is disliked for these to step forward and it is disliked to follow them as a tanzihi dislike. If it is possible to pray behind someone else, that is better; otherwise, following them is better than praying alone. And it should be that the place of dislike is when someone else is present; otherwise, there is no dislike, as is not hidden. And the author pointed out that if a freed slave and a free-born person are present, the free-born person is more deserving, given equality in knowledge and recitation, as in al-Khulasa. As for the innovator, he is the one of innovation (bid'ah). And it is, as in al-Mughrib, a noun from 'ibtada'a al-amra' if he initiates and introduces it, like rafqah from irtifaq and khilfah from ikhtilaf; it prevailed for an increase in religion or a decrease. He defined it by al-Shamni as what is introduced contrary to the truth received from the Messenger of Allah, may Allah bless him and grant him peace, whether knowledge, action, or state, by way of some doubt and approval, and he makes it a straight religion and a straight path. The author made 'innovator' absolute, including every innovator who is of our qibla. But in al-Muhit, al-Khulasa, al-Mujtaba and others, it is restricted to when his innovation does not render him a disbeliever; if it renders him a disbeliever, then prayer behind him is not permissible. The wording of al-Khulasa is: In al-Asl, following the people of desires is permissible except for the Jahmiyyah, Qadariyyah, the extreme Rafidah, those who say the Quran is created, the Khattabiyyah, and the Mushabbihah. The summary is: If he is of our qibla and does not go to extremes in his desire to the extent that he is judged a disbeliever, prayer behind him is permissible and disliked. And prayer is not permissible behind one who denies the intercession of the Prophet (peace be upon him), or denies the noble scribes, or denies the vision (of Allah), because he is a disbeliever. And if he says 'He is seen by His majesty and greatness,' he is an innovator. The Mushabbih: if he says that Allah has a hand or foot like that of servants, he is a disbeliever; if he says He is a body not like bodies, he is an innovator. The Rafidi: if he prefers Ali over others, he is an innovator; if he denies the caliphate of Abu Bakr, he is a disbeliever. Whoever denies the Isra' from Makkah to Jerusalem is a disbeliever; whoever denies the Mi'raj from Jerusalem is not a disbeliever. And in Fath al-Qadir he added... And it is not hidden that what is here is more appropriate due to the evidence presented. Reflect on his statement: (al-Ghali) which in al-Fath is 'al-Ghaliyyah'. Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on imamate, focusing on practical details. It first addresses the fasiq (sinful) imam: for Jumu'ah, if no better imam is available, one may pray behind him; for other prayers, one should seek another mosque. This is based on the principle of necessity. For Jumu'ah, if multiple Jumu'ah prayers are held in the city and one can transfer, it is disliked to follow the fasiq (according to Imam Muhammad, the mufta bihi). The passage then compares congregational prayer behind such imams versus praying alone: for a fasiq, congregation is better; for others (like the ignorant), it may be better to pray alone if they lack knowledge. The overall conclusion is that it is tanzihi-makruh for these individuals to lead and for others to follow them, unless no better imam is available. If there is another possibility, one should pray behind a better imam; otherwise, following them is better than praying alone. The passage also notes that between a freed slave and a free-born person, the free-born is preferred if equal in knowledge. Then it defines the innovator (mubtadi'): one who introduces something new into the religion contrary to the received truth. The key distinction is whether the innovation amounts to kufr (disbelief). The passage lists specific groups and doctrines: e.g., Jahmiyyah, Qadariyyah, extreme Rafidah, etc., whose beliefs constitute kufr, making prayer behind them invalid. Other innovations (like preferring Ali without denying the caliphate) are considered bid'ah but not kufr, so prayer behind such a person is valid but disliked. Finally, it cites a dispute among later Hanafis: al-Halabi held that the dislike for fasiq and mubtadi' is tahrimi (prohibitory), while the preferred view (as indicated by al-Ramli) is that it is tanzihi, based on the earlier evidence.

Key Terms
بدعة (bidʿah): An innovation in religion introduced after the era of the Prophet, either as an addition or reduction, contrary to the received truth.
مبتدع (mubtadiʿ): A person who practices bid'ah, whose innovation does not necessarily make him a disbeliever unless it contradicts essential beliefs.
كراهة تحريم (karāhat taḥrīm): Prohibitory dislike; an act that is close to haram and sinful to perform.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi), what is the degree of karahah for praying behind a fasiq or mubtadi' whose innovation is not kufr?
A) Tahrimi (prohibitory dislike)
B) Tanzihi (light dislike)
C) There is no karahah; it is fully permissible
D) The prayer is invalid

Key Takeaway
Prayer behind a fasiq or mubtadi' is valid but disliked (tanzihi), and imamate is only invalid if the innovation amounts to kufr.

Salah — Prayer

8 min
Ruling on Praying Behind a Fasiq or Mubtadi' Imam: Karahah Tanzih and Preference for Congregation
Ruling on permissibility and dislike of following a fasiq/mubtadi' imam.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on praying behind a fasiq or mubtadi' imam, explain the difference between tanzih and tahrim karahah, and determine when congregation is preferred over praying alone.

Core Idea
Praying behind a fasiq or mubtadi' is permissible but disliked (makruh tanzih) when a better imam is available; otherwise, congregation is preferable.

In the Hanafi school, the imamah (leading of prayer) of a sinful or innovative person raises questions of validity and preference. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq clarifies that while such an imam's prayer is valid, it is disliked (karahah tanzih) to follow them if a more suitable imam exists. However, if no alternative is available, joining the congregation is better than praying alone. The text also addresses the specific case of Jumu'ah when multiple congregations are established.

Guided Path
1
Identify the subject and the default ruling
The passage discusses the imamah of a fasiq (open sinner) and a mubtadi' (innovator). The default ruling is that following them is permissible (ja'iz) but disliked (makruh). Determine the level of karahah according to the text.
The text explicitly says 'كراهة تنزيهه' (a tanzihi dislike), though some later authorities considered it tahrim.
2
Examine the conditions for karahah
The dislike is conditional on the availability of another imam. If a better imam is present, following the fasiq/mubtadi' is disliked. If not, there is no karahah, and following them is actually preferable to praying alone.
The passage states: 'وينبغي أن يكون محل كراهة الاقتداء عند وجود غيرهم وإلا فلا كراهة'.
3
Apply the ruling to Jumu'ah with multiple congregations
When multiple Jumu'ah prayers are established in a city, it is disliked to follow a fasiq imam because he can transfer to another congregation. This is based on Muhammad's (al-Shaybani) view and is the mufta bihi position.
The text cites Fath al-Qadir: 'يكره الاقتداء به في الجمعة إذا تعددت إقامتها في المصر على قول محمد وهو المفتى به'.
4
Weigh the preference between following a fasiq and praying alone
For a fasiq, the text says following him is better than praying alone, as per earlier fatwa. For others (like ignorant imams), it may be better to pray alone if they themselves are ignorant of prayer conditions.
The passage references al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: 'أما في حق الفاسق فالصلاة خلفه أولى... وأما الآخرون فيمكن أن يكون الانفراد أولى'.

Book of Prayer - Chapter of Imamate. And your duty among yourselves and between you and your Lord, and the commentator and others mentioned that if a sinful person (fasiq) cannot be prevented, one prays Jumu'ah behind him, and for other prayers he moves to another mosque. And it was reasoned in al-Mi'raj that for other than Jumu'ah he can find another imam. So he said in Fath al-Qadir: According to this, it is disliked to follow him in Jumu'ah if its establishment is multiple in the city, according to the saying of Muhammad, and that is the mufta bihi, because he is able to transfer then. ... Then in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If you ask: What is better, praying behind these or alone? It is said: As for the fasiq, praying behind him is preferable due to what was mentioned in the Fatawa as we have presented. As for others, it is possible that praying alone is better due to their ignorance of the conditions of prayer, and it is possible that it is analogized to praying behind a fasiq, and the best is to pray behind someone else. So the conclusion is that it is disliked for these to lead and disliked to follow them with a tanzihi dislike. If it is possible to pray behind others, it is better; otherwise, following is preferable to praying alone. And it should be that the place of dislike of following is when others exist; otherwise there is no dislike, as is not hidden. And the author indicated that if a freed slave and a freeborn gather, the freeborn is more entitled after equality in knowledge and recitation, as in al-Khulasa. As for the innovator (mubtadi'), he is the one of innovation, and it is, as in al-Mughrib, a noun from ibtada'a al-amr if he initiates it and innovates it, like al-rafqah from al-irtifaq and al-khilfah from al-ikhtilaf, and it prevails upon an increase in religion or a decrease from it. And al-Shumunni defined it as what is innovated contrary to the truth received from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, whether knowledge, action, or state, with a kind of doubt and approval, and it is made a upright religion and straight path. And the author made the innovator absolute, so it includes every innovator who is from the people of our qibla. It was restricted in al-Muhit, al-Khulasa, al-Mujtaba, and others that his innovation should not amount to kufr, for if it amounts to kufr, prayer behind him is not permissible. And the wording of al-Khulasa is: In principle, following the people of desires is permissible except the Jahmiyyah, Qadariyyah, extreme Rafidah, those who say the Quran is created, al-Khattabiyyah, and al-Mushabbihah. And its summary: if he is from the people of our qibla and has not gone to extremes in his desires such that he is judged a disbeliever, prayer behind him is permissible and disliked. And prayer is not permissible for one who denies the intercession of the Prophet, peace be upon him, or denies the noble scribes, or denies the vision (of Allah in the hereafter) because he is a disbeliever. And if he says 'He is seen by His majesty and greatness' he is an innovator. And the Mushabbih if he says that Allah has a hand or foot like that of servants, he is a disbeliever; if he says He is a body unlike bodies, he is an innovator. The Rafidi if he prefers Ali over others, he is an innovator; if he denies the caliphate of al-Siddiq, he is a disbeliever. Whoever denies the Isra' from Mecca to Jerusalem is a disbeliever; whoever denies the Mi'raj from Jerusalem is not a disbeliever. And in Fath al-Qadir he added the blind as a special text, and this is appropriate for their absolute and limited exception of the blind. His saying: (So the conclusion is that it is disliked...) al-Ramli said: al-Halabi mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that the dislike of advancing the fasiq and innovator is a dislike of prohibition (tahrimi), while the slave, Bedouin, son of fornication, and blind, the dislike regarding them is less than the dislike regarding those two. And it is not hidden that what is here is more appropriate due to what preceded of the proof. Reflect on his saying: (al-Ghali) which in Fath is 'al-Ghaliyah'. His saying: (its interpretation is that) regarding al-Siddiq in this ruling, and perhaps their meaning of denying the caliphate is denying their entitlement to the caliphate, which contradicts the consensus of the Companions, not denying their having the position. And he reasoned for not declaring him a disbeliever in his saying 'not like bodies' because it only involves applying the word 'body' to Him, which suggests deficiency, but he negated that with his saying 'not like bodies', so nothing remains but mere application, and that is a disobedience that becomes a cause for punishment due to what we said of suggestion, unlike if he said it as a likeness, for then he is a disbeliever. It is said he becomes a disbeliever by mere application also, and this is good, nay, it is more appropriate for declaring disbelief. So the conclusion is that he is a disbeliever in two phrases: 'He is a body like bodies' and 'He is a body', and he becomes an innovator in 'not like bodies'. Then he said: Know that the judgment of disbelief of those we mentioned from the people of desires contradicts what is established from Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i of not declaring unbelievers among the people of our qibla from the innovators all. This is interpreted as meaning that that belief itself is disbelief, so the speaker says what is disbelief even if he is not declared a disbeliever, based on his statement being an exertion of his capacity as a mujtahid seeking truth. But their categorical statement of the invalidity of prayer behind him does not validate this combination, unless by 'invalidity' they mean it is not lawful, i.e., not permissible to do, which does not contradict validity; otherwise it is problematic. And Allah knows best. Unlike the absolute name of body with likeness, for he is declared a disbeliever for his choice of applying what suggests deficiency after knowing it; if he negates likeness, nothing remains except carelessness and light treatment. And thus these branches are problematic with what is established from the mujtahids. The investigator Sa'd al-Taftazani in Sharh al-Aqa'id objected to the answer in Fath al-Qadir, because his reasoning in al-Khulasa regarding one who denies the vision and similar things as being a disbeliever repels this interpretation. So what is better is what he himself mentioned in the chapter of rebels: that these branches transmitted in the Fatawa regarding declaring disbelief were not transmitted from the jurists (i.e., the mujtahids). Rather, what is transmitted from them is not declaring disbelief of one who is from our qibla, such that they did not rule the Khawarij who make permissible the blood and wealth of Muslims and the reviling of the Companions as disbelievers, because it is due to interpretation and doubt. And no regard is given to other than the mujtahids. And it is mentioned in al-Musayarah that the apparent meaning of the saying of al-Shafi'i and Abu Hanifa is that none of them is declared a disbeliever, even if it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said to Jahm: 'Get out from me, O disbeliever', this is interpreted as being due to his likening, and this is the choice of al-Razi. And it is mentioned in its commentary by al-Kamal ibn Abi Sharif that not declaring them disbelievers is what is transmitted from the majority of theologians currently. That belief itself is disbelief, etc. al-Halabi said: Accordingly, what is transmitted must be interpreted as applying to other than the extreme Rafidah and those like them, because such people do not exert effort in ijtihad. For one who says that Ali is God or that Jibril made a mistake and the like of such nonsense is merely an innovator with pure whim, and he is worse than those who said 'We worship them only that they may bring us nearer to Allah.' So it is not plausible that the two great imams would not rule that they are among the most disbelieving of disbelievers. Rather, their speech is about someone who has a doubt in what he holds, even if what he holds is in reality in itself disbelief, like the denier of the vision, punishment of the grave, and the like of what is known in theology, and like the denier of the caliphate of the two shaykhs and the reviler of them, for it involves denial of definitive consensus, but they deny the authority of consensus by accusing the Companions, so they have a doubt in general, even if it is apparently invalid in view of evidence. So due to that doubt which...

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the ruling of imamah behind a fasiq (sinner) and a mubtadi' (innovator). The commentary first addresses the situation of a fasiq imam: when he cannot be prevented, one may pray Jumu'ah behind him, but for other prayers one should go to another mosque. This is because for other prayers, alternative imams are usually available. The text then discusses whether it is better to pray behind such imams or alone. For a fasiq, praying behind him is considered better than praying alone, as per earlier fatwa, because of the sin of abandoning the congregation. For others (like the ignorant), praying alone might be better if they themselves are ignorant of prayer conditions. The overall ruling: it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) for such people to lead and to follow them. If another imam is available, it is superior to pray behind him; if not, following them is superior to praying alone. The karahah only applies when someone else is available. Then the author mentions the preference of a freeborn over a freed slave if equal in knowledge and recitation. The main focus shifts to the mubtadi'. The definition of bid'ah is given from al-Mughrib and from al-Shumunni: innovation contrary to received truth. The ruling: if the innovation does not amount to kufr, prayer behind the innovator is permissible but disliked; if it does amount to kufr, it is not permissible. The text then details categories from al-Khulasa: certain groups (Jahmiyyah, Qadariyyah, extreme Rafidah, etc.) are excluded from permissibility if their beliefs render them kafir. There follows a discussion on which beliefs constitute kufr (e.g., denying the vision of Allah, denying intercession, likening Allah to creation in absolute terms, denying the caliphate of Abu Bakr, denying Isra') and which only make one an innovator (e.g., preferring Ali over Abu Bakr, saying Allah is a body unlike bodies, denying the Mi'raj from Jerusalem). The commentary then discusses a dispute: although the general principle from Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i is not to declare ahl al-qibla as kafir, these specific rulings appear to do so. The resolution is that such rulings are from later fatwa (not from the founding imams) or are based on the idea that the belief itself is kufr even if the person is not declared kafir due to some doubt or ta'wil. The text reconciles by stating that those who have no valid doubt (like the extreme Rafidah) are indeed declared kafir. The author sides with the view that the founding imams did not rule takfir of any ahl al-qibla due to their respect for the possibility of ijtihad, but later scholars made exceptions for those whose views are beyond any doubt, like deifying Ali. The passage concludes with a note that the discussion is subtle and requires careful study.

Key Terms
فاسق (fāsiq): A person who openly commits major sins or persists in minor sins, not necessarily kafir.
مبتدع (mubtadiʿ): One who holds a belief or practice that is innovated in religion contrary to the Sunnah. In this text, it includes various sects like Jahmiyyah, Qadariyyah, etc., as long as the innovation does not amount to kufr.
بدعة (bidʿa): An innovation in religion that increases or decreases from it, introduced after the Prophet's time. Specific definitions from al-Mughrib and al-Shumunni are quoted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, when is it disliked (makruh tanzih) to pray behind a fasiq imam?
A) Always, regardless of circumstances.
B) Only when another suitable imam is available.
C) Only in Jumu'ah prayer.
D) Never; it is always permissible without dislike.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, following a fasiq or mubtadi' imam is disliked (makruh tanzih) only when a better alternative is available; otherwise, congregation is preferred over praying alone.

Categories of Innovators and the Takfir Dispute
Detailed Hanafi categorization of innovators and the scope of takfir.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between innovations that render the person a kafir and those that do not, and explain the Hanafi reconciliation between the principle of not declaring ahl al-qibla kafir and specific takfir fatwas.

Core Idea
Not every innovator is a disbeliever; the Hanafi school distinguishes between innovation born of doubtful interpretation and that which is pure kufr.

The Hanafi school holds a nuanced position on innovations in 'aqidah. While the founding imams, Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i, maintained that no one from the people of the qibla should be declared a disbeliever due to innovation, later fatwa works list specific beliefs that constitute kufr (e.g., denying the vision of Allah, denying the caliphate of Abu Bakr). This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq attempts to reconcile these two positions by introducing the concept of shubha (doubt) and distinguishing between extreme innovators who have no valid interpretation and those who do. The lesson will guide you through the definitions, the categories of innovators, and the resolution of the apparent contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Define bid'ah according to Hanafi sources
Review the definitions from al-Mughrib and al-Shumunni. Understand that bid'ah is an innovation in religion, often characterized as an increase or decrease. The legal definition emphasizes being contrary to the truth received from the Prophet.
The passage quotes: 'البدعة اسم من ابتدع الأمر إذا ابتدأه وأحدثه... غلبت على زيادة في الدين أو نقصان منه.'
2
Identify the categories of innovators from al-Khulasa
The text lists specific sects: Jahmiyyah, Qadariyyah, extreme Rafidah, those who say the Quran is created, al-Khattabiyyah, al-Mushabbihah. It also gives a general rule: if the innovation does not amount to kufr, following is permissible but disliked; if it does, it is not permissible.
The categorization is based on whether the innovation reaches the level of kufr or remains as bid'ah.
3
Distinguish between beliefs that constitute kufr and those that are merely bid'ah
The passage provides a list: denying intercession, denying the scribes, denying the vision (ru'yat) → kufr. Saying Allah is a body unlike bodies → bid'ah. Saying Allah is a body like bodies → kufr. Denying the caliphate of Abu Bakr → kufr. Denying Isra' → kufr. Denying Mi'raj from Jerusalem → not kufr. Categorize each.
The key is whether the belief is equivalent to clear kufr or has a possible ta'wil.
4
Examine the tension between the principle of non-takfir and specific fatwa rulings
Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i are reported to not declare ahl al-qibla kafir due to innovation. Yet later works like al-Khulasa declare certain beliefs as kufr. The author reconciles by stating that the belief itself is kufr, but the person may not be declared a kafir if he has a doubt (shubha). However, extreme groups like the ghulat (exaggerators) have no valid shubha and are indeed kafir.
The text quotes Sa'd al-Taftazani and al-Halabi to support this reconciliation.
5
Conclude with the practical implication for imamah
If the imam's innovation is kufr, prayer behind him is invalid. If it is bid'ah, it is valid but disliked. The text sides with the early imams' principle that takfir of ahl al-qibla is avoided, but acknowledges that later fatwa lists are based on the actual beliefs of extreme groups.
The author's view is that the rulings of takfir in fatwa books are not from the mujtahids themselves but from later scholars.

Book of Prayer - Chapter of Imamate. And your duty among yourselves and between you and your Lord, and the commentator and others mentioned that if a sinful person (fasiq) cannot be prevented, one prays Jumu'ah behind him, and for other prayers he moves to another mosque. And it was reasoned in al-Mi'raj that for other than Jumu'ah he can find another imam. So he said in Fath al-Qadir: According to this, it is disliked to follow him in Jumu'ah if its establishment is multiple in the city, according to the saying of Muhammad, and that is the mufta bihi, because he is able to transfer then. ... Then in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: If you ask: What is better, praying behind these or alone? It is said: As for the fasiq, praying behind him is preferable due to what was mentioned in the Fatawa as we have presented. As for others, it is possible that praying alone is better due to their ignorance of the conditions of prayer, and it is possible that it is analogized to praying behind a fasiq, and the best is to pray behind someone else. So the conclusion is that it is disliked for these to lead and disliked to follow them with a tanzihi dislike. If it is possible to pray behind others, it is better; otherwise, following is preferable to praying alone. And it should be that the place of dislike of following is when others exist; otherwise there is no dislike, as is not hidden. And the author indicated that if a freed slave and a freeborn gather, the freeborn is more entitled after equality in knowledge and recitation, as in al-Khulasa. As for the innovator (mubtadi'), he is the one of innovation, and it is, as in al-Mughrib, a noun from ibtada'a al-amr if he initiates it and innovates it, like al-rafqah from al-irtifaq and al-khilfah from al-ikhtilaf, and it prevails upon an increase in religion or a decrease from it. And al-Shumunni defined it as what is innovated contrary to the truth received from the Messenger of Allah, peace be upon him, whether knowledge, action, or state, with a kind of doubt and approval, and it is made a upright religion and straight path. And the author made the innovator absolute, so it includes every innovator who is from the people of our qibla. It was restricted in al-Muhit, al-Khulasa, al-Mujtaba, and others that his innovation should not amount to kufr, for if it amounts to kufr, prayer behind him is not permissible. And the wording of al-Khulasa is: In principle, following the people of desires is permissible except the Jahmiyyah, Qadariyyah, extreme Rafidah, those who say the Quran is created, al-Khattabiyyah, and al-Mushabbihah. And its summary: if he is from the people of our qibla and has not gone to extremes in his desires such that he is judged a disbeliever, prayer behind him is permissible and disliked. And prayer is not permissible for one who denies the intercession of the Prophet, peace be upon him, or denies the noble scribes, or denies the vision (of Allah in the hereafter) because he is a disbeliever. And if he says 'He is seen by His majesty and greatness' he is an innovator. And the Mushabbih if he says that Allah has a hand or foot like that of servants, he is a disbeliever; if he says He is a body unlike bodies, he is an innovator. The Rafidi if he prefers Ali over others, he is an innovator; if he denies the caliphate of al-Siddiq, he is a disbeliever. Whoever denies the Isra' from Mecca to Jerusalem is a disbeliever; whoever denies the Mi'raj from Jerusalem is not a disbeliever. And in Fath al-Qadir he added the blind as a special text, and this is appropriate for their absolute and limited exception of the blind. His saying: (So the conclusion is that it is disliked...) al-Ramli said: al-Halabi mentioned in Sharh Munyat al-Musalli that the dislike of advancing the fasiq and innovator is a dislike of prohibition (tahrimi), while the slave, Bedouin, son of fornication, and blind, the dislike regarding them is less than the dislike regarding those two. And it is not hidden that what is here is more appropriate due to what preceded of the proof. Reflect on his saying: (al-Ghali) which in Fath is 'al-Ghaliyah'. His saying: (its interpretation is that) regarding al-Siddiq in this ruling, and perhaps their meaning of denying the caliphate is denying their entitlement to the caliphate, which contradicts the consensus of the Companions, not denying their having the position. And he reasoned for not declaring him a disbeliever in his saying 'not like bodies' because it only involves applying the word 'body' to Him, which suggests deficiency, but he negated that with his saying 'not like bodies', so nothing remains but mere application, and that is a disobedience that becomes a cause for punishment due to what we said of suggestion, unlike if he said it as a likeness, for then he is a disbeliever. It is said he becomes a disbeliever by mere application also, and this is good, nay, it is more appropriate for declaring disbelief. So the conclusion is that he is a disbeliever in two phrases: 'He is a body like bodies' and 'He is a body', and he becomes an innovator in 'not like bodies'. Then he said: Know that the judgment of disbelief of those we mentioned from the people of desires contradicts what is established from Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i of not declaring unbelievers among the people of our qibla from the innovators all. This is interpreted as meaning that that belief itself is disbelief, so the speaker says what is disbelief even if he is not declared a disbeliever, based on his statement being an exertion of his capacity as a mujtahid seeking truth. But their categorical statement of the invalidity of prayer behind him does not validate this combination, unless by 'invalidity' they mean it is not lawful, i.e., not permissible to do, which does not contradict validity; otherwise it is problematic. And Allah knows best. Unlike the absolute name of body with likeness, for he is declared a disbeliever for his choice of applying what suggests deficiency after knowing it; if he negates likeness, nothing remains except carelessness and light treatment. And thus these branches are problematic with what is established from the mujtahids. The investigator Sa'd al-Taftazani in Sharh al-Aqa'id objected to the answer in Fath al-Qadir, because his reasoning in al-Khulasa regarding one who denies the vision and similar things as being a disbeliever repels this interpretation. So what is better is what he himself mentioned in the chapter of rebels: that these branches transmitted in the Fatawa regarding declaring disbelief were not transmitted from the jurists (i.e., the mujtahids). Rather, what is transmitted from them is not declaring disbelief of one who is from our qibla, such that they did not rule the Khawarij who make permissible the blood and wealth of Muslims and the reviling of the Companions as disbelievers, because it is due to interpretation and doubt. And no regard is given to other than the mujtahids. And it is mentioned in al-Musayarah that the apparent meaning of the saying of al-Shafi'i and Abu Hanifa is that none of them is declared a disbeliever, even if it is narrated from Abu Hanifa that he said to Jahm: 'Get out from me, O disbeliever', this is interpreted as being due to his likening, and this is the choice of al-Razi. And it is mentioned in its commentary by al-Kamal ibn Abi Sharif that not declaring them disbelievers is what is transmitted from the majority of theologians currently. That belief itself is disbelief, etc. al-Halabi said: Accordingly, what is transmitted must be interpreted as applying to other than the extreme Rafidah and those like them, because such people do not exert effort in ijtihad. For one who says that Ali is God or that Jibril made a mistake and the like of such nonsense is merely an innovator with pure whim, and he is worse than those who said 'We worship them only that they may bring us nearer to Allah.' So it is not plausible that the two great imams would not rule that they are among the most disbelieving of disbelievers. Rather, their speech is about someone who has a doubt in what he holds, even if what he holds is in reality in itself disbelief, like the denier of the vision, punishment of the grave, and the like of what is known in theology, and like the denier of the caliphate of the two shaykhs and the reviler of them, for it involves denial of definitive consensus, but they deny the authority of consensus by accusing the Companions, so they have a doubt in general, even if it is apparently invalid in view of evidence. So due to that doubt which...

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq is an expansion on the ruling of imamah behind a fasiq (sinner) and a mubtadi' (innovator). The commentary first addresses the situation of a fasiq imam: when he cannot be prevented, one may pray Jumu'ah behind him, but for other prayers one should go to another mosque. This is because for other prayers, alternative imams are usually available. The text then discusses whether it is better to pray behind such imams or alone. For a fasiq, praying behind him is considered better than praying alone, as per earlier fatwa, because of the sin of abandoning the congregation. For others (like the ignorant), praying alone might be better if they themselves are ignorant of prayer conditions. The overall ruling: it is makruh tanzihi (disliked) for such people to lead and to follow them. If another imam is available, it is superior to pray behind him; if not, following them is superior to praying alone. The karahah only applies when someone else is available. Then the author mentions the preference of a freeborn over a freed slave if equal in knowledge and recitation. The main focus shifts to the mubtadi'. The definition of bid'ah is given from al-Mughrib and from al-Shumunni: innovation contrary to received truth. The ruling: if the innovation does not amount to kufr, prayer behind the innovator is permissible but disliked; if it does amount to kufr, it is not permissible. The text then details categories from al-Khulasa: certain groups (Jahmiyyah, Qadariyyah, extreme Rafidah, etc.) are excluded from permissibility if their beliefs render them kafir. There follows a discussion on which beliefs constitute kufr (e.g., denying the vision of Allah, denying intercession, likening Allah to creation in absolute terms, denying the caliphate of Abu Bakr, denying Isra') and which only make one an innovator (e.g., preferring Ali over Abu Bakr, saying Allah is a body unlike bodies, denying the Mi'raj from Jerusalem). The commentary then discusses a dispute: although the general principle from Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i is not to declare ahl al-qibla as kafir, these specific rulings appear to do so. The resolution is that such rulings are from later fatwa (not from the founding imams) or are based on the idea that the belief itself is kufr even if the person is not declared kafir due to some doubt or ta'wil. The text reconciles by stating that those who have no valid doubt (like the extreme Rafidah) are indeed declared kafir. The author sides with the view that the founding imams did not rule takfir of any ahl al-qibla due to their respect for the possibility of ijtihad, but later scholars made exceptions for those whose views are beyond any doubt, like deifying Ali. The passage concludes with a note that the discussion is subtle and requires careful study.

Key Terms
فاسق (fāsiq): A person who openly commits major sins or persists in minor sins, not necessarily kafir.
مبتدع (mubtadiʿ): One who holds a belief or practice that is innovated in religion contrary to the Sunnah. In this text, it includes various sects like Jahmiyyah, Qadariyyah, etc., as long as the innovation does not amount to kufr.
بدعة (bidʿa): An innovation in religion that increases or decreases from it, introduced after the Prophet's time. Specific definitions from al-Mughrib and al-Shumunni are quoted.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, which of the following statements makes a person an innovator (mubtadi') but not a disbeliever?
A) 'Allah has a hand like the hands of servants.'
B) 'Allah is a body unlike bodies.'
C) 'The Prophet's intercession is denied.'
D) 'Abu Bakr was not the rightful caliph.'

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school preserves the principle of not rashly declaring ahl al-qibla as kafir, yet applies takfir to extreme innovations that are beyond any doubt.

Salah — Prayer
advanced
8 min
Takfir of Ahl al-Qibla: Hanafi Rulings on Anthropomorphic Statements and Their Effect on Leading Prayer
Explaining Hanafi position on takfir of innovators and its impact on leading prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to STATE the Hanafi classification of three types of anthropomorphic statements regarding Allah's attributes and APPLY the criteria for takfir to determine the validity of prayer behind such individuals.

Core Idea
Takfir requires clear denial of necessary religion; ambiguous statements about Allah's attributes may be heresy but not always disbelief.

The Hanafi school carefully distinguishes between statements that constitute kufr and those that are mere innovation (bid'ah). This lesson examines three key phrases concerning Allah being a 'body' and their legal consequences. It also addresses the apparent tension between declaring such statements kufr while generally avoiding takfir of Ahl al-Qibla, especially regarding the validity of praying behind an imam who holds innovated beliefs.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three statements and their rulings
From the passage, extract the three phrases: 'Allah is a body like bodies', 'Allah is a body', and 'Allah is not like bodies'. Note that the first two are ruled as kufr (disbelief) and the third as bid'ah (innovation).
The relied-upon view makes the second also kufr, though some earlier Hanafis considered it only bid'ah.
2
Reconcile the rulings with the general Hanafi position on takfir
The passage explains that despite these statements being kufr in themselves, the speaker may have a valid interpretation (ta'wil) or be a mujtahid, so takfir is not automatically applied. The key principle is that takfir is reserved for denial of matters known necessarily from religion (ma'lum min al-din bi al-darura).
This reconciliation is based on intent and capacity for ijtihad.
3
Analyze the effect on leading prayer (imamah)
The passage states that prayer behind an innovator (ahl al-ahwa) or a Shafi'i (who differs in some subsidiary rulings) is valid if the imam observes the conditions and pillars according to the Hanafi school, though it is disliked (makruh). If the imam is declared a kafir, prayer behind him is invalid.
The ruling on Shafi'is is analogous to any follower of a different madhhab.
4
Examine the scope of takfir and qualifications
The text cautions against extreme takfir, noting even the Khawarij are not declared disbelievers due to their interpretations. However, those who reject clear fundamentals (e.g., denial of resurrection) are unequivocally kafir. The passage also refutes the idea that fatwas of takfir are scare tactics.
The later Hanafi position is to avoid takfir based on shubha (doubt).

حنيفة وإنما هي من تفريعات المشايخ كألفاظ لتكفير المنقولة في الفتاوى والله سبحانه هو الموفق . وفي جمع الجوامع وشرحه : ولا نكفر أحداً من أهل القبلة ببدعة كمنكري صفات الله تعالى وخلقه أفعال عباده وجواز رؤيته يوم القيامة، ومنا من كفرهم. أما من خرج ببدعته من أهل القبلة كمنكري حدوث العالم والبعث والحشر للأجسام والعلم بـ الجزئيات فلا نزاع في كفرهم لإنكارهم بعض ما علم مجيء الرسول به ضرورة اهـ . وفي البزازي في الفتاوى بما يطول ذكره فراجعه اهـ. قلت: ونص كلامه في باب الردة ويحكى عن بعض من لا سلف له أنه كان يقول : ما ذكر في الفتاوى أنه يكفر بكذا وكذا فذلك للتخويف والتهويل لا لحقيقة الكفر وهذا كلام باطل، وحاشا أن يلعب أمناء الله تعالى - أعني علماء الأحكام - بالحرام والحلال والكفر والإسلام بل لا يقولون إلا الحق الثابت عن سيد الأنام عليه الصلاة والسلام وما أدى إليه اجتهاد الإمام من نص القرآن أنزله الملك العلام أو شرعه سيد الرسل العظام أو قاله الصحب الكرام والذي حررته هو مختار مشايخي الشافين لداء النغام بوأهم الله تعالى بفضله دار السلام وكل من يأتي بعدهم من علماء الدهر والأيام ما بقي دين الإسلام .اهـ. وحرر العلامة نوح أفندي أن مراد الإمام بما نقل عنه ما ذكره في الفقه الأكبر من عدم
Regarding al-Siddiq in this ruling: perhaps they mean that denial of the caliphate is denial of their entitlement to the caliphate, which contradicts the consensus of the Companions, not denial of its existence for them. It is reasoned that he is not a disbeliever in his statement 'not like bodies' because it only involves applying the term 'body' to Him, which implies deficiency, so he raised it by saying 'not like bodies', so nothing remains but mere application, and that is a sin that becomes a cause for punishment due to the implication, unlike if he said it as comparison, for then he is a disbeliever. And it is said he becomes a disbeliever by mere application as well, and that is good, indeed it is more deserving of takfir. So the result: he is a disbeliever in two expressions: 'He is a body like bodies' and 'He is a body', and becomes an innovator in 'not like bodies'. Then he said: Know that the ruling of disbelief on those we mentioned from the people of desires... the third is 'body' about... along with what is established from Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i that they do not declare disbelief on the people of the qibla from among the innovators entirely, its interpretation is that the belief itself is disbelief, so the utterer is uttering what is disbelief, even if he is not declared a disbeliever, based on his statement being the utmost of his capacity as a mujtahid seeking truth. But their decisiveness that prayer behind him is invalid does not validate this combination, unless they mean by 'disallowed' the lack of permissibility that does not negate validity; otherwise it is problematic—and Allah knows best. Contrary to the absolute name of 'body' with comparison, for he is a disbeliever because he chose to utter what implies deficiency after knowing that. And if he negates comparison, nothing remains but carelessness and disrespect. So this is the problem. These branches are problematic with what is established from the mujtahids... al-Sa'd al-Taftazani in Sharh al-Aqa'id... and the answer in Fath al-Qadir is questionable... because his reasoning in al-Khulasa that whoever denies the vision etc. is a disbeliever refutes this interpretation. The better view is what he mentioned in the chapter of al-Bughat: that these branches transmitted in fatwas of takfir were not transmitted from the jurists (i.e., the mujtahids). Rather, what is transmitted from them is not declaring disbelief of those who are of our qibla, to the extent that they did not rule on the Khawarij who consider permissible the blood and wealth of Muslims and insulting the Companions, because it is based on interpretation and doubt, and no consideration is given to non-mujtahids. It is mentioned in al-Musayara that the apparent position of al-Shafi'i and Abu Hanifa is that not a single one of them is declared a disbeliever, even if it is reported from Abu Hanifa that he said to Jahm: 'Get out from me, O disbeliever,' interpreting it as referring to comparison, and this is the choice of al-Razi. And in its commentary by Kamal ibn Abi Sharif it is mentioned that not declaring them disbelievers is what is transmitted from the majority of theologians. That belief itself is disbelief, etc. al-Halabi said: On this, what is transmitted should be understood as excluding the extreme Rafidis and those like them, for such people do not exert their utmost in ijtihad. For the one who says 'Ali is God' or that Jibril made a mistake and such nonsense is an innovator by mere desire, which is worse than those who say 'We only worship them to bring us nearer to Allah'. So it is not conceivable from the two great imams that they would not rule them as the most severe of disbelievers. Rather, their words apply to those who have a doubt in what they hold, even if that which they hold in itself is disbelief, like the denier of the vision, punishment of the grave, etc., as known in kalam, and like the denier of the caliphate of the two shaykhs and the one who curses them, for it involves denial of definite consensus, except that they deny the authority of consensus by accusing the Companions, so they have a doubt in general, even if it is apparently invalid in light of evidence; due to that doubt which led... al-Khulasa and the jurists: for Shaykh Abu al-Hasan al-Ash'ari said in his book Maqalat al-Islamiyyin: The Muslims differed after their Prophet in things, some declaring others astray and some disassociating from others, until they became scattered sects, yet Islam encompasses them all. And Imam al-Shafi'i said: I accept the testimony of the people of desires except the Khattabiyya because they give false testimony for their supporters. And what the author mentioned that it is the apparent position of Abu Hanifa is affirmed by al-Hakim, author of al-Mukhtasar, in his book al-Muntaqa, and it is the relied-upon view. So the conclusion: the madhhab is not to declare disbelief of any of the opponents in matters that are not among the foundations known necessarily from the religion. This is indicated by the statement 'their testimony except the Khattabiyya', and they did not elaborate in the book of testimonies. This indicates that these branches transmitted from others with explicit takfir were not transmitted from Abu Hanifa, but rather are from the derivations of the shaykhs, like the words of takfir transmitted in fatwas. And Allah is the Grantor of success. In Jami' al-Jawami' and its commentary: We do not declare disbelief of any of the people of the qibla due to innovation, like deniers of Allah's attributes, His creating the actions of servants, and the permissibility of seeing Him on the Day of Resurrection; and among us are those who declared them disbelievers. As for those who exit by their innovation from the people of the qibla, like deniers of the creation of the world, resurrection, gathering of bodies, and knowledge of particulars, there is no dispute about their disbelief because they deny some of what is known necessarily that the Messenger brought. In al-Khulasa from al-Halwani: It is prohibited to pray behind one who engages in theology and debates the people of desires. Al-Mujtaba interpreted it as referring to one who intends by debate to make his opponent slip. As for one who intends to reach the truth and guide creation, he is one who is blessed to be followed, and tribulation is warded off through his guidance. As for prayer behind Shafi'is, the conclusion in al-Mujtaba is that if he observes the conditions and pillars according to us, it is valid on the most correct view, but disliked; otherwise it is not valid at all. Its explanation will come in the chapter of Witr. There is no specificity to Shafi'is; rather, prayer behind anyone who opposes the madhhab is the same. Their ijtihad reached that they did not declare them disbelievers even though their belief is disbelief, as a precaution, unlike those we mentioned from the extremists. So reflect. His statement: (Because his reasoning in al-Khulasa) the author of al-Nahr said: How can he refute it when it is possible to interpret 'disbeliever' as meaning 'one who says something that is disbelief'? He does not deny that the wording became contrary to its apparent meaning. His statement: (This indicates that these branches...). Al-Nahr said: This statement was refuted by al-Bazzazi in al-Fatawa at length; refer to it. I say: The text of his words in the chapter of apostasy: It is reported from some who have no predecessor that he used to say: 'What is mentioned in fatwas that so-and-so is a disbeliever is for intimidation and exaggeration, not for the reality of disbelief.' This is false speech. Far be it that the trustees of Allah—meaning the scholars of ahkam—would play with the haram and halal, disbelief and Islam. Rather, they only say the truth established from the Sayyid of mankind, and that which the ijtihad of the Imam reaches from the text of the Qur'an, or from the legislation of the master of messengers, or from the noble Companions. What I have verified is the choice of my shaykhs... And the distinguished scholar Nuh Afandi verified that the meaning of the Imam from what is reported from him is what he mentioned in al-Fiqh al-Akbar: not...

Commentary
This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq deals with the delicate issue of takfir (declaring someone a disbeliever) in the context of imamah (leading prayer). It primarily discusses three statements concerning Allah's attributes: (1) "Allah is a body like bodies" – this is explicit tashbih (anthropomorphism) and constitutes kufr. (2) "Allah is a body" without qualification – this is also kufr according to the relied-upon view, even if the speaker does not intend comparison, because it implies deficiency. (3) "Allah is not like bodies" – this is not kufr but is bid'ah (innovation), because the speaker uses the term 'body' without proper understanding, although he negates similarity. The text then addresses an apparent contradiction: how can these rulings (that specific statements are kufr) be reconciled with the well-known position of Abu Hanifa and al-Shafi'i that they do not declare takfir of anyone from the People of the Qibla? The resolution offered is that the belief itself is kufr, but the speaker is not declared a disbeliever because he may have a valid interpretation (ta'wil) or be a mujtahid who exhausted his capacity. However, the text notes inconsistency in the scholars' decisive rejection of prayer behind such a person while not calling him a kafir. Later, the author aligns with the majority Hanafi position: takfir is avoided unless the person denies something necessarily known from the religion, such as the resurrection of bodies or the creation of the world. Even the Khawarij, who shed Muslim blood, are not declared disbelievers due to their interpretation. The discussion extends to praying behind ahl al-ahwa (innovators) and behind Shafi'is. According to al-Mujtaba, prayer behind a Shafi'i is valid if he observes the conditions according to the Hanafi school, but it is makruh. The same applies to any follower of a different madhhab. The passage ends with a strong condemnation of those who dismiss fatwas of takfir as mere scare tactics, asserting that the scholars are truthful. Overall, this passage teaches that takfir is a serious matter with strict criteria, and the Hanafi school exercises caution, reserving it for clear denial of essentials.

Key Terms
تكفير (takfir): Declaring a Muslim to be a disbeliever due to a statement or belief.
أهل الأهواء (ahl al-ahwa'): People of heretical desires who hold innovated beliefs but still face the Qibla.
شبهة (shubha): A plausible doubt or misinterpretation that prevents declaring someone a disbeliever.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) Hanafi ruling on a person who says 'Allah is a body' without adding 'like bodies' or 'not like bodies'?
A) He is a disbeliever, but if he negates similarities he becomes an innovator.
B) He is an innovator, not a disbeliever.
C) He is a disbeliever without exception or qualification.
D) He is a believer with no sin because he spoke metaphorically.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school exercises great caution in declaring takfir; statements that imply anthropomorphism may constitute kufr in themselves, but the speaker is often excused due to interpretation or ignorance, and prayer behind such a person is valid but disliked.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Dislike of Imam Prolonging Prayer and Women's Congregation
Rulings with proof on imam's lengthening and women's congregation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the imam prolonging prayer and on women forming a congregation, identify the dalil, and explain why the dislike is classified as karahah tahrimiyyah.

Core Idea
The imam's duty is to not burden the congregation; prolonging beyond sunnah is prohibitively disliked.

This passage from Al-Bahr al-Raiq addresses two issues concerning congregational prayer: the imam's length and women's congregation. The rulings are based on a clear hadith and principles of Hanafi usul. Understanding these rulings helps an imam fulfill his role without causing hardship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Two Rulings
The text states that it is disliked (makruh) for the imam to prolong the prayer and for women to form a congregation. Note the Arabic: 'وكره تطويل الصلاة' and 'وكره جماعة النساء'.
The ruling for women applies to them praying separately as a congregation, not their attending the mosque behind men.
2
Locate the Dalil
The proof for imam's prolongation is the hadith: إذا أم أحدكم الناس فليخفف (When one of you leads the people, let him lighten it). This is a command (amr).
The hadith is ahad (single-chain), so its thubut is zanni, but its dalala is considered qati in Hanafi usul.
3
Apply Usul to Determine Hukm
In Hanafi usul, a command indicates obligation (wujub) unless diverted by another evidence. Therefore, violating this command is a sin, making the action makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The text also notes that causing harm to others strengthens this ruling.
4
Examine the Exception and Definition
An exception is made for eclipse prayer (salat al-kusuf), where lengthening is sunnah. The definition of prolongation is 'what exceeds the prescribed sunnah measure', not the mere act of reciting something.
The Prophet's own recitation in Fajr was sometimes long, but that was his sunnah; the disliked prolongation is beyond that baseline.
5
Note Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Regarding lengthening bowing to allow a latecomer, Abu Hanifa forbids it absolutely (as riya'), while al-Faqih or al-Layth allow it if the latecomer is unknown. The relied-upon position is Abu Hanifa's.
This ikhtilaf shows how different considerations (mercy vs. sincerity) can affect subsidiary rulings.

قوله وتطويل (الصلاة) أي وكره للإمام تطويلها للحديث «إذا أم أحدكم الناس فليخفف» واستثنى المحقق في فتح القدير صلاة الكسوف فإنه السنة فيها التطويل حتى تنجلي الشمس. وأراد بالتطويل ما زاد على القدر المسنون كما في السراج الوهاج لا كما قد يتوهمه بعض الأئمة فيقرأ يسيراً في الفجر كغيرها. وفي المضمرات شرح القدوري : أي لا يزيد على القراءة المستحبة ولا يثقل على القوم ولكن يخفف بعد أن يكون على التمام والاستحباب اهـ . وذكره في فتح القدير بحثاً وعلل له بأنه نهى عن التطويل وكانت قراءته هي المسنونة فلا بد من كون ما نهى عنه غير ما كان دأبه إلا لضرورة كما روي عنه صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قرأ بالمعوذتين في الفجر، فلما فرغ قيل له أو جزت قال : سمعت بكاء فخشيت أن تفتتن أمه. وفي منية المصلي: ويكره للإمام أن يعجلهم عن إكمال السنة، والظاهر أنها في تطويل الصلاة كراهة تحريم للأمر بالتخفيف وهو للوجوب إلا لصارف ولإدخال الضرر على الغير . وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان القوم يحصون أو لا رضوا بالتطويل أو لا لإطلاق الحديث. وأطلق في التطويل فشمل إطالة القراءة أو الركوع أو السجود أو الأدعية واختار الفقيه أو الليث أنه يطيل الركوع لإدراك الجائي إذا لم يعرفه فإن عرفه فلا، وأبو حنيفة منع منه مطلقاً لأنه شرك أي رياء . قوله (وجماعة النساء) أي وكره جماعة النساء لأنها لا تخلو عن ارتكاب محرم وهو قيام الإمام وسط الصف فيكره كالعراة. كذا في الهداية، وهو يدل على أنها كراهة تحريم لأن التقدم واجب على الإمام للمواظبة من النبي عليه، وترك الواجب موجب لكراهة التحريم المقتضية للإثم، ويدل على كراهة التحريم في جماعة العراة بالأولى. واستثنى الشارحون جماعتهن في

His saying: 'and prolonging (the prayer)' meaning it is disliked for the imam to prolong it due to the hadith 'When one of you leads the people, let him lighten it.' And the muhaqqiq in Fath al-Qadir excepted the eclipse prayer, for the sunnah is to prolong it until the sun clears. What is meant by prolongation is what exceeds the prescribed measure, as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, not as some imams might imagine, so they recite a little in Fajr like other prayers. In al-Mudmarat Sharh al-Quduri: It means he should not exceed the recommended recitation and should not burden the people, but should lighten while still fulfilling completeness and recommendation. It is mentioned in Fath al-Qadir as a discussion, and he reasoned that he prohibited prolongation while his recitation was the sunnah, so what is prohibited must be other than his usual practice, except for necessity, as related that he recited al-Mu'awwidhatayn in Fajr, and when finished, it was said to him: 'Did you shorten?' He said: 'I heard a child crying, and I feared his mother would be seduced.' In Munyat al-Musalli: It is disliked for the imam to hurry them away from completing the sunnah. Apparently, prolonging the prayer is a prohibited dislike (karahah tahrim) because the command to lighten indicates obligation unless diverted, and due to causing harm to others. It is absolute, applying whether the congregation counts or not, whether they consent to prolongation or not, due to the absolute nature of the hadith. And prolongation is absolute, including lengthening recitation, bowing, prostration, or supplications. Al-Faqih or al-Layth chose that he lengthens the bowing to allow a latecomer to join if he does not know him; if he knows him, then no. Abu Hanifa forbade it absolutely because it is shirk i.e., riya'. His saying: 'and the congregation of women' meaning it is disliked for women to form a congregation because it does not avoid committing a prohibited act, i.e., the imam standing in the middle of the row, so it is disliked like the congregation of naked people. This is stated in al-Hidayah, and it indicates that it is a prohibited dislike because stepping forward is obligatory for the imam due to the Prophet's constant practice, and omitting an obligatory act leads to prohibited dislike that incurs sin, and implies prohibited dislike for the congregation of naked people by greater reason. The commentators excepted their congregation in ... [continues with commentary]
Source pages p. 614

Commentary
This passage presents two rulings: the dislike of the imam prolonging the prayer, and the dislike of women forming a congregation. For the first ruling, the proof is the hadith commanding the imam to lighten the prayer. The text explains that this refers to exceeding the sunnah length, not merely reading short surahs. Exception is made for the eclipse prayer, where lengthening is sunnah. The hadith is interpreted as a command of obligation, so violation is karahah tahrimiyyah (prohibited dislike). The imam's prolongation applies to all parts: recitation, bowing, prostration, and supplications. A difference of opinion exists regarding lengthening bowing to allow a latecomer: Abu Hanifa forbids it absolutely as it borders on riya'. For the second ruling, women's congregation is disliked because it leads to the imam standing in the middle of the row (which is prohibited for men, as imam should be ahead), and this is compared to the congregation of naked people (which is also disliked). The text clarifies that this is karahah tahrim (prohibited dislike) because it involves omitting the obligatory act of the imam standing ahead. The final part includes a discussion on the exception for women's congregation in certain cases and criticisms of previous statements regarding the nature of the dislike.

Key Terms
كراهة تحريم (karahah tahrimiyyah): A dislike that is close to prohibition, requiring avoidance and incurring sin if done.
تطويل (taltwil): Prolonging the prayer beyond the sunnah length, which is disliked for the imam.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi madhhab, what is the ruling on women forming their own congregation for prayer?
A) It is valid and recommended.
B) It is valid but disliked (makruh tahrimi).
C) It is invalid.
D) It is forbidden.

Key Takeaway
Both the imam's prolongation and women's congregation are prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) in the Hanafi school, based on the hadith command to lighten and the obligation of the imam to stand ahead.
