Dislike of Imam Prolonging Prayer
Ruling on imam prolonging prayer with proof

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on an imam prolonging prayer beyond the sunnah amount, apply the hadith proof, and identify the intra-Hanafi difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu al-Layth.

Core Idea
Prolonging prayer beyond the sunnah is prohibitively disliked (makruh tahrimi) because the command for brevity indicates obligation.

The imam's primary duty is to lead the congregation in worship without causing hardship. This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq explains that prolonging prayer beyond the established sunnah amount is disliked, based on the Prophet's command to be brief. We will unpack the evidence, define what counts as prolongation, and examine a nuanced difference among Hanafi scholars.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is the imam prolonging the prayer (tatwil al-imam al-salah). The ruling is that it is disliked (makruh). Determine the degree of karahah from the text: it is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked).
The text explicitly says 'كراهة تحريم' (karahah tahrimiyyah).
2
Locate the primary dalil
The proof is the hadith: 'When one of you leads the people in prayer, let him be brief' (إذا أم أحدكم الناس فليخفف). Identify its type: it is a hadith ahad, but the command (amr) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
The hadith is cited in the source text.
3
Analyze the wajh al-dalalah (aspect of evidence)
The imperative verb 'ليخفف' is understood as obligatory per the Hanafi rule 'al-amr yufidu al-wujub'. Violating an obligation without valid reason is prohibited, hence makruh tahrimi.
No overriding factor is present except for exceptions like eclipse prayer.
4
Define prolongation correctly
Prolongation means exceeding the masnun (prescribed sunnah) amount, not merely lengthening a bit. It includes recitation, bowing, prostration, and supplications. This dispels the misconception that 'brief' means minimal recitation even in Fajr.
The source cites al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and al-Mudmarat.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Abu Hanifa forbade prolongation absolutely. Abu al-Layth allowed prolonging bowing if a latecomer might catch the rak'ah, provided the imam does not know the latecomer (to avoid ostentation). The mufta bihi is Abu Hanifa's absolute prohibition.
This is a minor difference within the school.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله وتطويل (الصلاة) أي وكره للإمام تطويلها للحديث إذا أم أحدكم الناس فليخفف» واستثنى المحقق في فتح القدير صلاة الكسوف فإنه السنة فيها التطويل حتى تنجلي الشمس. وأراد بالتطويل ما زاد على القدر المسنون كما في السراج الوهاج لا كما قد يتوهمه بعض الأئمة فيقرأ يسيراً في الفجر كغيرها. وفي المضمرات شرح القدوري : أي لا يزيد على القراءة المستحبة ولا يثقل على القوم ولكن يخفف بعد أن يكون على التمام والاستحباب اهـ . وذكره في فتح القدير بحثاً وعلل له بأنه نهى عن التطويل وكانت قراءته هي المسنونة فلا بد من كون ما نهى عنه غير ما كان دأبه إلا لضرورة كما روي عنه صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه قرأ بالمعوذتين في الفجر، فلما فرغ قيل له أو جزت قال : سمعت بكاء فخشيت أن تفتتن أمه. وفي منية المصلي: ويكره للإمام أن يعجلهم عن إكمال السنة، والظاهر أنها في تطويل الصلاة كراهة تحريم للأمر بالتخفيف وهو للوجوب إلا لصارف ولإدخال الضرر على الغير . وأطلقه فشمل ما إذا كان القوم يحصون أو لا رضوا بالتطويل أو لا لإطلاق الحديث. وأطلق في التطويل فشمل إطالة القراءة أو الركوع أو السجود أو الأدعية واختار الفقيه أو الليث أنه يطيل الركوع لإدراك الجائي إذا لم يعرفه فإن عرفه فلا، وأبو حنيفة منع منه مطلقاً لأنه شرك أي رياء
His statement: 'and prolonging (the prayer)' means: it is disliked for the imam to prolong the prayer due to the hadith: 'When one of you leads the people in prayer, let him be brief.' The verifier in Fath al-Qadir excepted the eclipse prayer, for the sunnah in it is prolongation until the sun clears. He intended by prolongation what exceeds the prescribed amount as in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj, not as some imams mistakenly imagine, reciting a small amount in Fajr like other prayers. In al-Mudmarat Sharh al-Quduri: 'He should not exceed the recommended recitation and not burden the congregation, but he should be brief while maintaining completeness and desirability.' And he mentioned in Fath al-Qadir a discussion and reasoned by it saying: He forbade prolongation, and his recitation was the sunnah, so what is forbidden must be something other than his usual practice unless for necessity, as narrated that he recited al-Mu'awwidhatayn in Fajr, and when he finished it was said to him 'Did you cut it short?' He said: 'I heard a child crying and feared his mother would be tempted.' In Munyat al-Musalli: It is disliked for the imam to make them haste away from completing the sunnah. It appears that regarding prolonging prayer, it is a prohibition of tahrim due to the command for brevity, and the command indicates obligation unless there is an impediment, and due to causing harm to others. It is general, including whether the congregation counts or not, whether they are pleased with prolongation or not, due to the generality of the hadith. It is general in prolongation, including prolonging recitation, bowing, prostration, or supplications. Al-Faqih Abu al-Layth chose that he prolongs bowing to allow the latecomer to catch up if he does not know him; if he knows him, then no. Abu Hanifa forbade it absolutely because it is shirk, i.e., ostentation.
Source pages p. 614

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the dislike of the imam prolonging the prayer. The author states that it is disliked for the imam to prolong the prayer based on the hadith 'When one of you leads the people in prayer, let him be brief.' The exception is the eclipse prayer where prolongation is sunnah. Prolongation is defined as exceeding the prescribed (masnun) amount, not as a small amount as some imams mistakenly think. The karahah is considered tahrimi (prohibitive dislike) because the command for brevity indicates obligation, and causing harm to others is prohibited. This applies regardless of the congregation's consent or ability to count. The prolongation includes all parts of prayer. Abu Hanifa forbade it absolutely because it may involve ostentation (riya).

Key Terms
تطويل (tatwil): Prolonging the prayer beyond the prescribed sunnah amount in recitation, bowing, prostration, or supplications

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on an imam prolonging the prayer beyond the sunnah amount?
A) It is mustahabb if the congregation agrees
B) It is makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked)
C) It is makruh tahrimi (prohibitively disliked)
D) It is haram in all cases

Key Takeaway
An imam must not prolong prayer beyond the sunnah amount; doing so is prohibitively disliked regardless of congregation's consent.

Women Leading Congregational Prayer: Ruling and Requirements
Ruling on women leading prayer and the imam's position

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women's congregational prayer, explain the wajib position of the female imam, and identify the exception for funeral prayer.

Core Idea
Women's congregation is valid but makruh tahrimi; the female imam must stand in the middle, not in front.

This passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq addresses a common question: can women lead other women in prayer? The Hanafi ruling balances the validity of the act with the obligation of the imam's position. We will unpack the ruling, its proof, and its exceptions.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
Determine what the act is (women praying in congregation) and the school's legal classification (makruh tahrimi). Note that the ruling is based on the imam's required position.
The karahah is tahrimiyyah because it involves abandoning a wajib.
2
Locate the proof and its reasoning
Find the evidence cited: the Prophet's constant practice of standing in front (making it wajib) and the analogy with naked congregants. Understand how this leads to karahah tahrimi.
The act of standing in the middle is inherently prohibited because it violates the wajib of imam's position.
3
Examine the exception and its rationale
Note the exception for funeral prayer: the dislike is overridden to perform a fard. This is a case of choosing the lesser harm.
The principle: when a disliked act is necessary to fulfill a fard, it becomes permissible.
4
Analyze the intra-madhhab dispute on istikhlaf
Consider the case where a male imam appoints a woman as substitute for a mixed congregation. Compare the views of the three (invalid) and Zufr (valid). Understand the reasoning involving incompleteness of tahrīmah.
The majority view is mufta bihi.
5
Apply the required position for the female imam
The female imam must stand in the middle (wajib); if she stands in front she sins but prayer is valid. The middle is advised as less disliked.
This is derived from A'isha's practice and the need to minimize exposure.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله (وجماعة النساء) أي وكره جماعة النساء لأنها لا تخلو عن ارتكاب محرم وهو قيام الإمام وسط الصف فيكره كالعراة. كذا في الهداية، وهو يدل على أنها كراهة تحريم لأن التقدم واجب على الإمام للمواظبة من النبي عليه، وترك الواجب موجب لكراهة التحريم المقتضية للإثم، ويدل على كراهة التحريم في جماعة العراة بالأولى. واستثنى الشارحون جماعتهن في صلاة الجنازة فإنها لا تكره لأنها فريضة وترك التقدم مكروه فدار الأمر بين فعل المكروه لفعل الفرض أو ترك الفرض لتركه، فوجب الأول بخلاف جماعتهن في غيرها. ولو صلين فرادى فقد تسبق إحداهن فتكون صلاة الباقيات نفلاً، والتنفل بها مكروه فيكون فراغ تلك موجباً لفساد الفرضية لصلاة الباقيات كتقييد الخامس بالسجدة لمن ترك القعدة. وأفاد أن إمامة المرأة للنساء صحيحة، واستثنى في السراج الوهاج مسألة وهي ما لو استخلف الإمام امرأة وخلفه رجال ونساء فسدت صلاة الرجال والنساء والإمام والمقدمة في قول أصحابنا الثلاثة خلافاً لزفر، أما فساد صلاة الرجال فظاهر، وأما فساد صلاة النساء فلأنهم دخلوا في تحريمة كاملة فإذا انتقلوا إلى تحريمة ناقصة لم يجز كأنهم خرجوا من فرض إلى فرض آخر . قوله (فإن فعلن تقف الإمام وسطهن كالعراة لأن عائشة رضي الله عنها فعلت كذلك وحمل فعلها الجماعة على ابتداء الاسلام ولأن في التقدم زيادة الكشف. وأفاد بالتعبير بقوله «تقف» أنه واجب فلو تقدمت أثمت كما صرح به في فتح القدير والصلاة صحيحة، فإذا توسطت لا تزول الكراهة وإنما أرشدوا إلى التوسط لأنه أقل كراهية من التقدم. كذا في السراج الوهاج. ولو تأخرت لم يصح الاقتداء بها عندنا لعدم شرطه وهو عدم التأخر عن المأموم. وذكر في المغرب الإمام من يؤتم به أي يقتدى به ذكراً كان أو أنثى . وفي الواو مع السين الوسط بالتحريك اسم لعين ما بين طرفي الشيء كمركز الدائرة وبالسكون اسم مبهم لداخل الدائرة مثلاً ولذلك كان ظرفاً، فالأول يجعل مبتدأ أو فاعلاً ومفعولاً به وداخلاً عليه حرف الجر ولا يصح شيء من . هذا في الثاني، تقول وسطه خير من طرفه واتسع وسطه، وضربت وسطه، وجلست في وسط الدار، وجلست وسطها بالسكون لا غير ويوصف بالأول مستوياً فيه المذكر المؤنث والاثنان والجمع . قال الله تعالى جعلناكم أمة وسطاً) [البقرة: ١٤٣] ولله علي أن أهدي شاتين وسطاً إلى بيت الله أو أعتق عبدين وسطاً. وقد بنى منه أفعل التفضيل فقيل للذكر الأوسط وللمؤنث الوسطى قال تعالى من أوسط ما تطعمون أهليكم [المائدة: ۸۹] يعني المتوسط بين الإسراف والتقتير. وقد أكثروا في ذلك وهو في محل الرفع على البدل من اطعام أو كسوتهم معطوف عليه والصلاة الوسطى العصر وهو المشهور .اهـ. وضبطه هنا في السراج الوهاج بسكون السين لا غير. وفي الصحاح : كل موضع صلح فيه بين فهو وسط بالتسكين كجلست وسط القوم ، وإن لم يصلح فيه فهو بالتحريك كجلست وسط الدار بما سكن وليس بالوجه اهـ. وفي ضياء الحلوم الوسط بالسكون ظرف مكان، وبفتح السين اسم تقول وَسْطَ هو على ظاهره وجب بمعنى ثبت ولزم أي لما دار الأمر بين المحذورين ثبت وتعين الأول وهو جماعتهن. هذا ولا يخفى ما في تسمية جماعتهن بالفرض من البعد وكذا بالواجب لما سيصرح به المؤلف في الجنائز من أن الجماعة فيها غير واجبة. قوله : (وفي معراج الدراية والتشبيه الخ) فيه
His statement: 'And the congregation of women' means: it is disliked for women to pray in congregation because it inevitably involves a prohibited act, namely the imam standing in the middle of the row, so it is disliked like the congregation of naked people. Thus in al-Hidayah, and it indicates that it is karahah tahrimiyyah because the imam is required to stand in front due to the Prophet's constant practice; abandoning an obligation necessitates karahah tahrimiyyah which entails sin, and it indicates karahah tahrimiyyah in the congregation of naked people a fortiori. The commentators excepted their congregation in the funeral prayer: it is not disliked because it is a fard (obligation) and abandoning the forward position is disliked, so the matter is between committing a disliked act to perform an obligation or leaving the obligation, so the first is necessary, unlike their congregation in other prayers. If they pray individually, one of them may precede, making the prayer of the rest supererogatory, and performing supererogatory in that way is disliked, so that one's finishing causes the invalidation of the obligatory nature of the others' prayer, like binding the fifth with prostration for one who omitted the sitting. It indicates that a woman leading women is valid. Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj excepted a case: if the imam appoints a woman as substitute and behind her are men and women, then the prayer of the men, women, the imam, and the appointed woman is invalid according to our three masters, contrary to Zufr. The invalidity of the men's prayer is apparent; the invalidity of the women's prayer is because they entered with a complete tahrīmah and then moved to an incomplete one, which is impermissible, as if they left one fard for another. His statement: 'If they do so, the imam stands in the middle of them like the naked' because A'isha, may Allah be pleased with her, did so, and her action is interpreted as being at the beginning of Islam, and because standing in front increases exposure. The expression 'stands' indicates it is wajib; if she stands in front she sins, as stated in Fath al-Qadir, but the prayer is valid. If she stands in the middle, the dislike does not disappear; they only advised the middle because it is less disliked than standing in front. Thus in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj. If she stands behind, her leadership is not valid according to us because the condition (of not being behind the followers) is not met. In al-Mughrib: 'The imam is one who is followed (yu'tammu bihi), male or female.' ... [Linguistic section on 'wasat'...] It is clear that the word is as stated. He said: (In Mi'raj al-Dirayah and the similitude...)
Source pages p. 614

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the congregation of women. The author explains that it is disliked (makruh tahrimi) for women to pray in congregation because it involves a prohibited act: the imam (who is a woman) must stand in the middle of the row, whereas the imam is obligated to stand in front based on the Prophet's practice. This karahah is like that of naked people praying together. An exception is made for the funeral prayer, which is a fard; here the dislike is overlooked to fulfill the obligation. The imamah of a woman for women is valid, except in the case where a male imam appoints a woman as substitute for a mixed congregation, which invalidates everyone's prayer according to Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad (except Zufr). The proper position for the female imam is to stand in the middle of the row, following A'isha's practice; if she stands in front she sins, but the prayer remains valid. The passage then includes a detailed linguistic discussion of the word 'wasat' (middle) distinguishing its two pronunciations and uses, citing Quranic verses and classical lexicons. The conclusion is that the karahah remains even in the middle position, but it is less severe.

Key Terms
وسطة (wasatah): The female imam standing in the middle of the row of women followers
تكره (tukrah): It is disliked (makruh); the verb form indicates karahah.
استخلاف (istikhlāf): Appointing a substitute imam during prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on a woman leading other women in congregational prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) It is invalid and sinful
B) It is valid but makruh tahrimi, and she must stand in the middle of the row
C) It is valid and recommended
D) It is valid only if no men are present

Key Takeaway
Women's congregational prayer is valid but carries a sinful dislike (makruh tahrimi) due to the imam's wajib position; the female imam must stand in the middle of the row.

Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Women Leading Women in Prayer: Validity and the Exception with Men Present
Intra-Hanafi dispute on women's imamate with an exception for men's presence

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on women leading women in prayer, identify the exception when a woman is appointed as imam with men behind, and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between the three companions and Zufar.

Core Idea
Women leading women is valid, but if a woman is appointed imam with men behind, the prayer is invalid for all — a tahrimah-based exception.

In this passage from al-Bahr al-Ra'iq, the author affirms that a woman leading other women in prayer is generally valid. However, he cites an exception from al-Siraj al-Wahhaj: if a woman is appointed as imam with men in the congregation, the prayer becomes invalid for everyone. This ruling is based on the concept of tahrimah (consecration) and involves a disagreement within the Hanafi school, with Zufar dissenting.

Guided Path
1
State the general Hanafi position on women leading women
Recognize that the passage begins by affirming that a woman's imamate for women is valid (sahih). This is the general principle.
Compare with the funeral prayer mentioned earlier in the passage to understand the context.
2
Identify the exception and its conditions
Find the key phrase 'if the imam appoints a woman as his successor and behind him are men and women'. This is the specific scenario that triggers invalidity.
The exception requires: (1) a woman appointed by the original imam, (2) both men and women present behind her.
3
Explain the reasoning based on tahrimah
The passage states that the women entered with a complete tahrimah (from the original imam) and then transferred to an incomplete one (the woman's imamate), which is impermissible. This is the core reason for invalidity.
The men's invalidity is apparent — a woman cannot lead men in prayer.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Recognize that Zufar disagrees with the three companions (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad). His view is that the prayer remains valid in this exception.
The passage does not provide Zufar's dalil, but we note that he holds an opposing position.
5
Determine the mufta bihi position
Al-Siraj al-Wahhaj and the author prefer the majority view of the three companions. This is the relied-upon position for fatwa.
The practical consequence: if Zufar's view were followed, no repetition would be needed; otherwise, the prayer must be repeated.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
صلاة الجنازة فإنها لا تكره لأنها فريضة وترك التقدم مكروه فدار الأمر بين فعل المكروه لفعل الفرض أو ترك الفرض لتركه، فوجب الأول بخلاف جماعتهن في غيرها. ولو صلين فرادى فقد تسبق إحداهن فتكون صلاة الباقيات نفلاً، والتنفل بها مكروه فيكون فراغ تلك موجباً لفساد الفرضية لصلاة الباقيات كتقييد الخامس بالسجدة لمن ترك القعدة. وأفاد أن إمامة المرأة للنساء صحيحة، واستثنى في السراج الوهاج مسألة وهي ما لو استخلف الإمام امرأة وخلفه رجال ونساء فسدت صلاة الرجال والنساء والإمام والمقدمة في قول أصحابنا الثلاثة خلافاً لزفر، أما فساد صلاة الرجال فظاهر، وأما فساد صلاة النساء فلأنهم دخلوا في تحريمة كاملة فإذا انتقلوا إلى تحريمة ناقصة لم يجز كأنهم خرجوا من فرض إلى فرض آخر.
The funeral prayer is not disliked because it is an obligation, and refraining from going forward is disliked. So the matter revolves between doing the disliked for the sake of doing the obligatory or abandoning the obligatory for the sake of abandoning it, so the first is obligatory, unlike their congregation in other prayers. And if they pray individually, one of them may precede, making the prayer of the remaining ones supererogatory, and performing supererogatory prayer is disliked, so the completion of that prayer invalidates the obligatory status of the prayer of the remaining ones, like binding the fifth with the prostration for one who leaves the sitting. And it indicates that a woman's imamate for women is valid, and in al-Siraj al-Wahhaj an exception is made: if the imam appoints a woman as his successor and behind him are men and women, the prayers of the men, women, the imam, and the appointed woman are invalid according to the statement of our three companions, contrary to Zufar. As for the invalidity of the men's prayer, it is apparent. As for the invalidity of the women's prayer, it is because they entered into a complete consecration (tahrimah) and then transferred to an incomplete one, which is not permissible, as if they went from one obligation to another.
Source pages p. 615

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of women leading women in prayer. The author begins by comparing women's congregation in prayer to the funeral prayer. The general ruling is that a woman leading other women in prayer is valid (sahih) and not inherently invalid. However, al-Siraj al-Wahhaj notes an exception: if an imam appoints a woman as his successor (khalifah) while there are men and women behind him, the prayer becomes invalid for all—men, women, the original imam, and the appointed woman. This is the position of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad (the 'three companions'), but Zufar disagrees. The reasoning for the invalidity of the women's prayer is that they initially entered into a complete tahrimah (consecration for prayer) but then transferred to an incomplete one (since a woman's imamate is incomplete for men), which is impermissible. This is akin to abandoning an obligation for another.

Key Terms
تحريمة (tahrimah): The initial 'Allahu Akbar' that consecrates the prayer and makes forbidden (haram) actions that were previously permissible.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling when a woman is appointed imam and men are behind her?
A) The prayer is valid for all.
B) The prayer is invalid for the men only.
C) The prayer is invalid for all according to the three companions.
D) The prayer is invalid for the women only.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school generally permits women leading women in prayer, but invalidates the prayer when a woman is appointed as imam with men behind due to the incomplete nature of her tahrimah for men.
